the White Ladies of Worcester 

 CHAPTER I 

 the SUBTERRANEAN WAY 

 the slanting ray of afternoon sunshine , pour through stone arch , lie in broad , golden band , upon the flag of the Convent cloister . 

 the old lay - sister , Mary Antony , step from the cool shade of the cell passage and , blink at the sunshine , shuffle slowly to her appoint post at the top of the crypt step , up which would shortly pass the silent procession of nun return from vesper . 

 Daily they go , and daily they return , by the underground way , a 
 passage over a mile in length , lead from the Nunnery of the White 
 Ladies at Whytstone in Claines , to the Church of St. Mary and St. 
 Peter , the noble Cathedral within the wall of the city of Worcester . 
 enter this passage from the crypt in their own cloister , they walk in darkness below the sunny meadow , pass beneath the Fore - gate , move in silent procession under the busy street , until they reach the crypt of the Cathedral . 

 from the crypt , a wind stairway in the wall lead up to a chamber above the choir , whence , unseeing and unseen , the White Ladies of Worcester daily hear the holy monk below chant vesper . 

 to Sister Mary Antony fall the task of count the five - and - twenty veiled figure , as they pass down the step and disappear beneath the ground , and of again count they as they reappear , and move in stately silence along the cloister , each enter her own cell , to spend , in prayer and adoration , the hour until the Refectory bell should call they to the evening meal . 

 this counting of the White Ladies date from the day , now more than half a century ago , when Sister Agatha , weaken by prolonged fasting , and chance to walk last in the procession , faint and , fall silently , remain behind , unnoticed , in the solitude and darkness . 

 it be the habit of this saintly lady to abide in her own cell after vesper , dispense with the evening meal ; thus her absence be not discover until the following morning when Mary Antony , find the cell empty , hasten to report that Sister Agatha have long , like Enoch , walk with God , have , even , as Enoch , be translate ! 

 the nun who flock to the cell , incline to Mary Antony 's view of the strange happening , kneel upon the floor before the empty couch , and worship . 

 the Prioress of that time , however , be of a practical turn of mind , order the immediate lighting of the lantern , and herself descend to search the underground way . 

 she do not need to go far . 

 the saintly spirit of Sister Agatha have indeed be translate . 

 they find her frail body lie prone against the door , the hand break and tear by much wild beating upon its studded panel . 

 she have run to and fro in the dank darkness , beat first upon the door beneath the Convent cloister , then upon the door , a mile away , lead into the Cathedral crypt . 

 but the nun be shut into their cell , beyond the cloister ; the good people of Worcester city sleep peacefully , not dream of the despairing figure run to and fro beneath they tottering , stumble , fall , arise to fall again , yet hurry blindly onwards ; and the Cathedral Sacristan , when question , confess that , hear cry and rapping come from the crypt at a late hour , he speedily lock the outer gate , say an " Ave , " and go home to supper ; well know that , at such a time , none save spirit of evil would be wander below , in so great torment . 

 thus , through much tribulation , poor Sister Agatha enter into rest ; be hold in deep reverence ever after . 

 More than fifty year have go by . the Prioress of that day , and most of those who walk in that procession , have long lain beside Sister Agatha in the Convent burying - ground . but Mary Antony , now old of the lay - sister , never fail to make careful count , as each veil figure pass , nor to impart the mournful reason for this necessity to all new - comer . so that the nun whose turn it be to walk last in the procession , pray that she might not hear behind she the run foot of Sister Agatha ; while none go alone into the cloister after dark , lest they should hear the poor thin hand of Sister Agatha beat upon the panel of the door . 

 thus do the anguish of a torture brain leave its imperishable impress upon the surrounding in which the mind once suffer , though the freed spirit may have long forget , in the peace of Paradise , that slight affliction , which be but for a moment , through which it pass to the eternal weight of glory . 

 of late , the old lay - sister , Mary Antony , have grow fearful lest she should make mistake in this solemn office of the counting . therefore , in the secret of her own heart , she devise a plan , which she carry out under cover of her scapulary . twenty - five dry pea she hold ready in her wallet ; then , as each veil figure , have mount the step lead from the crypt doorway , move slowly past she , she drop a pea with her right hand into her left . when all the holy Ladies have pass , if all have return , five - and - twenty pea lie in her left hand , none remain in the wallet . 

 this secret dropping of pea become a kind of game to Mary Antony . she keep the pea in a small linen bag , and often take they out and play with they when alone in her cell , place they all in a row , and settle , to her own satisfaction , which pea should represent the various holy Ladies . 

 a large white pea , of fine aspect than the rest , stand for the noble Prioress herself ; a somewhat shrivelled pea , hard , brown , and wizene , do duty as Mother Sub - Prioress , an elderly nun , not love by Mary Antony because of her sharp tongue and strict fault - find way ; while a pale and speckled pea become Sister Mary Rebecca , hold in high scorn by the old lay - sister , as a traitress , sneak , and liar , for if ever tale of wrong or shame be whisper in the Convent , it could be trace for place of origin to the slanderous tongue and crooked mind of Sister Mary Rebecca . 

 when all the pea in line upon the floor of her cell be name , old Mary Antony mark out a distant flagstone , on which the sunlight fall , as heaven ; another , partially in shadow , purgatory ; a third , in a far corner of exceed darkness , hell . she then proceed , with well - direct fillip of thumb and middle finger , to send the holy Ladies there where , in her judgment , they belong . 

 if the game go well , the noble Prioress land safely in heaven , without even the most transitory visit to purgatory ; Mother Sub - Prioress , roll into purgatory , remain there ; while the pale and speckled pea go straight to hell ! 

 when these be safely land , Mary Antony rub her hand and , chuckle gleefully , finish the game at gay hap - hazard , it be of less importance where the rest of the holy Ladies chance to go . 

 CHAPTER II 

 SISTER MARY ANTONY discourse 

 as Mary Antony shuffle slowly from the shadow into the sunshine , a gay little flutter of wing precede she , and a robin perch upon the parapet behind the stone seat upon which it be the lay - sister 's custom to await the sound of the turning of the key in the lock of the heavy door beneath the cloister . 

 " thou good - for - nothing imp ! " exclaim Mary Antony , her old face crinkle with delight . " thou little vain man , in thy red jerkin ! beshrew thine impudence , intrude into a place where woman alone do dwell , and no male thing may enter . I would have thee take warning by the fate of the baker 's boy , who dare to climb into a tree , so that he might peep over the wall and spy upon the holy Ladies in their garden . boast afterward of that which he have do , and make merry over that which he pretend to have see , our great Lord Bishop hear of it , and send and take that baker 's boy , and though he cry for mercy , swear the whole tale be an empty boast , they put out his bold eye with heated tong , and hang he from the very branch he have climb . they would do the like to thee , thou little vain man , if Mary Antony report on thy way . wouldst like to hang , in thy red doublet ? " 

 the robin have hear this warn tale many time already , tell by old 
 Mary Antony with infinite variety . 
 sometimes the tongue of the baker 's boy be cut out at the root ; sometimes he lose his ear , or again , he be tie to a cart - tail , and flog through the tything . often he become a pieman , and once he be a turnspit in the household of the Lord Bishop himself . but , whatever the preliminary , and whether baker , pieman , or turnspit , his final catastrophe be always the same : he be hang from a bough of the very tree into which , impious and greatly daring , he have climb . 

 this be an ancient tale . all who might vouch for it , save the old lay - sister , have pass away ; and , of late , Mary Antony have be strictly forbid by the Reverend Mother , to tell it to new - comer , or to speak of it to any of the nun . 

 so , daily , she tell it to the robin ; and he , be neither baker 's lad , pieman , nor turnspit , and have a conscience void of offence , would listen , wholly unafraid ; then , hop near to Mary Antony , would look up at she , eager inquiry in his bright eye . 

 on this particular afternoon he fly up into the very tree climb by the prying and ill - fat baker 's lad , settle on a bough which branch out over the Convent wall , and pour forth a gay trill of song . 

 " ha , thou little vain man , in thy brown and red suit ! " chuckle Mary Antony , lean she gnarl hand on the stone parapet , as she stand frame in one of the cloister arch overlook the garden . " be that thy little ' grace before meat ' ? but , I pray thee , Sir Robin , who say there be cheese in my wallet ? Nay , be there like to be cheese in a wallet already contain five - and - twenty holy Ladies on their way back from vesper ? out upon thee for a most irreverent little glutton ! I fear I thou hast not only a high look , thou hast also a proud stomach ; just the reverse of the great french Cardinal who come , with much pomp , to visit we at Easter time . he have a proud look and a come down again , thou little naughty man , and I will tell thee what the Lord Cardinal have under his crimson sash . ' tis not a thing to shout to the tree - top . I might have to recite ten Paternosters , if I let thee tempt I so to do . for whisper it in thine ear , I should but say one ; for have remark it , none at all . fact be fact ; and , even in the case of so weighty a fact , the responsibility rest not upon the beholder . " 

 Mary Antony lean over the parapet , look upward . the afternoon sunlight fall full upon the russet parchment of her kind old face , shew the web of wrinkle spin by ninety year of the gently turn wheel of time . 

 but the robin , perch upon the bough , trill and sang , unmoved . he be weary of tale of baker and pieman . he be not at all curious as to what have be beneath the french Cardinal 's crimson sash . he want the tasty morsel which he know lie conceal in Sister Mary Antony 's leathern wallet . so he stay on the bough and sing . 

 the old face , peer up from between the pillar , soften into tenderness at the robin 's song . 

 " I can not let thy little grace return unto thee void , " she say , and fumble at the fastening of her wallet . 

 a flick of wing , a flash of red . the robin have drop from the bough , and perch beside she . 

 she dole out crumb , and fragment of cheese , push they toward he along the parapet ; leave her finger near , to see how close he would adventure to her hand . 

 she watch he peck a morsel of cheese into five tiny piece , then fly , with full beak , on eager wing , to the hidden nest , from which five gap mouth shriek a shrill and hungry welcome . then , back again swift as an arrow from the archer 's bow noting , with bright eye , and head turn sidewise , that the hand rest on the coping have move nearer ; yet brave to take all risk for the sake of those yellow beak , which would gape wide , in expectation , at sound of the beat of his wing . 

 " feed thyself , thou little worldling ! " chuckle old Antony , and cover the remain bit of cheese with her hand . " who art thou to come here presume to teach thy better lesson of self - sacrifice ? first feed thyself ; then give to the hungry , the fragment that remain . have I five squeal child here which Heaven forbid I should eat mine own mess , and count myself charitable if I let they lick the dish . the holy Ladies give to the poor at the Convent gate , that for which they have no further use . do thy jaunty fatherhood presume to shame our saintly celibacy ? Mother Sub - Prioress do chide I sharply because , to a poor soul with many hungry mouth to feed , I give a good piece of venison , and not the piece which be taint . truth to tell , I have already make away with the tainted piece ; but Mother Sub - Prioress be pleased to think it be in the pot , seethe for the holy Ladies ' evening meal ; and wherefore should Mother Sub - Prioress not think as she please ? 

 " ' woman ! ' she cry ; ' woman ! ' and when Mother Sub - Prioress say 
 ' woman ! ' the woman she address feel her estate would be high have 
 God Almighty be pleased to have let she be the Man , or even the 
 Serpent , so much contempt do Mother Sub - Prioress infuse into the 
 name ' woman ! ' say Mother Sub - Prioress , ' wouldst thou make all the 
 Ladies of the Convent ill ? ' 
 " ' nay , ' say I , ' that would I not . yet , if any need must be ill , ' twere easy to tend the holy Ladies in their cell , than the Poor , in humble home , outside the Convent wall , toss on bed of rush . ' 

 " ' tush , fool ! ' snarl Mother Sub - Prioress . " ' the Poor be not easily make ill . ' 

 " tush indeed ! I tell thee , little bright - eyed man , old Antony , can ' tush ' to well purpose ! that night there be strong purging herb in the broth of Mother Sub - Prioress . yet she do but keep her bed for one day . like the Poor , she be not easily make ill ! . . . well , have thy way ; only peck not my finger , Master Robin , or I will have thee flog through the tything at the cart - tail , as be do to a certain pieman , whose history I will now relate . 

 " once upon a time , when Sister Mary Antony be young , and fair to look upon Nay , wink not thy naughty eye " 

 at that moment come the sound of a key turning slowly in the lock of the door at the bottom of the step lead from the crypt to the cloister . 

 CHAPTER III 

 the PRIORESS pass 

 a key turn slowly in the lock of the oaken door at the entrance to the underground way . 

 the old lay - sister seize her wallet and pull out the bag of pea . 

 below , the heavy door swing back upon its hinge . 

 Mary Antony drop upon her knee to the right of the step , her hand hide beneath her scapulary , her eye bent in lowly reverence upon the sunlit flagstone , her lip mumble chance sentence from the Psalter . 

 the measured sound of softly move foot draw near , slightly shuffling as they reach the step and begin to mount , up from the mile - long darkness , into the sunset light . 

 first to appear be a young lay - sister , carry a lantern . hasten up the step , she extinguish the flame , grow sickly in the sunshine , place the lantern in a niche , and , drop upon her knee , opposite old Mary Antony , seek to join in the latter 's pious recitation . 

 " Adhaesit pavimento anima mea , " chant Mary Antony . " wherefore be the holy Ladies late to - day ? " 

 " one fall to weeping in the darkness , " intone the young lay - sister , " whereupon Mother Sub - Prioress cause all to stand still while she strove , by the light of my lantern hold high , to discover who have burst forth with a sob . none shew trace of tear , she give I back the lantern , herself walk last in the line , as all move on . " 

 " convertentur ad vesperam , and the devil catch the hindmost , " chant Mary Antony , with fervour . 

 " amen , " intone Sister Abigail , eye bent upon the ground ; for the tall figure of the prioress , mount the step , now come into view . 

 the Prioress pass up the cloister with a stately grace of motion which , even beneath the heavy cloth of her white robe , reveal the noble length of supple limb . her arm hang by her side , sway gently as she walk . there be a look of strength and of restfulness about the long finger and beautifully mould hand . her face , calm and purposeful , be lift to the sunlight . suffering and sorrow have leave thereon indelible mark ; but the clear grey eye , beneath level brow , be luminous with a light betoken the victory of a pure and noble spirit over passionate and most human flesh . 

 no sinner , in her presence , ever feel crush by hopeless weight of sin ; no saint , before the gaze of her calm eye , feel sure of be altogether faultless . 

 so truly be she woman , that all humanity seem lift to her level ; so completely be she saint , that sin do slink away abash before her come . 

 they who fear she most , be most conscious of her kindness . they who love she good , be least able to venture near . 

 in the first bloom of her womanhood she have leave the world , resign high rank , fair land , and the wealth which make for power . her faith in human love have be rudely shatter , she have seek security in Divine compassion , and consolation in the daily contemplation of the Man of Sorrows . in her cell , on a rough wooden cross , hang a life - size figure of the die Saviour . 

 she have not reach her twenty - fifth year when , flee from the world , she join the Order of the White Ladies of Worcester , and pass into the seclusion and outward calm of the Nunnery at Whytstone . 

 five year later , on the death of the aged prioress , she be elect , by a large majority , to fill the vacant place . 

 she have now , during two year , rule the Nunnery wisely and well . 

 she have rule her own spirit , even well . she have win the victory over the World and the Flesh ; there remain but the Devil . the Devil , alas , always remain . 

 as she move , with uplifted brow and mien of calm detachment , along the sunlit cloister to the lofty , stone passage , within , the Convent , she be fear by many , love by most , and obey by all . 

 and , as she pass , old Mary Antony , bow almost to the ground , drop a large white pea , from between her right thumb and finger , into the horny palm of her left hand . 

 behind the prioress there follow a nun , tall also , but ungainly . her short - sighted eye peer shiftily to right and leave ; her long nose go on before , scent possible scandal and wrong - doing ; her weak lip let loose a ready smile , insinuating , crafty , apologetic . she walk with hand cross upon her breast , in attitude of adoration and humility . as she move by , old Mary Antony let drop the pale and speckle pea . 

 keep their distance , mostly with shrouded face , bent head , and fold hand , all the White Ladies pass . 

 each go in silence to her cell , there kneel in prayer and contemplation until the Refectory bell should call to the evening meal . 

 as the last , save one , go by , the keen eye of the old lay - sister note that her hand be clench against her breast , that she stumble at the topmost step , and catch her breath with a half sob . 

 behind she , move quickly , come the spare form of the Sub - Prioress , ferret - face , alert , vigilant ; fearful lest sin should go unpunished ; wishful to be the punisher . 

 she must have hear the half - strangle sob burst from the slight figure stumble up the step before she , have not old Mary Antony be suddenly move at that moment to uplift her voice in a cracked and raucous " amen . " 

 startle , and vex at be startle , the Sub - Prioress turn upon 
 Mary Antony . 
 " peace , woman ! " she say . " the Convent cloister be not a hen - yard . such ill - time devotion well - nigh merit penance . rise from thy knee , and go at once about thy business . " 

 the Sub - Prioress hasten on . 

 scowl darkly , old Antony bend forward , look , past Mother 
 Sub - Prioress , up the cloister to the distant passage . 
 Sister Mary Seraphine have reach her cell . the door be shut . 

 Old Antony 's knee creak as she arise , but her wizened face be once more cheerful . 

 " Beans in her broth to - night , " she say . " one for ' woman ' ; another for the hen - yard ; a third for threaten penance when I do but chant a melodious ' amen . ' I will give her bean castor bean ! " 

 down the step she go , push the heavy door to , lock it , and draw forth the key ; then turn her step toward the cell of the Reverend Mother . 

 on her way thither , she pause at a certain door and listen , her ear against the oaken panel . then she hurry onward , knock upon the door of the Reverend Mother 's cell and , be bid to enter , pass within , close the door behind she , and drop upon her knee . 

 the Prioress stand beside the casement , gaze at the golden glory of the sunset . she be , for the moment , unconscious of her surrounding . her mind be away behind those crimson battlement . 

 presently she turn and see the old woman , kneel at the door . 

 " how now , dear Antony ? " she say , kindly . " get up ! hang the key in its appoint place , and make I thy report . have all return ? as always , be all well ? " 

 the old lay - sister rise , hang the massive key upon a nail ; then come to the foot of the prioress , and knelt again . 

 " Reverend Mother , " she say , " all who go forth have return . but all be not well . Sister Mary Seraphine be utter wild cry in her cell ; and much I fear I , Mother Sub - Prioress may pass by , and hear she . " 

 the face of the prioress grow stern and sad ; yet , withal , tender . she raise the lay - sister , and gently pat the old hand which tremble . 

 " go thy way , dear Antony , " she say . " I myself will visit the little 
 Sister in her cell . none will attempt to enter while I be there . " 
 CHAPTER IV 

 " give ME tenderness , " she say 

 the Prioress knelt before a marble group of the Virgin and Child , place where the ray of evening sunshine , enter through the western casement , play over its white beauty , shed a radiance on the pure face of the Madonna , and a halo of golden glory around the Infant Christ . 

 " Mother of God , " pray the prioress , with folded hand , " give I patience in deal with wilfulness ; grant I wisdom to cope with unreason ; may it be give I to share the pain of this heart in torment , even as when thou didst witness the suffering of thy dear Son , our Lord , on Calvary a sword pierce through thine own soul also . 

 " give I this gift of sympathy with suffering , though the cross be not mine own , but another 's . 

 " but give I firmness and authority : even as when thou didst say to the servant at Cana : ' Whatsoever he saith unto you , do it . ' " 

 the Prioress wait , with bow head . 

 then , of a sudden she put forth her hand , and touch the marble foot of the Babe . 

 " give I tenderness , " she say . 

 CHAPTER V 

 the WAYWARD NUN 

 Sister Mary Seraphine lie prone upon the floor of her cell . 

 tightly clench in her hand be fragment of her tear veil . 

 she beat her knuckle upon the stone with rhythmic regularity ; then , when her arm would lift no long , take up the measure with her toe , in wild imitation of a gallop horse . 

 as she lay , she repeat with monotonous reiteration : " trapping of crimson , and silver bell : mane and tail , like foam of the wave ; a palfrey as white as snow ! " 

 the Prioress enter , close the door behind she , and look searchingly at the prostrate figure ; then , lift the master - key which hang from her girdle , lock the door on the inside . 

 Sister Mary Seraphine have be silent long enough to hear the closing and locking of the door . 

 now she start afresh . 

 " trapping of crimson , and silver bell " 

 the Prioress walk over to the narrow casement , and stand look out at the rosy cloud wreathe a pale green sky . 

 " oh ! . . . oh ! . . . oh ! . . . " wail Sister Mary Seraphine , writhe upon the floor ; " mane and tail , like foam of the wave ; a palfrey as white as snow ! " 

 the Prioress watch the swallow on swift wing , chase fly in the evening light . 

 so complete be the silence , that Sister Mary Seraphine notwithstanding that turning of the key in the lock fancy she must be alone . 

 " trapping of crimson , and silver bell ! " she declaim with vehemence ; then lift her face to peep , and see the tall figure of the Prioress stand at the casement . 

 instantly , Sister Mary Seraphine drop her head . 

 " Mane and tail , " she begin then her courage fail ; the " foam of the wave " quaver into indecision ; and indecision , in such a case , be fatal . 

 for a while she lie quite still , moan plaintively , then , of a sudden , quiver from head to foot , start up alert , as if to listen . 

 " Wilfred ! " she shriek ; " Wilfred ! be you come to save I ? " 

 then she open her eye , and peep again . 

 the prioress , wholly unmove by the impending advent of " Wilfred , " stand at the casement , calmly watch the swallow . 

 Sister Mary Seraphine begin to weep . 

 at last the passionate sobbing cease . 

 unbroken silence reign in the cell . 

 from without , the latch of the door be lift ; but the lock hold . 

 presently Sister Mary Seraphine drag herself to the foot of the 
 Prioress , seize the hem of her robe , and kiss it . 
 then the Prioress turn . she firmly withdraw her robe from those cling hand ; yet look , with eye of tender compassion , upon the kneeling figure at her foot . 

 " Sister Seraphine , " she say , " for you must shew true penitence e'er I can permit you to be call by our Lady 's name you will now come to my cell , where I will presently speak with you . " 

 Sister Seraphine instantly fall prone . 

 " I can not walk , " she say . 

 " you will not walk , " reply the prioress , sternly . " you will travel upon your hand and knee . " 

 she cross to the door , unlocked and set it wide . 

 " moreover , " she add , from the doorway , " if you do not appear in my presence in reasonable time , I shall be constrain to send for Mother Sub - Prioress . " 

 the cell of the Prioress be situate at the opposite end of the long , stone passage ; but in less than reasonable time , Sister Seraphine crawl in . 

 the unwonted exercise have have a most salutary effect upon her frame of mind . 

 her straight habit , of heavy cloth , have render progress upon her knee awkward and difficult . her hand have become entangled in her tear veil . each moment she have fear lest cell door , on either side , should open ; old Antony might appear from the cloister , or great disaster of all Mother Sub - Prioress might advance toward she from the refectory stair ! in order to attain a great rate of speed , she have try lift her knee , as elephant lift their foot . this mode of progress , though ungainly , have prove efficacious ; but would have be distinctly mirth - provoking to beholder . the stone have hurt her hand and knee far more than she hurt they when she beat upon the floor of her own cell . 

 she arrive at the Reverend Mother 's footstool , heat in mind and body , ashamed of herself , vex with her garment , in fact in an altogether saner frame of mind than when she have call upon " Wilfred , " and make reiterated mention of trapping of crimson and silver bell . 

 perhaps the Prioress have foresee this result , when she impose the penance . leniency or sympathy , at that moment , would have be fatal and foolish ; and have not the Prioress make special petition for wisdom ? 

 she be seat at her table , when Sister Seraphine bump and shuffle into view . she do not raise her eye from the illuminated missal she be study . one hand lie on the massive clasp , the other rest in readiness to turn the page . her noble form seem stately calm personify . 

 when she hear Sister Seraphine pant close to her foot , she speak ; still without lift her eye . 

 " you may rise to your foot , " she say , " and shut to the door . " 

 then the wait hand turn the page , and silence fall . 

 " you may arrange the disorder of your dress , " say the prioress , and turn another page . 

 when at length she look up , Sister Seraphine , clothed and apparently in her right mind , stand humbly near the door . 

 the Prioress close the book , and shut the heavy clasp . 

 then she point to an oaken stool , sign to the nun to draw it forward . 

 " be seat , my child , " she say , in tone of infinite tenderness . " there be much which must now be say , and your mind will pay well heed , if your body be at rest . " 

 with her steadfast eye the prioress search the pretty , flushed face , swell with weeping , and now gather a look of petulant defiance , thinly veil beneath surface humility . 

 " what be the cause of this outburst , my child ? " ask the prioress , very gently . 

 " while in the Cathedral , Reverend Mother , up in our gallery , I , be place not far from a window , hear , in a moment of silence , the neighing of a horse in the street without . it be like to the neighing of mine own lovely palfrey , wait in the castle court at home , until I should come down and mount he . each time that steed neigh , I could see Snowflake more clearly , in trapping of gay crimson , with silver bell , amid many other prance impatiently , champ their bit as they wait ; for it please I to come out last , when all be mount . then the rider lift their plume cap when I appear , while Wilfred , push my page aside , do swing I into the saddle . thus , with shout and laughter and winding of horn , we would all ride out to the hunt or the tourney ; I first , on Snowflake ; Wilfred , close behind . " 

 very quietly the Prioress sit listen . she do not take her eye from the flushed face . a slight colour ting her own cheek . 

 " who be Wilfred ? " she ask , when Sister Seraphine pause for breath . 

 " my cousin , whom I should have we d if " 

 " if ? " 

 " if I have not leave the world . " 

 the Prioress consider this . 

 " if your heart be set upon wed your cousin , my child , why do you profess a vocation and , renounce all worldly and carnal desire , gain admission to our sacred order ? " 

 " my heart be not set on marry my cousin ! " cry Sister Seraphine , with petulance . " I be weary of Wilfred . I be weary of everything ! I want to profess . I wish to become a nun . there be people I could punish , and people I could surprise , well so , than in any other way . but Wilfred say that , when the time come , he would be there to carry I off . " 

 " and when the time come ? " 

 " he be not there . I never see he again . " 

 the Prioress turn , and look out through the oriel window . she seem to be weigh , carefully , what she should say . 

 when at length she speak , she keep her eye fix upon the wave tree - top beyond the Convent wall . 

 " Sister Seraphine , " she say , " many who embrace the religious life , know what it be to pass through the experience you have now have ; but , as a rule , they fight the temptation and conquer it in the secret of their own heart , in the silence of their own cell . 

 " Memories of the life that be , before , choose the well part , we leave the world , come back to haunt we , with a wanton sweetness . such memory can not change the state , fix forever by our vow ; but they may awaken in we vain regret or worldly longing . therein lie their sinfulness . 

 " to help you against this danger , I will now give you two prayer , which you must commit to memory , and repeat whenever need arise . the first be from the Breviary . " 

 the Prioress draw toward her a black book with silver clasp , open it , and read therefrom a short prayer in Latin . but see no light of response or of intelligence upon the face of Sister Seraphine , she slowly repeat a translation . 

 Almighty and Everlasting God , grant that our will be ever meekly subject to Thy will , and our heart be ever honestly ready to serve Thee . amen . 

 her eye rest , with a wistful smile , upon the book . 

 " this prayer might suffice , " she say , " if our heart be truly honest , if our will be ever yield . but , alas , our heart be deceitful above all thing , and our will be apt to turn traitor to our good intention . 

 " therefore I have find for you , in the Gregorian Sacramentary , another prayer less well - know , yet much more ancient , write over six hundred year ago . it deal effectually with the deceitful heart , the insidious , tempting thought , and the unstable will . here be a translation which I have myself inscribe upon the margin . " 

 the Prioress lay her fold hand upon the missal and as she repeat the ancient sixth - century prayer , in all its depth of inspire simplicity , her voice thrill with deep emotion , for she be give to another that which have mean infinitely much to her own inner life . 

 Almighty God , unto whom all heart be open , all desire know , and from whom no secret be hide : cleanse the thought of our heart by the inspiration of Thy Holy Spirit , that we may perfectly love Thee , and worthily magnify Thy Holy Name , through Christ our Lord . amen . 

 the Prioress turn her face from Sister Seraphine 's unresponsive countenance and fix her eye once more upon the tree - top . she be think of the long year of secret conflict , know only to he from whom no secret be hide ; of the constant cleansing of her thought , for which she have so earnestly plead ; of the fear lest she should never worthily magnify that Holy Name . 

 presently her heart fill with humble tenderness she turn to 
 Sister Seraphine . 
 " these prayer , my child , which you will commit to memory before you sleep this night , will protect you from a too insistent recollection of the world you have resign ; and will assist you , with real inward thoroughness , to die daily to self , in order that the Holy Name of our dear Lord may be more worthily magnify in you . " 

 but , alas ! this gentle treatment , these long silence , this quiet recitation of holy prayer , have but stir the naughty spirit in Sister Seraphine . 

 her shallow nature fail to understand the deep of the noble heart , deal thus tenderly with she . she measure its ocean - wide greatness , by the little artificial runnel of her own morbid emotion . she mistook gentleness for weakness ; calm self - control , for lack of strength of will . her wholesome awe of the Prioress be forget . 

 " but I do not want to die ! " she exclaim . " I want to live to live to live ! " 

 the Prioress look up , astonish . 

 the surface humility have depart from the swollen countenance of 
 Sister Seraphine . the petulant defiance be plainly visible . 
 " Kneel ! " command the prioress , with authority . 

 the wayward nun jerk down upon her knee , upset the stool behind she . 

 the Prioress make a quick movement , then restrain herself . she have pray for patience in deal with wilfulness . 

 " we die that we may live , " she say , solemnly . " Sister Seraphine , this be the lesson your wayward heart must learn . die to self , we live unto God . die to sin , we live unto righteousness . die to the world , we find the Life Eternal . " 

 on her knee upon the floor , Sister Seraphine feel her position to be such as lend itself to pathos . 

 " but I want to live to the world ! " she cry , and burst into tear . 

 now convent life do not tend to further individual grief . constant devout contemplation of the Supreme Sorrow which work the world 's salvation lessen the inclination to shed tear of self - pity . 

 the Prioress be startle and alarm by the pathetic sob of Sister 
 Seraphine . 
 this young nun have but lately be send on to the Nunnery at Whytstone from a convent at Tewkesbury in which she have serve her novitiate , and take her final vow . the Prioress now realise how little she know of the inner working of the mind of Sister Seraphine , and blame herself for have look upon the outward appearance rather than upon the heart , take too much for grant , and rely too entirely upon the report of other . her sense of failure , toward the Community in general , and toward Seraphine in particular , lend she a fresh stock of patience . 

 she raise the weeping nun from the floor , put her arm around she , with protective gesture , and lead she before the Shrine of the Madonna . 

 " my child , " she say , " there be thing we be call upon to suffer which we can well tell to our blessed Lady , herself . try to unburden your heart and find comfort . . . do your mind hark back to the thought of the earthly love you resign in order to give yourself solely to the heavenly ? . . . be you trouble by fear lest you wrong the man you love , when , leave he , you become the bride of Heaven ? " 

 Sister Seraphine smile a scornful little smile . " Nay , " she say , " I be weary of Wilfred . but there be other . " 

 the voice of the prioress grow even graver , and more sad . 

 " be it then the fact of marriage which you desire and regret ? " 

 Sister Seraphine laugh a hard , self - conscious , little laugh . 

 " Nay , I could not have brook to be bind to any man . but I like to be love , and I like to be first in the thought and heart of another . " 

 the Prioress look at the pretty , tear - stain face , at the softly mould form . then an idea come to she . to voice it , lift the veil from the very Holy of Holies of her own heart 's suffering ; but she would not shrink from aught which could help this soul she be strive to uplift . 

 with her eye rest upon the Babe in the arm of the Virgin Mother , she ask , gravely and low : 

 " be it the ceaseless longing to have have a little child of your own to hold in your arm , to gather to your breast , to put to sleep upon your knee , which keep your heart turn restlessly back to the world ? " 

 Sister Seraphine gaze at the prioress , in utter amazement . 

 " Nay , then , indeed ! " she reply , impatiently . " always have I hat child . to escape from the vexation of motherhood be reason enough for leave the world . " 

 then the Prioress withdraw her protective arm , and look sternly upon 
 Sister Seraphine . 
 " you be play false to your vow , " she say ; " you be slight your vocation ; yet no worthy or noble feeling draw your heart back to the world . you do but desire vain pomp and show ; all those thing which minister to the enthronement of self . return to your cell and spend three hour in prayer and penitence before the crucifix . " 

 the Prioress lift her hand and point to the figure of the Christ , hang upon the great rugged cross against the wall , face the door . the sublimity of a supreme adoration be in her voice , as she make she last appeal . 

 " surely , " she say , ' surely no love of self can live , in view of the death and sacrifice of our blessed Lord ! Kneel then before the crucifix and learn " 

 but the over - wrought mind of Sister Seraphine , suddenly convince of the futility of its hopeless rebellion , pass , in that moment , altogether beyond control . 

 with a shout of wild laughter , she fling back her head , point with outstretched finger at the crucifix . 

 " death ! death ! death ! " she shriek , " helpless , hopeless , terrible ! 
 I ask for life , I want to live ; I be young , I be gay , I be beautiful . 
 and they bid bid bid I kneel long hour watch death . " her 
 voice rise to a pierce scream . " ah , HA ! that will I not ! a dead 
 God can not help I ! I want life , not death ! " 
 shriek she leapt to her foot , fly across the room , beat upon the sacred Form with her fist ; tear at it with her finger . 

 one instant of petrify horror . then the prioress be upon she . 

 seize she by both wrist she fling she to the floor , then pull a rope pass over a pulley in the wall , which start the great alarm - bell , in the passage , clang wildly . 

 at once there come a rush of fly foot ; call for the Sub - Prioress ; but she be already there . 

 when they fling wide the door , lo , the prioress stand with white face and blaze eye , her arm outstretche between they and the crucifix . 

 upon the floor , a crumpled heap , lie Sister Mary Seraphine . 

 the nun , in a frightened crowd , fill the doorway , none dare to speak , or to enter ; till old Mary Antony , push past the Sub - Prioress , kneel down beside the Reverend Mother , and , lift the hem of her robe , kiss it and press it to her breast . 

 slowly the Prioress let fall her arm . 

 " Enter , " she say ; and they flock in . 

 " Sister Seraphine , " say the Prioress , in awful tone , " have profane the crucifix , revile our blessed Lord , who hang thereon . " 

 all the nun , fall upon their knee , hide their face in their hand . 

 there be a terrifying quality in the silence of the next moment . 

 slowly the Prioress turn , prostrate herself at the foot of the cross , and lay her forehead against the floor at its base . then the nun hear one deep , shudder sob . 

 not a head be lift . the only nun who peep be Sister Mary 
 Seraphine , prone upon the floor . 
 after a while , the Prioress arise , pale but calm . 

 " carry she to her cell , " she say . 

 two tall nun to whom she make sign lift Sister Seraphine , and bear she out . 

 when the shuffling of their foot die away in the distance , the 
 Prioress give further command . 
 " all will now go to their cell and kneel in adoration before the crucifix . door be to be leave stand wide . the Miserere be to be chant , until the ringing of the Refectory bell . Mother Sub - Prioress will remain behind . " 

 the nun disperse , as quickly as they have gather ; seek their cell , like frightened bird flee before a gathering storm . 

 the tall nun who have carry Sister Seraphine return and wait outside the Reverend Mother 's door . 

 the Prioress stand alone ; a tragic figure in her grief . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress draw near . her narrow face , peer from out her veil , more than ever resemble a ferret . her small eye gleam with a merciless light . 

 " be mine the task , Reverend Mother ? " she whisper . 

 the Prioress incline her head . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress murmur a second question . 

 the Prioress turn and look at the crucifix . 

 " yes , " she say , firmly . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress sidle nearer ; then whisper her third question . 

 the Prioress do not answer . she be look at the carve , oaken stool , overthrow . she be wonder whether she could have act with well judgment , speak more wisely . her heart be sore . such noble nature ever blame themselves for the wrong - doing of the worthless . 

 receive no reply , Mother Sub - Prioress whisper a suggestion . 

 " no , " say the Prioress . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress modify her suggestion . 

 the Prioress turn and look at the tender figure of the Madonna , brood over the blessed babe . 

 " no , " say the Prioress . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress frown , and make a further modification ; but in tone which suggest finality . 

 the Prioress incline her head . 

 the Sub - Prioress , bow low , lift the hem of the Reverend Mother 's veil , and kiss it ; then pass from the room . 

 the Prioress move to the window . 

 the sunset be over . the evening star shine , like a newly - light lamp , in a pale purple sky . the fleet - wing swallow have go to rest . 

 bat flit past the casement , like homeless soul who know not where to go . 

 low chanting begin in the cell ; the nun , with open door , sing miserere . 

 but , as she look at the evening star , the Prioress hear again , with startling distinctness , the final profanity of poor Sister Seraphine : " I want life not death ! " 

 along the corridor pass a short procession , on its way to the cell of 
 Mary Seraphine . 
 First go a nun , carry a lighted taper . 

 next , the two tall nun who have bear Mary Seraphine to her cell . 

 behind they , Mother Sub - Prioress , hold something beneath her scapulary which give to her more of a presence than she usually possess . 

 Solemn and official , nay , almost sacrificial be their measured shuffle , as they move along the passage , and enter the cell of Mary Seraphine . 

 the Prioress close her door , and , kneel before the crucifix , implore forgiveness for the sacrilege which , all unwittingly , she have provoke . 

 the nun , in their separate cell , chant the Miserere . but suddenly with one accord , their voice fall silent ; then hasten on , in uncertain , agitated rhythm . 

 Old Mary Antony below , play her favourite game , also pause , and prick up her ear : then fillipe the wizen pea , which stand for Mother Sub - Prioress , into the dark corner , and hurry off to brew a soothe balsam . 

 so , when the Refectory bell have summon all to the evening meal , the old lay - sister creep to the cell of Mary Seraphine , carry broth and comfort . 

 but Sister Seraphine be well content than she have be for many week . 

 at last she have become the centre of attention ; and , although , during the visit of Mother Sub - Prioress to her cell , this have be a peculiarly painful position to occupy , yet to the morbid mind of Mary Seraphine , the position seem worth the discomfort . 

 therefore , her mind now purge of its discontent , she cheerfully sup old Antony 's broth , and apply the soothe balsam ; yet plan the while , to gain favour with the prioress , by repeat to she , at the first convenient opportunity , the naughty remark concern Mother Sub - Prioress , now be make for her diversion , by the kind old woman who have risk reproof , in order to bring to she , in her disgrace , both food and consolation . 

 CHAPTER VI 

 the KNIGHT of the BLOODY VEST 

 " Nay , I have naught for thee this morning , " say Mary Antony to the robin ; " naught , that is , save spritely conversation . I can tell thee a tale or two ; I can give thee sage advice ; but , in my wallet , little Master Mendicant , I have but my bag of pea . " 

 the old lay - sister sit rest in the garden . she have have a busy hour , yet complicated in its busy - ness , for , start out to do weed , she have presently fancy herself intent upon make a posy , and now , sit upon the stone seat beneath the beech tree , hold a large nosegay make up of many kind of flower weed , arrange with much care , and bind round with convolvulus tendril . 

 Keen and uncommon shrewd though old Antony certainly be in many way , her great age occasionally betray itself by childish vagary . her mind would start off along the line of a false premise , land she eventually in a dream - like conclusion . as now , when wake from a moment 's nodding in the welcome shade , she wonder why her old back seem well - nigh break , and marvel to find herself hold a big posy of dandelion , groundsel , plantain , and bindweed . 

 on the other end of the seat , stand the robin . the beech be just near enough to the cloister , the pieman 's tree , and his own particular yew hedge , to come within his little kingdom . 

 have mention her bag of pea , Mary Antony experience an irresistible desire to view they and , moreover , to display they before the bright eye of the robin . 

 she lay the queer nosegay down upon the grass at her foot , turn sidewise on the stone slab , and draw the bag from her wallet . 

 " now , Master Pieman ! " she say . " at thine own risk thou doest it ; but with thine own bright eye thou shalt see the holy Ladies ; the Unnamed , all like pea in a pod , as the Lord know they do look , when they walk to and fro ; but first , if so be that I can find they , the few which I distinguish from among the rest . " 

 presently , after much peer into the bag , the fine white pea , the wizened pea , and the pale and speckle pea , lie in line upon the stone . 

 " this , " explain Mary Antony , point , with knobby forefinger , to the first , " be the Reverend Mother , Herself large , and pure , and noble . . . . Nay , hop not too close , Sir Redbreast ! when we enter her chamber we kneel at the threshold , till she bid we draw nearer . true , we be merely soberly - clothe , holy woman , whereas thou art a gay , gaudy man ; bold - eye , and , doubtless , steep in sin . but even thou must keep thy distance , in presence of this most Reverend pea of great price . 

 " this , " indicate the shrivelled pea , " be Mother Sub - Prioress , who would love to have the whipping of thee , thou naughty little rascal ! 

 " this be Sister Mary Rebecca who daily grow more crooked , both in mind and body ; yet who ever sweetly smileth . 

 " now will I show thee , if so be that I can find she , Sister Teresa , a kindly soul and gracious , but with a sniff which may be hear in the kitchen when that holy Lady taketh her turn at the refectory reading . and when , the reading over , have sniff every other minute , she at length , feel free to blow , beshrew I , Master Redbreast , one might think our old dun cow have just be part from a newly - bear calf . yea , a kind , gracious soul ; but noisy about the nose , and forgetful of the ear of other people , her own necessity seem excuse enough for veritable trumpet blast . " 

 Mary Antony , half turn as she talk , peer into the open bag in search of Sister Teresa . 

 then , quick as think , the unexpected happen . 

 three rapid hop , a jerky bend of the red breast , a flash of wing 

 the robin have fly off with the white pea ! the shrivelled and the speckle alone remain upon the seat . 

 utter a cry of horror and dismay , the old lay - sister fall upon her knee , lift despair hand to tree and sky . 

 down by the low wall , in earnest meditation , the prioress move back and forth , on the Cypress Walk . 

 Mary Antony 's shriek of dismay , faint but unmistakable , reach her ear . turn , she pass noiselessly up the green sward , on the further side of the yew hedge ; but pause , in surprise , as she draw level with the beech ; for the old lay - sister 's voice penetrate the hedge , and the first word she overhear seem to the Prioress wholly incomprehensible . 

 " ah , thou Knight of the Bloody Vest ! " moan Mary Antony . " Heaven send thy wicked perfidy may fall on thine own pate ! intrude thyself into our most private place ; beg food , which could not be refuse ; wheedle old Mary Antony into let thee have a peep at the holy Ladies thou bold , bad man ! and then carry off the Reverend Mother , herself ! ha ! hadst thou but catch away Mother Sub - Prioress , she would have reform thy home , whip thy child , and mend thine own vile manner , thou graceless churl ! or hadst thou take Sister Mary Rebecca , she would have bring the place about thine ear , tell thy wife fine tale of thine unfaithfulness ; whisper that Mary Antony be young and fair than she . but , nay , forsooth ! neither of these will do ! Thou must need snatch away the Reverend Mother , herself ! oh , sacrilegious fiend ! stand not there mock I ! where be the Reverend mother ? " 

 " why , here be I , dear Antony , " say the Prioress , in soothe tone , come quickly from behind the hedge . 

 one glance reveal , to her relief , that the lay - sister be alone . tear run down the furrow of her wear old face . she kneel upon the grass ; beside she a large nosegay of flower weed ; upon the seat , pea strew from out a much - use , linen bag . above she on a bough , a robin perch , bend to look , with roguish eye , at the scatter pea . 

 to the prioress it seem that indeed the old lay - sister must have take leave of her sens . 

 stoop , she try to raise she ; but Mary Antony , fling herself forward , clasped and kiss the Reverend Mother 's foot , in an abandonment of penitence and grief . 

 " Nay , rise , dear Antony , " say the prioress , firmly . " rise ! I command it . the day be warm . thou hast be dream . no bold , bad man have force his way within these wall . no ' Knight of the Bloody Vest ' be here . rise up and look . we be alone . " 

 but Mary Antony , still on her knee , half raise herself , and , point to the bough above , quaver , amid her sob : " the bold , bad man be there ! " 

 look up , the prioress meet the bright eye of the robin , peep down . 

 why , surely ? yes ! there be the " Bloody Vest . " 

 the Prioress smile . she begin to understand . 

 the robin burst into a stream of triumphant song . at which , old Mary 
 Antony , still kneel , shake her uplifted fist . 
 the Prioress raise and draw she to the seat . 

 " now sit thee here beside I , " she say , " and make full confession . ease thine old heart by tell I the entire tale . then I will pass sentence on the robin if , true to his name , he turn out to be a thief . " 

 so there , in the Convent garden , while the robin sing overhead , the Prioress listen to the quaint recital ; the dread of make mistake in the daily counting ; the elaborate plan of drop pea ; the manner in which the pea become identify with the personality of the White Ladies ; the game in the cell ; the taming of the robin ; the habit of share with the little bird , interest which might not be share with other , which have result that morning in the display of the pea , and this undreame of disaster the abduction of the Reverend Mother . 

 the Prioress listen with outward gravity , strive to conceal all sign of the inward mirth which seize and shake she . but more than once she have to turn her face from the peer eye of Mary Antony , strive anxiously to gather whether her chronicle of sin be place she outside the pale of possible forgiveness . 

 the Prioress do not hasten the recital . she know the importance , to the mind with which she deal , of even the most trivial detail . to be check or hurry , would leave Mary Antony with the sense of an incomplete confession . 

 therefore , with infinite patience the prioress listen , seat in the sunlit garden , undisturbed , save for the silent passing , once or twice , of a veil figure through the cloister , who , see the Reverend Mother seat beneath the beech , do reverence and hasten on , look not again . 

 when the garrulous old voice at last fall silent , the prioress , with kind hand , cover the restless finger clasp and unclasp in anxious contortion and firmly hold they in fold stillness . 

 her first word be of a thing as yet unmentione . 

 " Dear Antony , " she say , " be that thy posy lie at our foot ? " 

 " ah , Reverend Mother , " sigh the old lay - sister , " in this do I again do wrong meaning to do right . Sister Mary Augustine , come into the kitchen with leave , from Mother Sub - Prioress , to make the pasty , and desire to be free to make they heavy unhampere by my advice which , of a surety , would have help they to lightness bade I go out and weed the garden . 

 " weed , I bethink I how much liefer I would be gather a posy of choice flower for our sweet Lady 's shrine ; and , thus think , I begin to do , not accord to Sister Mary Augustine 's hard task , but accord to mine own heart 's prompting . yet , when the posy be finish , alack - a - day ! it be a posy of weed ! " 

 Tears fill the eye of the prioress ; at first she could not trust her voice to make reply . 

 then , stoop she pick up the nosegay . 

 " our Lady shall have it , " she say . " I will place it before her shrine , in mine own cell . she will understand know how often , though the hand perforce do weed , yet , all the time , the heart be gather choicest flower . 

 " Aye , and sometimes when we bring to God offering of fair flower , he see but worthless weed . and , when we mourn , because we have but weed to offer , he see they fragrant blossom . whatever , to the eye of man , the hand may hold , God see therein the bouquet of the heart 's intention . " 

 the Prioress pause , a look of great gladness on her face ; then , as she see the old lay - sister still eye her posy with dissatisfaction : " and , after all , dear Antony , " she say , " who shall decide which flower shall be dub ' weed ' ? no plant of his creation , however humble , be call a ' weed ' by the Creator . when , for man 's sin , he curse the ground , he say : ' thorn also and thistle shall it cause to bud . ' well ? sharpest thorn be find around the rose ; the thistle be the royal bloom of Scotland ; and , if our old white ass could speak her mind , doubtless she would call it king of Flowers . 

 " nowhere in Holy Books , be any plant name a ' weed . ' it be leave to man to proclaim that the flower he want not , be weed . 

 " look at each one of these . could you or I , labour for year , with all our skill , make anything so perfect as the mean of these weed ? 

 " Nay ; they be weed , because they grow , there where they should not be . the gorgeous scarlet poppy be a weed amid the corn . if rose overgrow the wheat , we should dub they weed , and root they out . 

 " and some of we have have , perforce , so to deal with the rose in our life ; those sweet and fragrant thing which overgrow our offering of the wheat of service , our sacrifice of praise and prayer . 

 " perhaps , when our weed be all tear out , and cast in a tangled heap before his foot , our Lord behold in they a garland of choice blossom . the crown of thorn on earth , may prove , in Paradise , a diadem of flower . " 

 the Prioress lay the posy on the seat beside she . 

 " now , Antony , about thy game with pea . there be no wrong in keep count with pea of those who daily walk to and from Vespers ; though , I admit , it seem to I , it be easy to count one , two , three , with fold hand , than to let fall the pea from one hand to the other , beneath thy scapulary . Howbeit , a method which would be but a pitfall to one , may prove a prop to another . so I give thee leave to continue to count with thy pea . also the game in thy cell be harmless , and lead I to think , as already I have sometimes think , that game with ball or ring , something in which eye guide the hand , and mind the eye , might be helpful for all , on summer evening . 

 " but I can not have thee take upon thyself to decide the future state of the White Ladies . who art thou , to send I to Paradise with a fillip of thine old finger - nail , yet to keep our excellent Sub - Prioress in Purgatory ? shame upon thee , Mary Antony ! " but the sternness of the Reverend Mother 's tone be belie by the merriment in her grey eye . 

 " so no more of that , my Antony ; though , truth to tell , thy story give I relief , answer a question I be mean to put to thee . I hear , not an hour ago , that Sister Antony have boast that with a turn of her thumb and finger she could , any night , send Mother Sub - Prioress to Purgatory . " 

 " who say that of I ? " stutter Mary Antony . " who say it , Reverend 
 Mother ? " 
 " a little bird , " murmur the prioress . " a little bird , dear Antony ; but not thy pretty robin . also , the boast be take to mean poison in the broth of Mother Sub - Prioress . Hast thou ever put harmful thing in the broth of Mother Sub - Prioress ? " 

 Mary Antony slip to her knee . 

 " only bean , Reverend Mother , castor bean ; and , when her temper be vilest , purge herb . nothing more , I swear it ! Old Antony know naught of poison ; only of mix balsam ah , ha ! and soothe ointment ! our blessed Lady know the tale be false . " 

 hastily the prioress lift the nosegay and bury her face in bindweed and dandelion . 

 " I believe thee , " she say , in a voice not over steady . " rise from thy knee . but , remember , I forbid thee to put aught into Mother Sub - Prioress 's broth , save thing that soothe and comfort . give I thy word for this , Antony . " 

 the old woman humbly lift the hem of the prioress 's robe , and press it to her lip . 

 " I promise , Reverend Mother , " she say , " and I do repent I of my sin . " 

 " sit beside I , " command the prioress . " I have more to say to thee . . . . think not hard thought of the Sub - prioress . she be stern , and extreme to mark what be do amiss , but this she conceive to be her duty . she be a most pious Lady . her zeal be but a sign of her piety . " 

 Mary Antony 's keen eye , meet those of the Prioress , twinkle . 

 once again the prioress take refuge in the posy . she be begin to have have enough of the scent of dandelion . 

 " Mother Sub - Prioress be sick , " she say . " the cold strike she last evening , after sunset , in the orchard . I have bid she to keep her bed awhile . we must tend she kindly , Antony , and help she back to health again . 

 " Sister Mary Rebecca be also sick , with pain in her bone and slight fever . she too keep her bed to - day . strive to feel kindly toward she , Antony . I know she oft think evil where none be mean , tell tale of wrong which be mostly of her own imagining . but , in so do , she harm herself more than she can harm other . 

 " by stir up the mud in a dark pool , you dim the reflection of the star which , before , shine bright within it . but you do not dim the star , shin on high . 

 " so be it with the slanderous thought of evil mind . they stir up their own murkiness ; but they fail to dim the star . 

 " we must bear with Sister Mary Rebecca . " 

 " go not nigh they , Reverend Mother , " beg old Antony . " I will tend they with due care and patience . these pain in bone , and general shivering , be give quickly from one to another . I pray you , go not near . remember you be take alas ! alas ! and they be leave ! " 

 at this the prioress laugh , gaily . 

 " but I be not take decently , with pain in my bone and a - bed , dear 
 Antony . I be carry off by a bold , bad man thy Knight of the Bloody 
 Vest . " 
 " oh , pray ! " cry the old lay - sister . " I fear I it be an omen . the angel Gabriel , Reverend Mother , send to bear you from earth to heaven . ' the one shall be take , and the other left . ' ah , if he have but fly off with Mother Sub - Prioress ! " 

 the prioress laugh again . " Dear Antony , thy little bird take the first pea he see . have there but be a crumb , or a morsel of cheese , he would have leave thee thy white pea . . . Hark how he sing his little song of praise ! . . . be it not wonderful to call to mind how , century ago , when white - rob Druids cut mistletoe from british oak , the robin redbreast hop around , and sing ; when , early still , man be wild and savage , dwell in hole and cave and hut of mud , when church and cloister be unknown in this land and the one true God undreame of , robin mat and make their nest , the speckle thrush sing , ' do it now do it now , ' as they seek food for their young , the blackbird whistle , and the swallow flash by on joyous wing . Aye , and when Eve and Adam walk in Eden , amid strange beast and gaily plumage bird , here in these Isles the robin redbreast sing , and all our british bird busily build their nest and rear their young ; live their little joyous life , as he who make they teach they how to do . 

 " and , in the century to come , when all thing may be change in this our land , when we shall long have go to dust , when our love cloister may have crumble into ruin ; still the hill of Malvern will stand , and the silvery severn flow along the valley ; while here , in this very garden if it be a garden still the robin will build his nest , and carol his happy song . 

 " mark you this , dear Mary Antony : all thing make by man hold within they the element of change and of decay . but nature be at one with God , and therefore immutable . earthly kingdom may rise and wane ; mighty city may spring up , then fall into ruin . nation may conquer and , in their turn , be conquer . Man may slay man and , in his turn , be slay . but , through it all , the mountain stand , the river flow , the forest wave , and the redbreast build his nest in the hawthorn , and warble a love - song to his mate . " 

 the Prioress rise and stretch wide her arm to the sunlit garden , to the bough where the robin sing . 

 " oh , to be one with God and with Nature ! " she cry . " oh , to know the essential mystery of Life and Light and Love ! this be Life Eternal ! " 

 she have forget the old lay - sister ; aye , for the moment she have forget the Convent and the cloister , the mile - long walk in darkness , the chant of the unseen monk . she trod again the springy heather of her youth ; she hear the rush of the mountain stream ; the sigh of the great forest ; the rustle of the sunlit glade , alive with , life . these all be in the robin 's song . then 

 within the Convent , the Refectory bell clang loudly . 

 the Prioress let fall her arm . 

 she pick up the nosegay of weed .

 CHAPTER VII 

 the MADONNA in the CLOISTER 

 the Prioress knelt , in prayer and meditation , before the figure of the 
 Virgin Mother hold upon her knee the holy Babe .

 " Mother of God , " she say , " help this poor ache heart ; still the wild hunger at my breast . make I content to be at one with the Divine , and to let nature go . . . . Thou know it be not the man I want . in all the long year since he play traitor to his troth to I , I have not want the man . the woman he we d may have he , unbegrudge by I . I want the little foot , rest together in my hand . . . . all Nature sing of life , and the power to bestow life . yet mine arm be empty , and my strength do but carry mine own self to and fro . . . . oh , give I grace to turn my thought from Life to Sacrifice .  " the Lord looketh on the heart . "

 CHAPTER VIII 

 on the wing of the storm

 as the prioress walk to and fro , unconsciously miss the daily exercise of the passage to the Cathedral , she note a sudden darkening of her chamber . go to the window , she see the sky grow black with thunder cloud . so quickly the storm gather , that the bright summer world without seem suddenly hang over with a deep purple pall .

" she gasp . then the stern displeasure on that love face silence she . she drop upon her knee , ashen and trembling .

 " twenty White Ladies go , " whisper the old lay - sister . " I count they . twenty White Ladies go ; but " 

 " well ? " 

 " Twenty - one return , " chatter Mary Antony , and hide her face in the Reverend Mother 's robe .

 " Reverend Mother , twenty holy Ladies go " 

 " I know . and twenty return . " 

 " aye , " say the old woman more firmly , nettle out of her speechlessness ; " twenty return ; and twenty pea I drop from hand to hand . then when no pea remain yet another White Lady glide by ; and with she go an icy wind , and around she come the blackness of the storm .

I flee to the Reverend Mother , and run in on the roar of the thunder . " 

 " see you her face , Mary Antony ? " 

 " Nay , Reverend Mother . but , of late , the holy Ladies mostly walk by with their face shroud . "

 " but how could that be ? " object the prioress . " if twenty go , but twenty could return . who should be the twenty - first ? "

 but , even as she say it , swift come a name to the mind of the prioress , answer her own question , and fill she with consternation and a great anger . " Wilfred ! Wilfred , be you come to save I ? " foolish little Seraphine have say . be such sacrilege possible ? could one from the outside world have dare to intrude into their holy Sanctuary ?

 that the Dead should come again , and walk and move among the haunt of man , seek out the surrounding they have love and leave , seem always to hold terror for the untutored mind , which know not that the Dead be more alive than the living ; and that there be no death , save the death of sin . 

 but to the Reverend Mother , guard her flock from sin or shame , a visitor from the Unseen World hold less of horror than a possible intruder from the Seen . 

 a rapid glance as she sound the bell , have show she that the passage be empty .

 " now listen , dear Antony , " say the Prioress , hold the old woman with her look . " I must make sure that this twenty - first White Lady of thine be but a trick play on thee by thy pea . should she be anywhere in the Convent I shall most certainly have speech with she .

I shall pass to each cell and make sure that none be too greatly alarmed . "

 CHAPTER ix 

 the prioress shuts the DOOR

 in that dark corner , motionless , with shrouded face , stand a tall figure , garb in the dress of the nun of the Order of the White Ladies of Worcester . 

 perhaps the habit of silence be never of great value than in moment of sudden shock and horror . 

 one cry from the Prioress would have mean the instant opening of many door , and the arrival , on fly foot , of a score of frightened nun . 

 instead of scream , the prioress stand silent and perfectly still ; while every pulse in her body cease beat , during one moment of uncontrollable , cold horror . then , with a leap , her heart go on ; pound so loudly , that she could hear it in the silence . yet she keep command of every impulse which drive to sound or motion .

 " who art thou , and what doest thou here ? " 

 the figure answer not . 

 " art thou a ghostly visitor come back amongst we , from the Realm of the 
 Unseen ? " 
 the figure make no sign . " art thou then flesh and blood , and mortal as ourselves ? "

I warn you that your life have never hang by frailer thread than now it hang . your only hope of safety lie in do as I bid you . pass before I along this passage until you reach a chamber on the right , of which the door stand open . enter , and place yourself against the wall on the side farth from the door . there I will speak with you . " 

 with the shuffle step of a woman , and the bent shoulder of the very old , the figure move slowly forward , step upon the front of the white robe , stumble , but recover . 

 the Prioress watching , laugh a short scornful laugh , hold more of anger than of merriment .

 CHAPTER x 

 " I know you for a MAN " 

 enter her cell , the Prioress see at once that her order have be obey .

 the thunder rumble far away in the distance .

" you stand there , reveal ; and surely you stand there , sham . by plot and planning , by assume our dress , you have succeed in force your undesired presence into this sacred cloister , where dwell a little company of woman who have leave the world , never to return to it again ; who have give up much in order to devote themselves to a life of continual worship and adoration , gain thereby a power in intercession which bring down blessing upon those who still fight life 's battle in the world without . 

 " but it have mean the breaking of many a tender tie . there be father and brother dear to they , whom the nun would love to see again ; but they can not do so , save , on rare occasion , in the guest - room at the gate ; and then , with the grille between . 

 " Saving Bishop or Priest , no foot of man may tread our cloister ; no voice of man may be hear in these cell .

 the Prioress pause . 

 the figure stand , with fold arm , immovable , lean against the

 Wilfred . "

 CHAPTER XI 

 the YEARS ROLL back

 then the year roll back 

           

 it be moonlight on the battlement . the horse champ in the courtyard below . they two have climb to the topmost turret , that they might part as near the star as possible , and that , unseen by other , she might watch he ride away .

" then she catch his face to her breast . " thine and none other 's , forever , " she say ; and he feel her bosom heave with one deep sob .

 and now

 " seven month after I leave thee , a messenger reach our camp , bear letter from England ; no word for I from thee ; but a long missive from thy half - sister Eleanor , break to I the news that , be weary of my absence , and somewhat over - persuade , thou hadst wed Humphry ; Earl of Carnforth .

 " ' what good be it , ' she say , ' to beg the King for leave to hasten home ? if you kill Humphry , Hugh , you do but make a widow of the woman you have love ; nor could you we d the widow of a man yourself have slay . if Humphry kill you well , a valiant arm be lose to the Holy Cause , and other heart , more faithful than her , may come nigh to breaking . stay here , and play the man . '

 " these letter , with other from the camp , go back to England by that clerkly messenger . no answer be return to mine . 

 " meanwhile I go , with my despair , out to the battlefield . 

 " no tender shield be round I any more . I fight , like a mad wild beast . so often be I wound , that they dub I ' the Knight of the Bloody Vest . '

I need not tell thee , my cousin ' Frida fail . the Queen herself as good as bid I we d her favourite Lady . the Queen herself have to discover that she could command an english soldier 's life , but not his love . 

 " back in the field again , I find myself one day , cut off , surround , hew down , take prisoner ; but by a generous foe . 

 " thereafter follow year of much adventure ; escape , far distant wandering , strange company . many month I spend in a mountain fastness with a wise Hebrew Rabbi , who teach I his sacred scripture ; go back to the beginning of all thing , before the world be ; yet shrewd in judgment of the present , and throw a weird light forward upon the future . a strange man ; wise , as be all of that choose Race ; and a faithful friend . he do much to heal my hurt and woo I back to sanity . 

 " later , more than a year with a band of holy monk in a desert monastery , high among the rock ; good father who believe in Greek and Latin as sure of all balsam for a wound spirit , and who make I to become deeply learn in apostolic writing , and in the teaching of the Church . but , for all their good endeavour , I could not feel call to the perpetual calm of the Cloister . we be a line of fighter and hunter , man to whom pride of race and love of hearth and home , be primal instinct . 

 " thus , after many further wandering and much varying adventure , have by a strange chance hear news of the death of my father , and that my mother mourn . in solitude , the opening of this year find I land in England I who , by most , have long be give up for dead ; though Martin Goodfellow , fail to find trace of I in Palestine , have go back to Cumberland , and staunchly maintain his belief that I live , a captive , and should some day make my escape , and return . 

 " I pass with all speed to our Castle on the moor , know a mother 's heart wait here , for mother never cease to watch and hope . and , sure enough , as I ride up , the great door fly wide ; the house wait its master ; the mother be on the threshold to greet her son . aye ! it be good to be at home once more even in the land where my woman be bear child to another man . 

 " we spend a few happy day , I and my mother , together . then the joy of hope fulfil be sometimes a swifter harbinger to another world than the heavy load of sorrow she pass , without pain or sickness , smile , in her sleep ; she pass leave my home desolate indeed .

" 

 " with the first stirring of spring in forest and pasture , I feel move to ride south to the Court , and report my return to the king ; yet wait , strangely loath to go abroad where any turn of the road might bring I face to face with Humphry . I doubt , should we meet , if I could pass , without slay he , the man who have steal my betroth from I . so I stay in my own domain , bring thing into order , work in the armoury , and strive by hard exercise to throttle the grim demon of despair . 

 " April bring a burst of early summer ; and , on the first day of May , I set off for Windsor . 

 " pass through carnforth on my way , I find the town keep high holiday . I ask the reason , and be tell of a Tourney now in progress in the neighbourhood , to which the Earl have that morning ride in state , accompany by his Countess , who indeed be choose Queen of Beauty , and be to sit enthrone , attend by her little daughter , two tiny son act as page .

 " Thy sister Eleanor have die the year before . to thy beautiful castle and land , so near mine own , Eleanor 's son have succeed , and rule there in thy stead . he be at Court just then , I see he not , nor could I hear direct news of thee , though rumour say a convent .

 " I and my man await he . 

 " he have fatten on his hush - money ! he be no long lean and out at elbow . 

 " he screech at sight of I , think I rise from the dead . 

 " he screech still louder when he see the noose , fling over a strong bough . 

 " we leave he hang , when we ride away . that Judas kind will do the darkest deed for greed of gain . the first of the tribe himself shew the way by which it be most fitting to speed they from a world into which it have be good for they never to have be bear .

' the young prioress in the kingdom , ' say the Bishop , ' yet none could be wise or well fit to hold high authority . ' little do he dream that any mention of thee be as water to the parch desert ; yet he talk on , for love of speak of thee , while I sit pray he might tell I more ; yet barely answer yea or nay , seem to be absorb in mine own melancholy thought .

I mark that the nun descending , could not keep in view the nun in front who have just step forth into the crypt ; while she , move forward , would not perceive it if , slip from behind a pillar , another white figure silently join the procession behind she . once within the Convent , I trust to our Lady to help I to speech alone with thee ; and our blessed Lady hath not fail I . 

 " now I have tell thee all . " 

 with that the Knight leave speak ; and , after the long steady recitation , the ceasing of his voice cause a silence which , seem , to hold the very air suspend .

 CHAPTER XII 

 ALAS , the pity of it ! 

 at length the prioress speak . 

 " alas , " she say , " the pity of it ! ah , the cruel , cruel pity of it ! " 

 her voice , so sweet and tender , yet so hopeless in the unquestione finality of its regret , strike cold upon the heart of the Knight . 

 " but , my beloved , I have find thee , " he say , and drop upon one knee at her foot , he put out his hand to cover both her . but the Prioress be too quick for he . she hide her hand beneath her scapulary . the Knight 's brown finger close on the lion ' head . 

 " touch I not , " say the Prioress . 

 the Knight flush , darkly . 

 " you be mine , " he say . " mine to have and to keep . during these wretched year we have school ourselves each to think of the other as wed . now we know that neither have be faithless . I have find thee , my beloved , and I will not let thee go . "
