 " you be mine ! " say the Knight , fiercely ; and he lay his great hand upon her knee . 

 from beneath her scapulary , the Prioress draw the dagger . 

 " before I go to the cloister door , " she say , " I take this from its hiding - place , and put it in my girdle . I guess I have a man to deal with ; though , Heaven know , I dream not it be thou ! but I tell thee , Hugh , if thou , or any man , attempt to lay defiling touch upon any nun in this Priory myself , or another I strike , and I strike home . this blade will be drive up to the hilt in the offender 's heart . " 

 the Knight rise to his foot , step to the window and lean , with fold arm , against the wall . 

 " put back thy weapon , " he say , sternly , " into its hiding - place . no other man be here ; yet , should another come , my sword would well suffice to guard thine honour , and the honour of thy nun . " 

 she look at his dark face , scornful in its pain ; then go at once , obedient , to the secret panel . 

 " yes , Hugh , " she say . " that much of trust indeed I owe thy love . " 

 as she place the dagger in the wall and close the panel , something fall from she , intangible , yet real . 

 for so long , she have have to command . bow , kneeling , hurry woman fly to do her behest . each vie with the other to magnify her office . often , she feel lonely by reason of her dignity . 

 and now a man 's dark face frown on she in scornful anger ; a man 's stern voice fling back her elaborate threat with a short command , which disarm she , yet which she obey . moreover , she find it strangely sweet to obey . behind the sternness , behind the scornful anger , there throb a great love . in that love she trust ; but with that love she have to deal , put it from she with a finality which should be beyond question . 

 yet the " prioress " fall from she , as she close the panel . it be the 
 Woman and the Saint who move over to the window and stand beside the 
 Knight , in the radiance of a golden sunset after storm . 
 there be about she , as she speak , a wistful humbleness ; and a patient sadness , infinitely touching .

I hasten to offer to God the love and the life which have be slight by man . I confess this have since seem to I but a poor second - good to have bring to he , who indeed should have our very good . but , daily kneeling at his foot , I say : ' a broken and a contrite heart , Lord , Thou wilt not despise . ' my heart be ' break , ' when I bring it here . it have be ' contrite ' since . and well I know , although so far from worthy , it have not be despise . " 

 she lift her eye to the golden glory behind the battlement of purple cloud .

 the Knight be breathe hard . the fold arm rise and fall , with the heaving of his chest . but he keep his lip firm shut ; though pray , all the while , that our Lady might have , also , some understanding of the heart of a man ! 

 " I think it right that you should know , dear Hugh , " go on the sad voice , gently ; " that , at first , I suffer greatly . I spend long agonizing night , kneel before our Lady 's shrine , implore strength to conquer the love and the longing which have become sin . " 

 a stifle groan break from the Knight . 

 the golden light shine in her steadfast eye , and play about her noble brow .

 " Mora ! " cry the Knight she start . it be so long since she have hear her own name " you pray for strength to conquer , when you think it sin ; just as I ride out to meet the foe , to fight and slay , and afterward wrestle with unknown tongue , do all those thing which be hard , while strive to quench my love for you . but when I know that no other man have right to you or ever have have right , why then I find that nothing have slay my love , nor ever could . and Mora , now you know that I be free , be your love dead ? " 

 she clasp her hand over the cross at her breast . his voice hold a deep passion of appeal ; yet he strove , loyally , to keep it calm .

" if , think I faithless , you have turn for consolation to another ; if , though you bring she but your second well , you yet have win and we d she ; now , find after all that I have not wed Humphry , would you leave your bride , and try to wake again your love for I ? "

 she pal , but persist . 

 " but , if , Hugh ? if ? " 

 " then , no , " he say . " I should not leave one I have we d. but "

Nay , then , never ! " 

 she tremble , waver ; then flee to the shrine of the Virgin , kneel with hand outstretche .

 he follow , and kneel beside she ; his proud head bent ; his voice break with emotion .

" Thou who didst dwell in the earthly home at Nazareth , help this woman of mine to understand , that if she break she troth to I , hold herself from I , now when I be come to claim she , she send I forth to an empty life , to a hearth beside which no woman will sit , to a home forever desolate .  loose her hand from his , she clasp both upon her breast .

 " Mora , " he say , and his voice hold a new tone , a tone of sadness and solemnity ; " far be it from I to tempt you . I will plead with you but once again , in presence of our Lady and of the Holy Child ; and , have so do , I will say no more .

I ask you to keep your plighted word to I , and to become my wife . if you refuse , I go , return not again .  " you leave to I the crucifix heart break , love betray ; foot and hand nail to the wood of cruel circumstance ; side pierce by spear of treachery lonely , forsaken . but you take from I all the good , both in life and in religion ; all that tell of love , of joy , of hope for the year to come .

Mora ? . . . come ! " 

 the Prioress rise and face he . 

 " I can not come , " she say . " that which I have teach to other , I must myself perform . Hugh , I be dead to the world ; and if I be dead to the world , how can I live to you ? have I , in very deed , die and be entomb , you would not have go down into the vault and force my resting - place , that you might look upon my face , clasp my cold hand , and pour into deaf ear a tale of love . yet that be what , by trick and artifice , you now have do . you come to a dead woman , say ; ' love I , and be my wife . ' she must , perforce , make answer : ' how shall I , who be dead to the world , live any long therein ? ' take a wife from among the Living , Hugh . come not to seek a bride among the Dead . " 

 " Mother of God ! " exclaim the Knight , " be this religion ? " 

 he turn to the window , then to the door . " how can I go from here ? " 

 the stifle horror in his voice chill the very soul of the woman to whom he speak . she have , indeed at last make he to understand .

I fear I , you must go back the way you come ; nor can you go alone . we hold the key to unlock the door lead from our passage into the Cathedral crypt . I will now send all the nun to the Refectory . then I myself must take you to the crypt . " 

 " can I not walk alone , " ask the Knight , brusquely ; " return you the key by messenger ? " 

 " Nay , " say the prioress , " I dare run no risk . so quickly rumour be afloat . to - morrow , this strange hour must be a dream ; and you and I alone , the dreamer . now , while I go and make safe the way , put you on again the robe and hood . when I return and beckon , follow silently . " 

 the Prioress pass out , close the door behind she . 

 CHAPTER XIII 

 " SEND she to I ! " 

 the Prioress stand for a moment outside the closed door . the peaceful silence of the passage help she to the outward calm which must be her before she could bring herself to face her nun . 

 move slowly to the farth end , she unlock the cell of Sister Mary Seraphine , feel a sham humility that she should have make so sure she have to deal with " Wilfred , " and have think such scorn of he and Seraphine . alas ! the wrong deed of those they love , oft humble the pure , noble spirit into the soil dust . 

 next , the Prioress herself rang the Refectory bell . 

 the hour for the evening meal be long pass ; the nun hasten out , readily . 

 as they troop toward the stair lead down to the Refectory , they see their prioress , very pale , very erect , stand with she back to the door of her chamber . 

 each nun make a genuflexion as she pass ; and to each , the Prioress slightly incline her head .

 stand motionless at the top of the refectory step , she could hear the distant clatter of platter , the shuffle foot of the lay - sister as they carry the dish to and from the kitchen ; and , above it all , the monotonous voice of Sister Mary Rebecca read aloud to the nun while they sup . 

 then the Prioress take down one of the crypt lantern and light it . 

           

 meanwhile the Knight , leave alone , stand for a few moment , as if stun . 

 he have play for a big stake and lose ; yet he feel more unnerved by the unexpected finality of his own acquiescence in defeat , than by the firm refusal which have bring that defeat about . 

 it seem to he , as he now stand alone , that suddenly he have realise the extraordinary detachment work by year of cloistered life . Aflame with love and longing he have come , seek the living among the Dead . it would have be less bitter to have kneel beside her tomb , know the heart forever still have , to the last , beat true with love for he ; know the dead arm , lie cold and stiff , have he come soon , would have be fling around he ; know the lip , now silent in death , living , would have call to he in tender greeting . 

 but this cold travesty of the radiant woman he have leave , say : " touch I not , " and bid he seek a wife elsewhere ; he , who have remain faithful to she , even when he have think her faithless . 

 and yet , cold though she be , in her saintly aloofness , she be still the woman he love . moreover she still have the noble carriage , the rich womanly beauty , the look of vital , physical vigour , which mark she out as mean by Nature to be the mother of brave son and fair daughter . yet he must leave she to this ! 

 he look round the room , note the low archway lead to the sleep chamber , take a step toward it , then fall back as from a sanctuary ; mark the great table , cover with missal , parchment , and vellum . it might well have be the cell of a learn monk , rather than the chamber of the woman he love . his eye , travel round , fall upon the Madonna and Child . 

 in the pure evening light there be a strangely arrest quality about the marble group ; something infinitely human in the brood tenderness of the Mother , as she bend over the smile Babe . it speak of home , rather than of the cloister . it strike a chord in the heart of the Knight , a chord which ring clear and true , above the jangle of disputation and bitterness . 

 he put out his hand and touch the little foot of the Holy Babe . 

 " Mother of God , " he say aloud , ' send she to I ! take pity on a hungry heart , a lonely home , a desolate hearth . send she to I ! " 

 then he lift from the floor the white robe and hood , and draw they on . 

 CHAPTER XIV 

 farewell here , and now 

 when the prioress , a lighted lantern in her hand , open the door of her chamber , a tall figure in the dress of the White Ladies of Worcester stand motionless against the wall , face the door . 

 " come ! " she whisper , beckoning ; and , noiselessly , it stand beside she . then she close the door and , use her master - key , lock it behind she . 

 silently the two white figure pass along the passage , through the cloister , and down the flight of step into the Convent crypt . the Prioress unlock the door and stoop they pass under the arch , and enter the subterranean way . 

 place the lantern on the ground , the Prioress draw out the key , close the door , and lock it on the inside . 

 she turn , and lift the lantern , see that the Knight have rid himself of his disguise , and now stand before she , very straight and tall , just within the circle of light cast by her lantern . 

 with the closing and locking of the door a strange sense come over they , as of stand together in a third world neither his nor her tomblike in its complete isolation and darkness ; heavy with a smell of earth and damp stone ; the slight sound reverberate in hollow exaggeration ; yet , in itself , silent as the grave . 

 this tomblike quality in their surrounding seem to make their own vitality strong and more palpitating . 

 the second of silence , after the grating of the key in the lock cease , seem hour . 

 then the Knight speak . 

 " give I the lantern , " he say . 

 she meet his eye . again the dignity of her Office slip from she . 
 again it be sweet to obey . 
 he hold the lantern so that its light illumine her face and his . 

 " Mora , " he say , " it be long since thou and I last walk together over the sunny field , amid buttercup and cowslip , and the sweet - smell clover . to - night we walk beneath the field instead of through they . we be under the grass , my sweet . I seem to stand beside thee in the grave . and truly my hope lie slain ; the promise of our love be dead , and shall soon be bury . yet thou and I still live , and now must walk together side by side , the sad ghost of our former self . 

 " so now I ask thee , Mora , for the sake of those past walk among the flower , to lay thy hand within my arm and walk with I in gentle fellowship , here in this place of gloom and darkness , as , long ago , we walk among the flower . " 

 his dark eye search her face . an almost youthful eagerness vibrate in his voice . 

 she hesitate , lift her eye to his . then slowly move toward he and lay her hand within his arm . 

 then , side by side , they pace on through the darkness ; he , in his right hand , hold the lantern , swing low , to light their foot ; she , lean on his left arm , keep slow pace with he . 

 over their head , in the meadow , walk lover , arm in arm ; young man and maiden out in the gathering twilight . all nature , refresh , pour forth a fragrant sweetness . but the rose , with its dewy petal , seem to the youth less sweet than the lip of the maid . this , he shyly venture to tell she ; whereupon , as she bend to its fragrance , her cheek reflect the crimson of those delicate fold . 

 so walk and talk young lover in the Worcester meadow ; little dream that , beneath their happy foot , the Knight and the prioress pace slowly , side by side , through the darkness . 

 no word pass between they . with , her hand upon his arm , her face so near his shoulder , his arm press her hand close and close against his heart , silence say more than speech . and in silence they walk . 

 they pass beneath the city wall , under the Foregate . 

 the Sheriff ride home to supper , well pleased with a stroke of business accomplish in a house in which he have chance to shelter during the storm . 

 the good people of Worcester buy and sell in the market . man whose day 's work be over , hasten to reach the rest and comfort of wife and home . crowd jostle gaily through the street , little dream that beneath their hurrying , busy foot , the Knight and the prioress pace slowly , side by side , through the darkness . 

 have the Knight speak , her mind would have be up in arm to resist he . but , because he walk in silence , her heart have leisure to remember ; and , remembering , it grow sorely tender . 

 at length they reach the doorway lead into the Cathedral crypt . 

 the Prioress carry the key in her left hand . free she right from the grip of his arm , she slip the key noiselessly into the lock ; but , leave it there unturned , she pause , and face the Knight . 

 " Hugh , " she say , " I beg you , for my sake and for the sake of all whose fair fame be under my care , to pass through quickly into the crypt , and to go from thence , if possible , unseen , or in such manner as shall prevent any suspicion that you come from out this hide way . tale of wrong be tell so readily , and so quickly grow . " 

 " I will observe the utmost caution , " say the Knight . 

 " Hugh , " she say , " I grieve to have have , perforce , to disappoint you . " the brave voice shake . " this be our final farewell . do you forgive I , Hugh ? will you think kindly , if you ever think on I ? " 

 the Knight hold the lantern so that its ray illumine both her face and his . 

 " Mora , " he say , " I can not as yet take thine answer as final . I will return no more , nor try to speak with thee again . but five day long , I shall wait . Nay , speak not ! hear I out . 

 " Daily , after vesper , I shall stand hide among the pillar , close to the wind stair . one step aside only one step and my arm will be around thee . a new life of love and home will lie before we .  he swing the lantern high . she see the lovelight and the triumph , in his eye . " I shall take thee home ! " he say .

 " our last farewell ? " he say . 

 " our last . " 

 " here and now ? " 

 " here and now , dear Hugh . " 

 look into that calm face , so lovely in its sadness , he see that she mean it . 

 of a sudden he know he have lose she ; he know life 's way stretch lonely before he , evermore . 

 " yes , " he say , " yes . it be indeed farewell here and now forever . " 

 the dull despair in the voice which , but a few moment before , have vibrate with love and hope , wring her heart . 

 she still hold her hand before she , as if to ward he off . 

 " ah , Hugh , " she cry , sharply , " be merciful , and go ! spare I , and go quickly . " 

 the Knight hear in her voice a tone it have not hitherto hold . but he love she loyally ; therefore he keep his own anguish under strong control .

 with which he lift the hem of her robe , and press his lip upon it .

 long they stand thus . in that embrace a life - time of pain pass from they , a life - time of bliss be bear , and come with a rush to maturity , bring with it a sense of utter completeness . a world of sweetest trust and certainty fill they ; a joy so perfect , that the lonely vista of future year seem , in that moment , to matter not at all . 

 all about they be darkness , silence as of the tomb ; the heavy smell of earth ; the dank chill of the grave . 

 yet theirs be life more abundant ; theirs , joy undreame of ; theirs , love beyond all imagining , while those moment last . 

 then 

 the hand about his neck loosened , unclasped , fall gently away . 

 he set free her lip , and they take their liberty .

 then the Prioress turn the key in the lock .

 it be farewell , here and now ; farewell forever .

 CHAPTER XV 

 " SHARPEN the wit of MARY ANTONY " 

 when the prioress start upon her pilgrimage to the Cathedral with the Knight , she lock the door of her chamber , know that thus her absence would remain undiscovered ; for if any , knock on the door , receive no answer , or try it , find it fast , they would hasten away without question ; conclude that some special hour of devotion or time of study demand that the Reverend Mother should be free from intrusion . 

 the atmosphere of the empty cell , charge during the past hour with such unaccustomed force of conflict and of passion , settle into the quietude of an unbroken stillness . 

 the Madonna smile serenely upon the Holy Babe . the dead Christ , with bow head , hang forlorn upon the wooden cross . the ponderous volume in black and silver binding , lie undisturbed upon the table ; and the Bishop 's chair stand empty , with that obtrusive emptiness which , in an empty seat , seem to suggest an unseen presence fill it . the silence be complete . 

 but presently a queer shuffle sound begin in the inner cell , as of something stiff and torpid compelling itself to action .

 CHAPTER XVI 

 the echo of wild voices 

 when the prioress enter her cell , she stand for a moment bewilder by the rapid walk in the darkness . she could hardly realise that the long strain be over ; that she have safely regain her chamber . 

 all be as she have leave it . apparently she have not be miss , and have return unobserved . Hugh be by now safely in the hostel at Worcester . none need ever know that he have be here . 

 none need ever know yet , alas , it be that knowledge which hold the 
 Prioress root to the spot on which she stand , gaze round her cell . 
 Hugh have be here ; and when he be here , her one desire have be to get he speedily away . 

 but now ? 

 dumb with the pain of a great yearning , she look about she . 

 yes ; just there he have stand ; here he have kneel , and there he have stand again . 

 this calm monastic air have vibrate to the fervour of his voice . 

 it have grow calm again . 

 would her poor heart in time also grow calm ? would her lip stop tremble , and cease to feel the fire of his ? 

 yet for one moment , only , her mind dwelt upon herself . then all thought of self be merge in the realisation of his loneliness , his suffering , his bitter disillusion . to have find she dead , would have be hard ; to have lose her living , be almost past bearing . would it cost he his faith in God , in truth , in purity , in honour ? 

 the Prioress feel the insistent need of prayer . but pass the gracious image of the Virgin and Child , she cast herself down at the foot of the crucifix . 

 she have see a strong man in agony , nail , by the cruel iron of circumstance , to the cross - beam of sacrifice and surrender . to the suffering Saviour she turn , instinctively , for help and consolation . 

 thus speedily have her prayer of the previous night be grant . the pierce foot of our dear Lord , crucify , have become more to she than the baby foot of the Infant Jesus , on his mother 's knee . 

 yet , even as she kneel supplicate , interceding , adore there echo in her memory the wicked shriek of Mary Seraphine : " a dead God can not help I ! I want life , not death ! " follow almost instantly by Hugh 's stern question : " be this religion ? " 

 truly , of late , wild voice have take liberty of speech in the cell of the prioress , and have leave their impious utterance echo behind they . 

 CHAPTER XVII 

 the dimness of MARY ANTONY 

 the Prioress have be back in her cell for nearly an hour , when a gentle tap come on the door . 

 " Enter , " command the prioress , and Mary Antony appear , bear broth and bread , fruit and a cup of wine . 

 the Prioress sit at her table , parchment and an open missal before she . 
 her face be very white ; also there be dark shadow beneath her eye . 
 she do not smile at sight of old Antony , thus laden . 
 " how now , Antony ? " she say , almost sternly . " I do not bid thee to bring I food . " 

 " Reverend Mother , " say the old lay - sister , in a voice which strove to be steady , yet quaver ; " for long hour you have study , not heed that the evening meal be over . Chide not old Antony for bring you some of that broth , which you like the good . you will not sleep unless you eat . " 

 the Prioress look at her uncomprehendingly ; as if , for the moment , word convey no meaning to her mind . then she see those old hand tremble , and a sudden flood of colour flush the pallor of her face . 

 this sweet stirring of fresh life within her own heart give she to see , in the old woman 's untiring devotion , a human element hitherto unperceive . it bring a rush of comfort , in her sadness . 

 she close the volume , and push aside the parchment . " how kind of thee , dear Antony , to take so much thought for I . place the bowl on the table . . . . now draw up that stool , and stay near I while I sup . I be weary this night , and shall like thy company . " 

 have the golden gate of heaven open before she , and Saint Peter himself invite she to enter , Sister Mary Antony would not have be more astonished and certainly could hardly have be more gratified . it be a thing undreame of , that she should be bid to sit with the Reverend Mother in her cell . 

 draw the carven stool two foot from the wall , Mary Antony take her seat upon it . 

 " Nearer , Antony , nearer , " say the Prioress . " place the stool here , close beside the corner of my table . I have much to say to thee , and would wish to speak low . " 

 truly Sister Antony find herself in the seventh heaven ! 

 yet , quietly observe , the prioress could not fail to note the draw weariness on the old face , the yellow pallor of the wizen skin , which usually wear the bright tint of a russet apple . 

 the Prioress take a portion of the broth ; then push the bowl from she , and turn to the fruit . 

 " there , Antony , " she say . " the broth be excellent ; but I have enough . 
 finish it thyself . it will pleasure I to see thee enjoy it . " 
 faint and thankful , old Antony seize the bowl . and as she drink the broth , her shrewd eye twinkle . for have not the Devil say she would sup on it herself ; know that much , yet not know that she would receive it from the hand of the Reverend Mother ? 

 it have be ever so , from Eden onwards , when the Devil try his hand at prophecy . 

 for a while the prioress talk lightly , of flower and bird ; of the garden and the orchard ; of the gift of three fine salmon , send to they by the good monk of the Priory at Worcester . 

 but , presently , when the broth be finish and a faint colour tint the old cheek , she pass on to the storm and the sunset , the rolling thunder and the torrent of rain . then of a sudden she say : 

 " by the way , Antony , hast thou make mention , to any , of thy fearsome tale of the walking through the cloister , in line with the White Ladies , of the Spectre of the saintly Sister Agatha ? " 

 " Nay , Reverend Mother , " say Mary Antony . " do not you forbid I to speak of it ? " 

 " true , " say the prioress . " well , Antony , I go in the storm , to look for she ; but I find not Sister Agatha . " 

 " that I already know , " say Mary Antony , nod her head sagaciously . 

 the Prioress cast upon she a quick , anxious look . 

 " what mean you , Antony ? " 

 then old Mary Antony fall upon her knee , and kiss the hem of the prioress 's robe . " oh , Reverend Mother , " she stammer , " I have a confession to make ! " 

 " make it , " say the Prioress , with white lip . 

 " Reverend Mother , when you send I from you , after make my report , I go first , as command , to the kitchen . but afterward , in my cell , I find these . " 

 Mary Antony open her wallet and draw out the linen bag in which she keep her pea . shake its content into the palm of her hand , she hold out six pea to view . 

 " Reverend Mother , " she say , " there be twenty - five in the bag . I think I have count twenty out into my hand ; so when all the pea have drop and yet another holy Lady pass , I think that make twenty - one . but when I find six pea in my bag , I become aware of my folly . I have but count nineteen , and have no pea to let fall for the twentieth holy Lady . yet I run in haste with my false report , when , have I but think to look in my wallet , all would have be make clear . will the Reverend Mother forgive old Mary Antony ? " 

 she shoot a quick glance at the prioress ; and , at sight of the immense relief on that love face , feel ready for any punishment with which it might please Heaven to visit her deceit . 

 " Dear Antony , " begin the Reverend Mother , smile . 

 " Dear Antony " she say , and laugh aloud . 

 then she place her hand beneath the old woman 's arm , and gently raise she . " mistake arise so easily , " she say . " with the good of intention , we all sometimes make mistake . there be nothing to forgive , my Antony . " 

 " I be old , and dim , and stupid , " say the lay - sister , humbly ; " but I have beg of our sweet Lady to sharpen the old wit of Mary Antony . " 

 after which statement , make in a voice of humble penitence , Mary Antony , unseen by the thankful prioress , do give a knowing wink with the eye next to the Madonna . our blessed Lady smile . the sweet Babe look merry . the prioress rise , a great light of relief illumine her weary face . 

 " let we to bed , dear Antony ; then , with the dawn of a new day we shall all arise with heart refresh and wit more keen . so now God rest thee . " 

 leave alone , the Prioress kneel long in prayer before the shrine of the 
 Madonna . once , she reach out her right hand to the empty space where 
 Hugh have kneel , strive to feel remembrance of his strong clasp . 
 at length she seek her couch . but sleep refuse to come , and presently she creep back in the white moonlight , and kneeling press her lip to the stone on which Hugh have kneel ; then flee , in shame that our Lady should see such weakness ; and dare not glance toward the shadowy form of the dead Christ , crucify . for with the coming of Love to seek she , Life have come ; and where Life enter , death be put to flight ; even as before the triumphant march of the rise sun , darkness and shadow flee away . 

 yet , even then , our Lady gently smile , and the Babe on her knee look merry . 

 CHAPTER xviii 

 in the CATHEDRAL CRYPT 

 on the day follow , in the afternoon , shortly before the hour of Vespers , a stretcher be carry through the street of Worcester , by four man - at - arm wear the livery of Sir Hugh d'Argent . 

 beside it walk the Knight , with bent head , his eye upon the ground . 

 the body of the man upon the stretcher be cover by a fine linen sheet , over which lie a blue cloak , richly embroider with silver . his head be swathe in a bandage of many fold , partially conceal the face . 

 the little procession pass through the Precincts ; then enter the 
 Cathedral by the great door lead into the nave . 
 here a monk stand , take careful note of all who pass in or out of the building . as the stretcher approach , he step forward with hand upraise . 

 there be a pause in the measured tramp of the bearer ' foot . 

 the Knight lift his eye , and see the monk bar the way , he draw forth a parchment and tender it . 

 " I have the leave of the Lord Bishop , good father , " he say , " to carry this man upon the stretcher daily into the crypt , and there to let he lie before the shrine of Saint Oswald , during the hour of Vespers ; from which daily pilgrimage and prayer , we hope a great recovery and restoration . " 

 at sight of the Lord Bishop 's signature and seal , the monk make deep obeisance , and hasten to call the Sacristan , bid he attend the Knight on his passage to the crypt and give he every facility in place the sick man there where he might most conveniently lie before the holy altar of the bless Saint Oswald . 

 so presently , the stretcher be safely deposit , the man - at - arm stand each against a pillar , and the Knight fold back the covering , in order that the man who lie beneath , might have sight of the altar and the shrine . 

 as the Knight stand gaze through the vista of many column , he find the old Sacristan stand at his elbow . 

 " most worshipful Knight , " say the old man , with deference , " our Lord Bishop 's mandate supersede all rule . be it not so , it would be my duty to clear the crypt before vesper . see you that stairway yonder , beneath the arch ? not many minute hence , up those step will pass the holy nun from the Convent of the White Ladies at Whytstone noble lady all , and of great repute for saintliness . daily they come to Vespers by a secret way ; enter the crypt , they pass across to a wind stair in the wall , and so arrive at a gallery above the choir , from which they can , unseen , hear the chanting of the monk . I must to my duty above . will you undertake , Sir Knight , that your man go not nigh where the White Ladies pass , nor in any way molest they ? " 

 " none shall stir hand or foot , as they pass , nor in any way molest they , " say the Knight . 

 Hugh d'Argent be kneel before the altar , his fold hand rest upon the cross on the hilt of his sword , when the faint sound of a key turning in a distant lock , catch his ear . 

 then up the step and across the crypt pass , in silent procession , the White Ladies of Worcester . 

 there be something ghostly and awe - inspire about those veil figure , move noiselessly among the pillar in the dimly - light crypt ; then vanish , one by one , up the wind stairway in the wall . 

 the Knight do not stir . he stay upon his knee , his hand clasp upon his sword - hilt ; but he follow each silent figure with his eye . 

 the last have barely disappear from view when , from above , come the solemn chant of monk and chorister . 

 this harmony , descend from above , seem to uplift the soul all the more readily , because the sacred word and noble sound reach the listener , unhampere by association with the personality , either youthful or ponderous , of the singer . all that be of the earth remain unseen ; while that which be so near akin to heaven , enter the listening ear . 

 Kneeling in lowly reverence with bow head , the Knight find himself wonder whether the ascending sound reach that distant gallery in the clerestory where the White Ladies knelt , as greatly soften , sweeten , and enrich , as they now come steal down into the crypt . be the heart of those veil worshipper also lift heavenward ; or be already above the music do the ascend voice rather tend to draw they down to earth ? 

 upon which the Knight fall to meditating as to whether that which be high always uplift ; whereas that which be low tend to debase . certainly the upward look betoken hope and joy ; while the downward casting of the eye , be sign of sorrow and despondency . 

 " Levavi oculo meo in monte " chant the monk , in the choir above . 

 he certainly look high when he lift the eye of his insistent desire to the Prioress of the White Ladies . so high do he lift they , and so unattainable be she , that most man would say he might as well ask the silvery moon , sail across the firmament , to come down and be his bride ! 

 he have hold her high , in her maiden loveliness and purity . but now that he have find she , a noble woman , mature , ripen by sorrow rather than harden , yet firm in her determination to die to the world , to deny self , crucify the flesh , and resist the Devil he feel indeed that she walk among the star . 

 yet he could not bring himself to regard she as unattainable . it have ever be his firm belief that a man could win any woman upon whom he wholly set his heart always suppose that no other man have already win she . and this woman have be his own betrothed , when treachery intervene and sunder they . yet that do not now count for much . 

 he have leave a girl ; he have come back to find a woman . that woman have infinitely more to give ; but it would be infinitely more difficult to persuade she to give it . 

 at the close of their interview in her cell , the day before , all hope have leave he . but later , as they pace together in the darkness , hope have revive . 

 the strange isolation in which they then find themselves between locked door a mile apart , earth above , earth beneath , earth all around they , they two alone , entomb yet vividly conscious of glow life have bring she nearer to he ; and when at last the moment of parting arrive and again he face it as final , there have come all unheralded the sudden wonder of her surrender . 

 true , she have afterwards withdraw herself ; true , she have send he from she ; true , he have go , without a word . but that be because no promise could have be so binding , as that silent embrace . 

 he have go from she on the impulse of the sweetness of obey instantly her slight wish ; buoy up by the certainty that no convent wall could long divide lip which have meet and clung with such a passion of mutual need . 

 that evening when , after much adventure , he at length gain the street of the city , he have tread they with the mien of a victor . 

 that night he have sleep as he have not sleep since the hour when his whole life have be embitter by a lie letter and a traitorous tongue .

 yet he carry out his plan , and keep to his undertaking , though here , in the calm atmosphere of the crypt , holy chanting descend from above , the remembrance still with he of the aloofness of those stately white figure glide between the pillar in the distance , he face the madness of his hope , and the mournful prospect of a life of loneliness . 

 presently he arise , cross the crypt , and take up his position behind a pillar to the right of the exit from the wind stair . 

 the chanting cease . vesper be over . 

 he hear the sound of soft footstep draw nearer . 

 the White Ladies be come . 

 they come . 

 the Knight be not keep long in suspense . the prioress walk first . her face be hide , but her height and carriage reveal she to her lover . she look neither to right nor leave but , turn away from the pillar behind which the Knight stand conceal , cross to the step lead down to the subterranean way , and so pass swiftly out of sight .

 one , tall but ungainly , crook of body , and doubtless short of vision , miss her way among the column and pass perilously near to the Knight . with his long arm , he could have clasp she . how old Antony would have chuckle , could she but have know ! " Sister Mary Rebecca embrace by the Knight of the Bloody Vest ? Nay then ; the saint forbid ! " 

 the stretcher , bear by four man - at - arm , pass out from the Cathedral . 

 the Knight walk beside it , with bent head , and eye upon the ground .

 CHAPTER XIX 

 the BISHOP put on his biretta 

 Symon , Lord Bishop of Worcester , have receive a letter from the Prioress of the White Ladies , pray he for an interview at his leisure , send back at once a most courtly and gracious answer , that he would that same day give himself the pleasure of visit the Reverend Mother , at the Nunnery , an hour after vesper . 

 the great gate be throw open , and the Bishop ride his palfrey into the courtyard . 

 the Prioress herself meet he at the door and , kneeling , kiss his ring ; then lead he through the low hall , where the nun kneel to receive his blessing , and up the wide staircase , to the privacy of her own cell . 

 there she presently unfold to he the history of her difficulty with that wayward little nun , Sister Mary Seraphine . 

 " but the point which I chiefly desire to lay before you , Reverend Father , " conclude the prioress , " be this : if the neighing of a palfrey call more loudly to she than the voice of God ; if her mind be still set upon the thing of the world ; if she profess without a true vocation , merely because she wish to be the central figure of a great ceremony , yet be all the while expect a man to intervene and carry she off ; if all this bespeak her true state of heart , then to my mind there come the question : be she do good , either to herself or to other , by belong to our order ? would she not be well away ? 

 " my lord , I fear I greatly shock you by name such a possibility . but truly I be pursue by the remembrance of that young thing , beat the floor with her hand , and sing a mournful dirge about the crimson trapping of her palfrey . and , alas ! when I reason with she and exhort , she break out , as I have tell you , Reverend Father , into grievous blasphemy for which she be severely deal with by Mother Sub - Prioress , and have since be outwardly amenable to rule and discipline . 

 " but , though she may outwardly conform , how about her inward state ? well I know that our vow be lifelong vow ; all who belong to our order be wed to Heaven ; we be thankful to know that the calm of the Cloister shall be exchange only for the great peace of Paradise . but , suppose a young heart have mistake its vocation ; suppose the voice of an earthly lover call when it be too late ; would it seem right or possible to you , Reverend Father , to grant any sort of absolution from the vow ; tacitly to allow the opening of the cage door , that the little foolish bird might , if it wish , escape into the liberty for which it chafe and sigh ? " 

 the Bishop sit in the spanish chair , draw up near the oriel window , so that he could either gaze at the glory of the distant sunset , or , by slightly turn his head , look on the beautiful but grave face of the prioress , seat before he . 

 while she be speak he watch she keenly , with those bright search eye , so much more youthful than aught else about he . but now that he must make reply , he look away to the sunset . 

 the light shine on the plain gold cross at his breast , and on the violet silk of his cassock . his face , against the background of the black spanish wood , look strangely white and thin ; strong in contour , with a virile strength ; in expression , sensitive as a woman 's . he have remove his biretta , and place it upon the table . his silvery hair roll back from his forehead in silky wave . his be the look of the saint and the scholar , almost of the mystic save for the tender humour in those keen blue eye , gleam like beacon light from beneath the level eyebrow ; eye which have win the confidence of many a man who else have not dare unfold his very human story , to one of such saintly aspect as Symon , Bishop of Worcester . they be turn toward the sunset , as he make answer to the prioress . 

 " the little foolish bird , " say the Bishop and he speak in that gently muse tone , which convey to the mind of the hearer a sense of infinite leisure in which to weigh and consider the subject in hand " the little foolish bird might soon wish herself back in the safety of the cage . on such as she , the cruel hawk of life do love to prey . absorb in the contemplation of her own charm , she see not , until too late , the danger which surround she . such little foolish bird , my daughter , be good in the safe shelter of the cloister . moreover , of what value be they in the world ? none . if Popinjays we d they , they do but hatch out brood of foolish little popinjays . if true man , catch by mere surface beauty , we d they , it can mean naught save heartbreak and sorrow , and deterioration of the race . woman of fine mould " for an instant the Bishop 's eye stray from the sunset " be need , to be the mother of the man who , in the year to come , be to make England great . Nay , rather than let one escape , I would shut up all the little foolish bird in a Nunnery , with our excellent Sub - prioress to administer necessary discipline . " 

 with his elbow rest upon the arm of the chair , the Bishop put his finger together , so that the tip meet most precisely ; then bent his lip to they , and look at the prioress . 

 she , troubled and sick at heart , lift deep pool of silent misery , meet the merry twinkle in the Bishop 's eye , and sit astonish . what be it like ? why it be like the song of a robin , perch on a frosty bough , on Christmas morning ! it be so young and gay ; so jocund , and so hopeful . 

 meet it , the Prioress realise fully , what she have many time half - divine , that the revered and reverend Prelate sit opposite , for all his robe and dignity , his panoply of Church and State , have the heart of a merry schoolboy out on a holiday . 

 for the moment she feel much old than the Bishop , infinitely sadder ; more travel - wear and worldly - wise . 

 then she look at the silver hair ; the firm mouth , with a shrewd curve at either corner ; the thoughtful brow . 

 and then she look at the Bishop 's ring . 

 the Bishop wear a remarkable ring ; not a signet , but a large gem of great value , beautifully cut in many facet , and clear set in massive gold . this precious stone , say to be a chrysoprasus , have be give to the Bishop by a russian prince , in acknowledgment of a great service render he when he come on pilgrimage to Rome . the rarity of these gem arise partly from the fact that the sovereign of Russia have decree that they should be hold exclusively for royal ornament , forbid their use or purchase by people of less degree . 

 but its beauty and its rarity be not the only quality of the precious stone in the Bishop 's ring . the strange thing about it be that its colour varied , accord to the Bishop 's mood and surrounding .

 the Prioress return to the subject , with studied seriousness . 

 " I do not suppose , Reverend Father , that it be to be of any advantage to the world , that Sister Seraphine should return to it . the advantage be to be to she , and also to this whole community , well rid of the presence of one who find our sacred exercise irksome ; our beautiful Nunnery , a prison ; her cell , a live tomb . she cry out for life . ' I want to live , ' she say , ' I be young , I be gay , I be beautiful ! I want life . ' " 

 " to such as Sister Seraphine , " remark the Bishop , gravely , " life be but a mirror which reflect themselves . other form and face may flit by , in the background ; dimly see , scarcely notice . there be but one face and form occupy the entire foreground . life be , to such , the mirror which minister to vanity . should a husband appear in the picture , he be soon relegate to the background , receive only occasional glance over the shoulder . if child dance into the field of vision , they be petulantly drive elsewhere . tell I ? do Sister Seraphine 's desire for life include any expression of the desire to give life ? " 

 involuntarily the prioress glance at the sweet Babe upon the Virgin 's knee . 

 " no , " she say , very low . 

 " I think not , " say the Bishop . " self - centre , shallow nature be not capable of the sublime passion for motherhood ; partly , no doubt , because they themselves possess no life worth pass on . " 

 the prioress rise quickly and , move to the window , fling open a second casement . it be imperative , at that moment , to hide her face ; for the uncontrollable flood of emotion at her heart , could scarce fail to send a tell - tale wave to disturb the calm of her countenance . 

 Whereupon the Bishop turn , to see at what the Prioress have glance before answer his question . 

 " no , " he muse , as she resume her seat , his eye upon the tree - top beyond the casement , " the Seraphines have not the instinct of motherhood . and the future greatness of our race depend upon those noble woman who be able to pass on to their son and daughter a life which be true , and brave , and worthy ; a life whose foundation be self - sacrifice , whose cornerstone be loyalty , and from whose summit wave the banner of unsullied love of hearth and home . 

 " a woman with the true instinct of motherhood can not see a little child without yearn to clasp it to her bosom . when she find her mate , she think more of be the mother of his child than the object of his devotion , because the self in she be subservient to the maternal instinct for self - sacrifice . these woman be pure as snow , and they hold their man to the high and the good . such woman be need in the world . our Lady knoweth , I speak not lightly , unadvisedly nor wantonly ; but be Seraphine such an one as this , I should say ; ' leave the door on the latch . without permission , yet without reproach let she go . ' " 

 " be Seraphine such an one as that , my lord , " say the prioress , firmly , " then would there be no question of her go . if the cornerstone of character be loyalty , the very essential of loyalty be the keeping of vow . " 

 " quite so , " murmur the Bishop ; " undoubtedly , my daughter . unless , by some strange fatality , those vow be make under a total misapprehension . you tell I Sister Seraphine expect a man to intervene ? " 

 the Bishop sit up , of a sudden keenly alert . his eye , no long humorous and tender , become search and bright young still , but with the fire of youth , rather than its merriment . as he lean forward in his chair , his hand grip his knee . look at his ring the prioress see the stone the colour of red wine .

 " a Knight arrive in this city , rather more than a month ago ; a very noble Knight , splendid to look upon ; one of our brave Crusaders . he arrive here in sore anguish of heart . his betrothed have be take from he during his absence from England , wag war against the Turks in Palestine take from he by a most dastardly and heartless plot . he make many inquiry concern this Nunnery and Order , ride north again on urgent business , but return , with a large retinue , five day since . "

 but the Bishop , now eagerly launch , have no interest in pallor , or possible palsy . his vigorous word cut the calm atmosphere . the gem on his finger sparkle like red wine in a goblet .

 the Prioress smile ; and truly it be a very creditable smile for a face which might have be carve in marble .

 " Nay , there I do not agree , " say the Bishop . " it be ever opposite which attract . the tall we d the short ; the stout , the lean ; the dark , the fair ; the grave , the gay . wherefore my stern Crusader may be break his heart for your foolish little bird . " 

 " I do not think so , " say the prioress , shortly ; then hasten to add : 
 " not that I would presume to differ from you , Reverend Father . 
 Doubtless you be well verse in such matter than i. but if it be 
 as you suppose what measure do you suggest ? how be I to deal with 
 Sister Mary Seraphine ? " 
 the Bishop lean forward and whisper , though not another soul be within hearing ; but at this juncture in the conversation , a whisper be both dramatic and effective . also , when he lean forward , he could almost hear the angry beating of the heart of the prioress . 

 the Bishop hold the Prioress in high regard , and love not to distress she . but he do not think it right that a woman should have such complete mastery over herself , and therefore over other . a fine quality in a man , may be a blemish in a woman . for which reason the Bishop lean forward and whisper . 

 " let she fly , my daughter ; let she fly . if his arm await she , she will not have far to go , nor many danger to face . her lover will know how to guard his own . "

 the prioress flash and quiver ; rise to her foot and tower ; fling her arm wide , and pace the floor .

 the Bishop put on his biretta .

 then , suddenly , the Prioress knelt at the foot of the Bishop .

" you be not angry with I , nor with the brave Crusader , nor with the foolish seraphine . your anger , all unconsciously , be arouse by a system , a method of life which be contrary to Nature , and therefore surely at variance with the will of God . I have long have my doubt concern these vow of perpetual celibacy for woman . for man , it be different . the creative power in a man , if deny their natural function , stir he to great enterprise , move he to beget fine phantasy , creation of his brain , child of his intellect . if he stamp not his image on brave son and fair daughter , he leave his mark on life in many other way , both brave and fair . but it be not so with woman ; in the very nature of thing it can not be . methink these nunnery would serve a well purpose be they school from which to send woman forth into the world to be good wife and mother , rather than store - house fill with sad sample of Nature 's great purpose deliberately unfulfilled .  Amazement be writ large than ever , on her face ; but she hold herself well under control . 

 " such view , my lord , if freely express and adopt , would change the entire monastic system . " 

 " I know it , " say the Bishop . " and I would not express they , save to you and to one other , to whom I also talk freely . but the old I grow , the more clearly do I see that system be man - make , and therefore often mistaken , injurious , pernicious . but nature be Divine . those who live in close touch with Nature , who rule their life by Nature 's rule , do not stray far from the divine plan of the Creator . but when man take upon himself to say ' thou shalt , ' or ' thou shalt not , ' quickly confusion enter . a false premise become the starting - point ; and the goal , if it stop short of perdition , be , at good , folly and failure . "

 " think you so , Reverend Father ? then what do you counsel I to do with Seraphine ? " 

 " speak to she gently , and with great care and prudence . say to her much of that which you have say to I , and a little of that which I have say to you , but express in such manner as will be suit to a foolish mind . you and I can hurl brick at one another , my dear prioress , and be the well for the exercise . but we must not fle at little Seraphine aught hard than a pillow of down . empty head , like empty eggshell , be soon break . tell she you have consult I concern her desire to return to the world ; and that I , be lenient , and hold somewhat wide view on this subject than the majority of prelate , also be well acquainted with the mind of his Holiness the Pope concern those who embrace the religious life for reason other than a true vocation , have promise to arrange the matter of a dispensation . but add that there must be no possibility of any scandal connect with the Nunnery . since the Lady Wulgeova , mother of Bishop Wulstan , of blessed memory , take the veil here a century and a half ago , this house have ever be above reproach . you will tacitly allow she to slip away ; and , once away , I will set matter right for she . but nothing must transpire which could stumble or scandalise the other member of the Community . the peculiar circumstance which the Knight make known to I always , of course , without make any mention of the name of Seraphine can hardly have occur in any other case . it be not likely , for instance , that our worthy Sub - Prioress be tear by treachery from the arm of a despairing lover ; and she would undoubtedly share your very limit idea of a lover 's physical quality and requirement ; possibly not even allow he a voice .

I ask of he what he expect would result from so do . he make answer : ' a great recovery and restoration . ' " 

 the Bishop pause , as if meditate upon the word . then he slowly repeat they , take evident pleasure in each syllable .

" 

 the Bishop stretch out his hand and take up his biretta . 

 " when do the nun last have a Play day ? " he ask . 

 " not a month ago , " reply the prioress . " they make the hay in the river meadow , and carry it themselves . they think it rare sport . "

 CHAPTER XX 

 HOLLY and MISTLETOE 

 Symon , Bishop of Worcester , have bid Sir Hugh d'Argent to sup with he at the Palace . 

 it be upon the second day after the Bishop 's conversation with the 
 Prioress in the Convent at Whytstone ; the evening of the Nun 's Play 
 Day , grant in honour of his visit . 
 the Bishop and the Knight sup together , with much stately ceremony , in the great banqueting hall . 

 know the Bishop 's love of the beautiful , and his habit of be punctilious in matter of array and deportment , acquire no doubt during his lengthy sojourn in France and Italy , the Knight have don his fine court suit white satin , embroider with silver ; jewel collar , belt , and shoe ; a small - sword of exquisite workmanship at his side . a white cloak , also richly embroider with silver , hang from his shoulder ; white silk hose set off the shapely length of his limb . the blood - red gleam of the magnificent ruby on his breast , sword - belt , and shoe - buckle , be the only point of colour in his attire . 

 the Bishop 's keen eye note with quiet pleasure how greatly this somewhat fantastically beautiful dress enhance the dark splendour of the Knight 's noble countenance , display his superb carriage , and shew off the supple grace of his limb , which , in his ordinary garb , rather give the idea of massive strength alone . 

 the Bishop himself wear crimson and gold ; and , just as the dark beauty of the Knight be enhance by the fair white and silver of his dress , so do these gorgeous italian robe set off the frail whiteness of the Bishop 's delicate face , the silvery softness of his abundant hair . and just as the collar of ruby gleam like fiery eye upon the Knight 's white satin doublet , so from out the pallor of the Prelate 's countenance the eye shine forth , bright with the fire of eternal , youth , the gay joy of life , the twinkle humour of a shrewd yet kindly wit . 

 they sup at a round table of small size , in the very centre of the huge apartment . it form a point of light and brightness from which all else merge into shadow , and yet deep shadow , until the eye reach the dark panelling of the wall . 

 the light seem to centre in the Knight white and silver ; the colour , in the figure of the Bishop crimson and gold . 

 in and out of the shadow , swift and silent , on sandalled foot , move the lay - brother serve the feast ; watchful of each detail ; quickly supply every need . 

 at length they load the table with fruit ; put upon it fresh flagon of wine , and finally withdraw ; each black - rob figure merge into the black shadow , and vanish in silence . 

 the Bishop 's Chaplain appear in a distant doorway . 

 " Benedicite , " say Symon of Worcester , look up . 

 " Deus , " reply the Chaplain , make a profound obeisance . 

 then he stand erect a grim , austere figure , hard feature , hollow eye , half - shroud within his cowl . 

 he look with sinister disapproval at the distant table , laden with fruit and flagon ; at the Bishop and the Knight , now sit nigh to one another ; the Bishop in his chair of state face the door , the Knight , on a high - back seat at the Bishop 's right hand , half - way round the table . 

 " Holly and Mistletoe , " mutter the Chaplain , as he close the great door . 

 " yea , verily ! Mistletoe and Holly , " he repeat , as he stride to his cell . " the Reverend Father sup with the World , and indulge the Flesh . methink the Devil can not be far off . " 

 nor be he . 

 he be very near . 

 he have look over the Chaplain 's shoulder as he make his false obeisance in the doorway . 

 but he like not the pure white of the Knight 's dress , and he fear the clear light in the Prelate 's eye . so , when the Chaplain close the door , the Devil stay on the outside , and now walk beside the Chaplain along the passage lead to his cell . 

 there be no surer way of secure the company of the Devil , than to make sure he be at that moment busy with another particularly if that other chance to be the most saintly man you know , and merely displease to you , at the moment , because he hath not bid you to sup with he . the Devil and the Chaplain make a night of it . 

 the Bishop 's gentle " Benedicite " spread white wing and fly , like an affrighted dove , over the head of the bow Chaplain , into the chill passage beyond . 

 but , just as the great door be close , it dart in again , circle round the banqueting hall , and come back to rest in the safe nest of the kindly heart which have send it forth . 

 no blessing , truly vitalise , ever cease to live . if the bless be unworthy , it return on swift wing to the blesser . 

 CHAPTER XXI 

 so MUCH for SERAPHINE ! 

 a sense of peace fall upon the banqueting hall , with the closing of the door . all unrest and suspicion seem to have depart . an atmosphere of confidence and serenity pervade the great chamber . it be in the Bishop 's smile , as he turn to the Knight . 

 " at length the time have come when we may talk freely ; and truly , my son , we have much to say . "

" 

 the Bishop , sign to the Knight to help himself to fruit , move the wine toward he . at his own right hand stand a venetian flagon and goblet of ruby glass , ornament with vine leaf and cluster of grape . the Bishop drink only from this flagon , pour its content himself into the goblet which he hold to the light before he drink from it , enjoy the rich glow of colour , and the beauty of the engraving . his guest sometimes wonder what specially choice kind of wine the Bishop keep for his own , exclusive use . if they ask , he tell they . 

 " the kind use at the marriage feast at Cana in Galilee , when the supply of an inferior quality have fail . this , my friend , be pure water , wholesome , refresh , and not costly .  " the gift of circumstance , life , and nature , vary , not so much in themselves , as in the human vessel which contain they . if the heart be a ruby goblet , the humble form of pure love fill it , will assume the rich tint and fervour of romance . if the mind be , in itself , a thing of vivid tint and glow colour , the dull thought within it will take on a lustre , a sparkle , a glow of brilliancy . thus , whensoever man or matter seem to I dull or wearisome , to myself I say : ' Symon ! Thou art this day , thyself , a pewter pot . ' " 

 then the Bishop would fill up his goblet and hold it to the light .

' the water of earth draw by faithful servant , act in unquestione obedience to the command of the blessed Mother of our Lord transmute by the word and power of the Divine Son ; outpoure for other , in love service ; this be ever ' the good wine .  this princely figure , with his crimson robe and golden cross , so visibly represent the power and authority of the Church .

 CHAPTER XXII 

 what BROTHER PHILIP had to tell 

 the Bishop sit back in his chair , smile , as at a mental picture which give he pleasure , couple with some amusement . 

 ignore the Knight 's sullen silence , he begin his story in the cheerful voice which take for grant a willing and an interested listener . 

 " when the Prioress and myself be discuss your hope , my son , and I be urge , in your interest , liberty of flight for Sister Mary Seraphine , I inform the Reverend Mother that the carrying out of your plan , carefully lay in order to keep any scandal concern the White Ladies from reach the city , would involve for Seraphine a ride of many hour to Warwick , almost immediately upon safely reach the Star hostel . this seem as nothing to the lover who , by his own shewing , have ofttime see she ' ride like a bird , all day , on the moor . ' but to we who know the effect of monastic life and how quickly such matter as these become lose art through disuse , this romantic ride in the late afternoon and on into the summer night , loom large as a possible obstacle to the successful flight of Seraphine . 

 " therefore , in order that our little bird might try her wing , regain her seat and mastery of a horse , and rid herself of a first painful stiffness , I persuade the Reverend Mother to grant the nun a Play day , in honour of my visit , promise to send they my white palfrey , suitably caparison , in safe charge of a good lay - brother , so that all nun who please , might ride in the river meadow . you would not think it , " say the Bishop , with a smile , " but the White Ladies dearly love such sport , when it be lawful . they have an aged ass which they gleefully mount in turn , on Play day , in the courtyard and in the meadow . therefore riding be not altogether strange to they , although my palfrey , Iconoklastes , be somewhat of an advance upon their mild ass , Sheba . " 

 the Knight 's sad face have brighten at mention of the beast . 

 " wherefore ' iconoklaste ' ? " he ask , with interest . it strike he as a curious name for a palfrey . 

 " because , " reply the Bishop , ' soon after I have buy he he trample to ruin , in a fit of misplaced merriment , some flower bed on which I have spend much precious time and care , and of which I be inordinately fond . " 

 " Brute , " say the Knight , puzzle , but unwilling to admit it . " methink I should have name he ' Devil , ' for the doing of such diabolic mischief . " 

 " Nay , " say the Bishop , gently . " the Devil would have spar my flower bed . they be a snare unto I . " 

 " and wherefore ' Sheba ' ? " query the Knight . 

 " I name she so , when I give she to the prioress , " say the Bishop , " in reply to a question put to I by the Reverend Mother . the ass be elderly and mild , even then , but a handsome creature , of good breed . the Prioress ask I whether she still have too much spirit to be easily manage by the lay - sister . I answer that her name be ' Sheba . ' " 

 the Bishop pause and rub his hand softly over each other , in gleeful enjoyment of the recollection . 

 but the Knight again look blank . 

 " do that content the prioress ? " he ask ; but chiefly for love of mention her name . 

 " perfectly , " reply the Bishop . " she smile and say : ' that be well . ' and the name stick to the ass , though the Reverend Mother and I alone understand its meaning . "

 " ah , yes ! about the Play Day . the time choose be after noon on this day , in order that the prioress might first accomplish her talk with Seraphine , thus clear the way for our experiment . although write last evening , I have not receive the Reverend Mother 's decisive letter , when iconoklaste set forth ; and , I confess , I look forward with keen interest , to question the lay - brother on his return . as I have tell you , I have doubt concern Seraphine ; but I know the Prioress would see to it that my meaning and intention reach the member of the Community actually concern , be she Seraphine or another ; and I should have light , both on the identity of the lady and on her probable course of action , when report reach I as to which of the nun have take the riding seriously . therefore , with no little interest , I await the return of Iconoklastes , in charge of Brother Philip . " 

 the Bishop lift the faggot - fork and , bend over the hearth , begin to build the log , quicken the die flame .

 " I pause , my son , that you might say : ' wherefore " Philip " ? ' " 

 " the name of man interest I not , " say the Knight , with impatience . 
 " I care but to know the reason for the name of beast . " 
 " quite right , " say the Bishop . " Adam name the beast ; Eve name the man . yet , I would like you to ask ' wherefore " Philip , " ' because the prioress at once put that question , when she hear I call Brother Mark by his new name . "

 " because ' Philip ' signifie ' a lover of horse . ' I name the good brother so , when he develop a great affection for all the steed in my stable .

 CHAPTER XXIII 

 the midnight ARRIVAL 

 Hugh d'Argent sit speechless , return the Bishop 's steady gaze . 

 no fear be in his face ; only a great surprise . 

 presently into the eye of both there creep a look which be half - smile , half - wistful sorrow , but wholly trustful ; a look to which , as yet , the Bishop alone hold the key . 

 " so you know , my lord , " say Hugh d'Argent . 

 " yes , my son ; I know . " 

 " since this morning ? " 

 " Nay , then ! since the first day you arrive with your story ; ask such careful question , carelessly . but be not wroth with yourself , Hugh . faithful to the hilt , have you be . only no true lover be ever a diplomat ! matter which mean more than life , can not be dissemble by true heart from keen eye . "

 " peace , lad ! Fash not thyself over it . be it not a part of my sacred office to follow in the footstep of my Master and to be a discerner of the thought and intent of the heart ? also , respect , yea , approve your reason for reticence , I would have let you depart not suspect my knowledge of that which you wish to conceal , be it not that we must now face this fact together : since pen that message of apparent finality , the Prioress have try her wing . " 

 a rush of bewildered joy flood the face of the Knight .

 Symon of Worcester consider this question carefully , sit in his favourite attitude , his lip compress against his finger - tip . 

 at length ; " I think it mean just this , " he say . " a conflict , in she , between the mental and the physical ; between reason and instinct ; thought and feeling . the calm , collected mind send you that reason message of final refusal . the sentient body , vibrant with bound life , instinctively prepare itself for the possibility of the ride with you to Warwick . this give equal balance to the scale . but a third factor will be call in , finally to decide the matter . by that she will abide ; and neither you nor I , neither earth nor hell , neither thing past , thing present , nor thing to come , could avail to move she . "

 " with that , there come over the Knight a sudden sense of compunction . 
 he begin for the first time to see the matter as it must appear to the 
 Bishop and the nun . his own obstinate and determine self - seeking 
 sham he .

 " that I should have seek , and should still be seek , to tempt the 
 Prioress to wrong - doing . " 
 the Bishop 's questioning gaze take on a brightness which almost become the light of sublime contempt . 

 " you tempt she ? " he say . " tempt she to wrong - doing ! the man live not , who could succeed in that ! she will not come to you unless she know it to be right to come , and believe it to be wrong to stay . if I think you be tempt she , think you I would stand aside and watch the conflict ? Nay ! but I stand aside and wait while she of purer , clear vision , and walk near Heaven than you or I discern the right , and , choose it , reject the wrong . should she be satisfied that life with you be indeed God 's will for she and I tell you honestly , it will take a miracle to bring this about she will come to you . but she will not come to you unless , in so do , she be choose what to she be the hard part . " 

 " the hard part ! " exclaim the Knight . " you forget , my lord , she love I . " 

 " do I forget ? " reply the Bishop . " have you find I give to forget ? the very fact that she love you , be the heavy factor against you just now . to such woman there come ever the instinctive feeling , that that which would be sweet must be wrong , and the hard path of renunciation the only right one . they climb not Zion 's mount to reach the crown . they turn and wend their way through Gethsemane to Calvary , sure that thus alone can they at last inherit . and what can we say ? be they not follow in the footstep of the Son of God ? I fear my nature turn another way . I incline to follow King David , or Solomon in all his glory , chant glad Songs of Ascent , from the Palace on Mount Zion to the Temple on Mount Moriah . all thing harmonious , in sound , form , or colour , seem to I good and , therefore , right . but long year in Italy have soak I in the worship of the beautiful , inextricably intermingle with the adoration of the Divine . I mistrust mine own judgment , and I fear I " say the Prelate , whose gentle charity have win so many to religion " I greatly fear I , I be far from be christlike . but I recognise the spirit of self - crucifixion , when I see it . and the warning that I give you , be not because I forget , but because I remember . "

 they come .

" 

 the Bishop smile as he look into the blue eye and open countenance of young Roger de Berchelai , a youth wholly devoted to his service . here be another who remember in picture , and Symon of Worcester love the gallop , and rush , and breeze of the sea , which have sweep through the chamber , in the eager young voice of his envoy .

" you have return , not merely in time , but with two day to spare . be there ever fleeter messenger ! indeed my choice be well make and my trust well place . now you must sup and then take a much - need rest , dear lad ; and to - morrow tell I if you have need to spend more than I give you . I shall not need your presence nor that of any of the brother , save those whose watch it chance to be . . . . Benedicite . "

 the brown riding - suit vanish through the archway .

 CHAPTER XXIV 

 the POPE 'S MANDATE 

 the Bishop and Hugh d'Argent be once more alone . it be characteristic of both that they sit for some minute in unbroken silence . 

 then the Bishop put out his hand , take up the packet from Rome , and look at the Knight .

 he could hear the Bishop break the seal of the Pope 's letter . 

 below in the courtyard , all be quiet . the great gate be bar . he wonder whether the steam horse have be well rub down , clothe , and give a warm mash mix with ale .

 the Palace stand on the same side of the Cathedral as the main street of the city , in the direct route to the Foregate , the Tithing , and the White Ladies ' Nunnery at Whytstone . how strange to remember , that beneath he lie that mile - long walk in darkness ; that just under the Palace , so near the Cathedral , she and he , pace together , have know the end of their strange pilgrimage to be at hand . yet then

 furthermore the deed empower Symon , Bishop of Worcester or any priest he might appoint , to unite in marriage the Knight Crusader , Hugh d'Argent , and Mora de Norelle , sometime prioress of the White Ladies of Worcester . 

 the Knight walk back to the hearth and stand before the Bishop , the parchment in his hand .

" Nay , my son . surely no dream of thine be ever sign by his Holiness , nor bore suspend from it the great seal of the Vatican ! the document you hold will be sufficient answer to all question , and will ensure your wife 's position at Court and her stand in the outer world should she elect to re - enter it . 

 " but whether she shall do this , or no , be not a matter upon which the Church would give a decisive or even an authoritative pronouncement ; and the Holy Father add , in , his letter to I , far important instruction . 

 " firstly : that it must be the Prioress 's own wish and decision , apart from any undue pressure from without , to resign her office and to accept this dispensation , free she from her vow .

 the Bishop 's lip be press against his finger - tip .

" good heaven , man ! dare I we d you to a woman you know so little ? not for one instant , into her consideration of the matter , will have enter any question as to what Church or State might say or do . for she the question stand upon simple , truer , line , not involve by rule or dogma : ' be it right for I , or wrong for I ? be it the will of God that I should do this thing ?  " what will she then say ? " Symon of Worcester softly laugh , as at something which stir an exceeding tender memory . " she will probably say : ' you amaze I , my lord ! indeed , my lord , you amaze I ! his Holiness the Pope may rule at Rome ; you , my Lord Bishop , rule in the city of this diocese ; but I rule in this Nunnery , and while I rule here , such a thing as this shall never be ! ' " 

 the Bishop gently pass his hand the one over the other , as be his habit when a recollection give he keen mental pleasure .

" 

 " my lord , " say the Knight , with much earnestness , " how come that full knowledge to his Holiness in Rome ? "
