I know the Holy Father well ; his openness of mind , his charity and kindliness ; his firm desire to do justly , and to love mercy . moreover , his friendship for I be such , that he would not lightly refuse I a request . also he would , of his kindness , incline to be guide by my judgment . 

 " wherefore , no soon be all the fact in my possession , those you tell I , those I already know , and those I do for myself deduce from both , than I send for young Roger de Berchelai , whose wit and devotion I could safely trust , give he all he would need for board and lodging , boat and steed , that he might accomplish the journey in the short possible time , and despatch he to Rome with a write account of the whole matter , under my private seal , to his Holiness the Pope . " 

 the Knight stand during this recital , his eye fix in search question upon the Bishop 's face . 

 then : " my lord , " he say , ' such kindness on your part , pass all understanding . that you should have bear with I while I tell my tale , be much . that you should tacitly have allow I the chance to have speech with my betrothed , be more . but that , all this time , while I be give you half - confidence , and she no confidence at all , you should have be work , spending , plan for we , risk much if the Holy Father have take your largeness of heart and breadth of mind amiss ! all this , you do , for Mora and for I ! that you be , as you tell I , a frequent guest in my childhood 's home , hold my parent in warm esteem , might account for the exceed kindness of the welcome you do give I . but this generosity this wondrous goodness I stand amazed , confound ! that you should do so great a thing to make it possible that I should we d the Prioress it pass understanding ! " 

 when Hugh d'Argent cease speaking , Symon of Worcester do not immediately make reply . he sit look into the fire , fingering , with his left hand , the gold cross at his breast , and drumming , with the finger of his right , upon the carve lion 's head which form the arm of his chair . 

 it seem as if the Bishop have , of a sudden , grow restive under the Knight 's gratitude ; or as if some train of thought have awaken within he , to which he do not choose to give expression , and which must be beat back before he allow himself to speak . 

 at length , fold his hand , he make answer to the Knight , still look into the fire , a certain air of detachment wrap he round , as with an invisible yet impenetrable shield . 

 " you overwhelm I , my dear Hugh , with your gratitude . it have not seem to I that my action in this matter would demand either thank or explanation . there be occasion when to do less than our good , would be to sin against all that which we hold most sacred . to my mind , the most useful definition of sin , in the sacred writing , be that of the apostle Saint James , most practical of all the inspire writer , when he say : ' to he that knoweth to do good , and doeth it not , to he it be sin . ' I know quite clearly the ' good ' to be do in this case . therefore no gratitude be due to I for fail to fall into the sin of omission . 

 " also , my son , many who seem to deserve the gratitude of other , would be find not to deserve it , if the entire inward truth of motive could be fully reveal . 

 " with I it be well - nigh a passion that all good thing should attain unto full completeness . 

 " it may be I be well able to give full understanding to your tale because , for love of a woman , I dwell seven year in exile from this land , fear lest my great love for she , which come to I all unsought , should by become know to her lead her young heart , as yet fresh and unawakened , to respond . there be never any question of break my vow ; and I hold not with love - friendship between man and woman , there where marriage be not possible . they be , at good , selfish on the part of the man . they keep the woman from enter into her kingdom . the crown of womanhood be to bear child to the man she love to take her place in his home , as wife and mother . the man who can not offer this , yet stand in the way of the man who can , be a poor and an unworthy lover . " 

 the Bishop pause , unclasp his hand , withdraw his steadfast regard from the fire , and sit back in his chair . the stone in his ring gleam blue , the colour of forget - I - not beside a meadow brook . 

 presently he look at the silent Knight . there be a kindly smile , in his eye , rather than upon his lip . 

 " it may be , my dear Hugh , that this heart discipline of mine of which , by the way , I have never before speak have make I quick to understand the suffering of other man . also it may explain the great desire I always experience to see a truly noble woman come to the full completion of her womanhood . 

 " I return to England not long after your betrothed have enter the cloister life in the Whytstone Nunnery . I be appoint to this see of Worcester , which appointment give I the spiritual control of the White Ladies . my friendship with the Prioress have be a source of interest , pleasure , and true helpfulness to myself and I trust to she also . I think I tell you while we sup that , many year ago , I have know she at the Court when I be confessor to the Queen , and preceptor to her lady . but no mention have ever be make between the Prioress and myself of any previous acquaintance . I doubt whether she recognise , in the frail , white - haired , old prelate who arrive from Italy , the vigorous , bearded priest know to she , in her girlhood 's day , as " the Bishop pause and look steadily at the Knight " as Father Gervaise . " 

 " Father Gervaise ! " exclaim Hugh d'Argent , lift his hand to cross himself as he name the Dead , yet arrest in this instinctive movement by something in those keen blue eye . " Father Gervaise , my lord , perish in a stormy sea . the ship founder , and none who sail in she be see again . " 

 the Knight speak with conviction ; yet , even as he speak , the amazing truth rush in upon he , and strike he dumb . of a sudden he know why the Bishop 's eye have instantly win his fearless confidence . a trust friend of his childhood have look out at he from their dear depth . often he have search his memory , since the Bishop have claim knowledge of he in his boyhood , and have marvel that no recollection of Symon as a guest in his parent ' home come back to he . 

 now in this moment of revelation how clearly he could see the figure of the famous priest , in brown habit , cloak , and hood , a cord at his waist , with tonsured head , full brown beard , and sandalle foot , pace the great hall , stand in the armoury , or climb the Cumberland hill to visit the chapel of the Holy Mount and the hermit who dwelt beside it . 

 as be the way with childhood 's memory , the small , most trivial detail leapt up vivid , crystal clear . the present be forget , the future disregard , in the sudden intimate dearness of that long - ago past . 

 the Bishop allow time for this realisation . then he speak . 

 " true , the ship founder , Hugh ; true , none who sail in she be see again . and , if I tell you that one swimmer , after long buffeting , be fling up on a rocky coast , lie for many week sick unto death in a fisherman 's humble cot , rise at last the frail shadow of his former self , to find that his hair have turn white in that desperate night , to find that none know his name nor his estate , that leave Father Gervaise and his failure at the bottom of the ocean he could shave his beard , and make his way to Rome under any name he please ; if I tell you all this , I trust you with a secret , Hugh , know to one other only , during all these year his Holiness , the Pope . " 

 " Father ! " exclaim the Knight , with deep emotion ; " Father " then , his voice break . he drop on one knee in front of the Bishop , and clasp the band stretch out to he . 

 what strange thing have happen ? one , greatly love and long mourn , have rise from the dead ; yet she who have well love and most mourn he , have herself pass to the Realm of Shadows , and be not here to wonder and to rejoice . 

 " Father , " say Hugh , when he could trust his voice , " in her last word to I , my mother speak of you . I go to her chamber to bid her sleep well , and together we knelt before the crucifix . ' let we repeat , ' whisper my mother , ' those holy word of comfort which Father Gervaise ever bid his penitent to say , as they kneel before the die Redeemer . ' ' mother , ' say I , ' I know they not . ' ' thou wert so young , my son , ' she say , ' when Father Gervaise last be with we . ' ' tell I the word , ' I say ; ' I should like well to have they from thy lip . ' so , lift her eye to the dead Christ , my mother say , with awe and reverence in her voice and a deep gladness on her face : ' he ever liveth to make intercession for we . ' and , in the dawn of the new day , her spirit pass . " 

 the Bishop lay his hand upon the Knight 's bow head . " my son , " he say , " of all the woman I have know , thy gentle mother bear the most beautiful and saintly character . I would there be more such as she , in our british home . " 

 " Father , " say Hugh , brokenly , " know you how much she have to bear ? my father 's fierce feud with all , shut she up at last to utter loneliness . his anger against Holy Church and his contempt of her priest , cost my mother the comfort of your visit . his life - long quarrel with Earl Eustace de Norelle cause that our family , though dwell within a three hour ' ride , be allow no intercourse . never do I enter Castle Norelle until I ride up from the South , with a message for Mora from the king . and , to this day , Mora have never be within the courtyard of my home ! when we be betroth , I dare not tell my parent though Earl Eustace and his Countess both be dead lest my father 's wrath might reach Mora , when I have go . news of his death , chance to I in a far - off land , bring I home . and truly , it be home indeed , at last ! peace and content , where always there have be turbulence and strain . Father , I tell you this because I know my gentle mother fear you do not understand , and that you may have think her love for you have fail . " 

 Symon of Worcester smile . 

 " dear lad , " he say , " I understand . " 

 " ah why , " cry Hugh , with sudden passion , " why should a woman 's whole life be spoil , and other life be darken and make sad , just by the angry , churlish , sullen whim of " 

 " hush , boy ! " say the Bishop , quickly . " you speak of your father , and you name the Dead . something die in the living , each time they speak evil of the Dead . I know your father ; and , though he love I not , yet , to be honest , I must say this of he : Sir Hugo be a good man and true ; upright , and a man of honour . he carry his shield untarnished . if he be fear by his friend , he be also fear by his foe . brave he be and fearless . one thing he lack ; and often , alas , they who lack just one thing , lack all . 

 " Hugo d'Argent know not love for his fellow - man . to be a man , be to earn his frown ; all thing human call forth his disdain . to view the same landscape , breathe the same air , in fact walk the same earth as he , be to stand in his way , and raise his ire . yet in his harsh , vex manner he love his wife , and love his little son . nor have he any self - conceit . he realise in himself his own bad foe . lest we fall into this snare , it be well daily to pray : ' o Lover of Mankind , grant unto I truly to love my fellow - man ; to honour they , until they prove worthless ; to trust they , until they prove faithless ; and ever to expect well of they , than I expect of myself ; to think well of they , than I think of myself . ' let we go through life , my son , search for good in other , not for evil ; we may miss the good , if we search not for it ; the evil , alas , will find we , quite soon enough , unsought . " 

 suddenly Hugh lift his head . 

 " Father , " he say , " the starling ! mind you the starling with the broken wing , which you and I find in the wood and carry home ; and you do set his wing , and tame he , and teach he to say ' hugh ' ? each time I bring he food , you say : ' Hugh ! hugh ! ' and soon the starling , see I come , also say : ' Hugh ! hugh ! ' do you remember , Father ? " 

 " I do remember , " say the Bishop . " I see thee now , come across the courtyard , bread and meat in thy hand a little lad , bareheade in the sunshine , glow with pleasure because the starling run to meet thee , shout ' Hugh ! ' " 

 " then listen , dear Father .   ah , how often have I wish to tell you this !   soon after you be go , that starle rudely teach I a hard lesson . gain strength , one day he leave the courtyard , run through the buttery , and wander in the garden . I follow , whistle and watch . it greatly delight the bird to find himself on turf . there have be rain . the grass be wet . presently a rash worm , glide from its hole , adventure forth . the starling run to the worm , call it ' hugh . ' ' Hugh ! Hugh ! ' he cry , and tug it from the earth . ' Hugh ! hugh ! ' and peck it , where helpless it lie squirm . then , shout ' Hugh ! ' once more , gobble it down . I stand with heavy heart , for I have think that starle love I with a true , personal love , when he run at my approach shout my name . yet now I know it be the food I carry , he call ' Hugh ' ; it be the food , not I , he love . Glad be I when , his wing grow strong , he fly away . it cut I to the heart to hear the worm , the grub , the snail , the caterpillar , all call ' Hugh ' ! " 

 the Bishop smile , then sigh . " poor little eager heart , " he say , " learn so hard a lesson , all alone ! yet be it a lesson , lad , soon or later learn in sadness by all generous heart . . . . and now , leave the past , with all its memory , let we return to the present , and face the uncertain future . also , dear Knight , I must ask you to remember , even when we be alone , that your old friend , Father Gervaise , in his brown habit , lie at the bottom of the ocean ; yet that your new friend , Symon of Worcester , hold you and your interest very near his heart . " 

 the Bishop put out his hand . 

 Hugh seize and kiss it , know this be his farewell to Father 
 Gervaise . 
 then he rise to his foot . 

 the Bishop say nothing ; but an indefinable change come over he . 
 again he extend his hand . 
 the Knight kneel , and kiss the Bishop 's ring . 

 " I thank you , my lord , " he say , " for your great trust in I . I will not prove unworthy . " with this he go back to his seat . 

 the Bishop , lift the faggot - fork , carefully stir and build up the log . 

 " what be we say , my dear Knight , when we stray into a side issue ? ah , I remember ! I be tell you of my appointment to the see of Worcester , and my belief that the Prioress fail to recognise in I , one she have know long year before . " 

 the Bishop put by the faggot - fork and turn from the fire . 

 " I find the promise of that radiant girlhood more than fulfil . she be change ; she shew obvious sign of have pass through the furnace ; but pure gold can stand the fire . the strength of purpose , the noble outlook upon life , the gracious tenderness for other , have mature and develop . even the necessary restriction of monastic life could not modify the grand line both mental , and physical on which Nature have mould she . 

 " I endeavour to think no thought concern she , other than should be think of a holy lady who have take vow of celibacy . yet , see she so fit to have make house home for a man , help he upward , and to have be the mother of a fine race of son and daughter , I feel it grievous that in leave the world for a reason which in no sense could be consider a true vocation , she should have cut herself off from such power and possibility . 

 " so pass the year in the calm service of God and of the Church ; yet always I seem aware that a crisis would come , and that , when that crisis come , she would need I . " 

 the Bishop pause and look at the Knight . 

 Hugh 's face be in shadow ; but , as the Bishop look at he , the ruby on his breast glitter in the firelight , as if some sudden thought have set he strongly quiver . 

 at sight of which , a flash of firm resolve , like the swift drawing of a sword , break o'er the Bishop 's calmness . it be quick and powerful ; it seem to divide asunder soul and spirit , joint and marrow , and to discern the thought and intent of the heart . and before that two - edge blade could sheathe itself again , swiftly the Bishop speak . 

 " therefore , my dear Hugh , when you arrive with your tale of wrong and treachery , all unconsciously to yourself , every word you speak of your betrothed reveal she to the man who have love she while you be yet a youth , with your spur to win , and all life before you . 

 " I see in your arrival , and in the strange tale you tell , a wondrous chance for she of that full development of life for which I know she to be so perfectly fit . 

 " it have seem indeed the irony of fate that , while I have flee and dwelt in exile lest my presence should hold she back from marriage , the treachery of other should have drive she into a life of celibacy . 

 " therefore while , with my tacit consent , you go to work in your own way , I send my messenger to Rome bear to the Holy Father a full account of all , petition a dispensation from vow take owe to deception , and ask leave to unite in the holy sacrament of marriage these long - sunder lover , undertake that no scandal should arise therefrom , either in the Nunnery or in the City of Worcester . 

 " as you have see , my messenger this night return ; and we now find ourselves arm with the full sanction of his Holiness , provide the prioress , of her own free will , desire to renounce the high position she have win in her holy calling , and to come to you . " 

 the quiet voice cease speak . 

 the Knight rise slowly to his foot . at first he stand silent . then he speak with a calm dignity which prove he worthy of the Bishop 's trust . 

 " I greatly honour you , my lord , " he say ; " and be our age and condition other than they be , so that we might fight for the woman we love , I should be proud to cross sword with you . " 

 the Bishop sit look into the fire . a faint smile flicker at the corner of the sensitive mouth . the fight he have fight for the woman he love have be of stern quality than the mere crossing of knightly sword . 

 Hugh d'Argent speak again . 

 " profoundly do I thank you , Reverend Father , for all that you have do ; and even more , for that which you do not do . it be six year after her first sojourn at the Court that I meet Mora , love she , and win she ; and well I know that the sweet love she give to I be a love from which no man have brush the bloom . " 

 Hugh pause . 

 those kindly and very luminous eye be still bent upon the fire . be the Bishop find it hard to face the fact that his life 's secret have now , by his own act , pass into the keeping of another ? 

 Hugh move a pace nearer . 

 " and deeply do I love you , Reverend Father , for your wondrous goodness to she , and for her sake to I . and I pray heaven , " add Hugh d'Argent simply , " that if she come to I , she may never know that she once win the love of so greatly well a man than he who win her . " 

 with which the Knight drop upon one knee , and humbly kiss the hem of the Bishop 's robe . 

 Symon of Worcester be greatly move . 

 " my son , " he say , " we be at one in desire her happiness and high good . for the rest , God , and her own pure heart , must guide her foot into the way of peace . " 

 the Bishop rise , and go to the casement . 

 " the aurora break in the east . the dawn be near . come with I , Hugh , to the chapel . we pray for his Holiness , give thank for his gracious letter and mandate ; we praise for the safe return of my messenger . but we will also offer up devout petition that the Prioress may have clear light at this parting of the way , and that our enterprise may be bring to a happy conclusion . " 

 so , presently , in the dimly - light chapel , the Knight knelt alone ; while , away at the high altar , remote , wrapt , absorb in the supreme act of his priestly office , stand the Bishop , celebrate mass . 

 yet one anxious prayer ascend from the heart of both . 

 and , in the pale dawn of that new day , the woman for whom both the Knight and the Bishop pray , keep vigil in her cell , before the shrine of the Madonna . 

 " Blessed Virgin , " she say ; " thou who lovedst Saint Joseph , be betroth to he , yet didst keep thyself an holy shrine consecrate to the Lord and his need of thee oh , grant unto I strength to put from I this constant torment at the thought of his suffering to whom once I give my troth , and to reconsecrate myself wholly to the service of my Lord . " 

 thus these three knelt , as a new day dawn . 

 and the Knight pray : " give she to I ! " 

 and the Bishop pray : " guide her foot into the way of peace . " 

 and the prioress , with hand cross upon her breast and eye uplifted , say : " cause I to know the way wherein I should walk ; for I lift up my soul unto Thee . " 

 the silver streak of the aurora pal before soar shafts of gold , bright herald of the rise sun . 

 then from the Convent garden trill softly the first note , poignant but pass sweet , of the robin 's song . 

 CHAPTER XXV 

 MARY ANTONY receive the BISHOP 

 the morning after the return from Rome of the Bishop 's messenger , the old lay - sister , Mary Antony , chance to be cross the Convent courtyard , when there come a loud knock on the outer gate . 

 Mary Antony , hastening , thrust aside the buxom porteress , and herself open the guichet , and look out . 

 the Lord Bishop , mount upon his white palfrey , wait without ; 
 Brother Philip in attendance . 
 what a bewildering surprise ! what a fortunate thing , think old Antony , that she should chance to be there to deal with such an emergency . 

 never do the Bishop visit the Nunnery , without send a messenger beforehand to know whether the prioress could see he , state the exact hour of his propose arrival ; so that , when the great door be fling wide and the Bishop ride into the courtyard , the Prioress would be stand at the top of the step to receive he ; Mother Sub - Prioress in attendance in the background ; the other holy lady upon their knee within the entrance ; Mary Antony , well out of sight , yet where peeping be possible , because she love to see the Reverend Mother kneel and kiss the Bishop 's ring , rise to her foot again without pause , make of the whole movement one graceful , deep obeisance . after which , Mary Antony , still peep , greatly love to see the prioress mount the wide , stone staircase with the Bishop ; each shew a courtly deference to the other . 

  one of Mary Antony 's most exalt dream of heaven , be of a place where she should sit upon a jasper seat and see the Reverend Mother and the great Lord Bishop mount together interminable flight of golden stair ; while Mother Sub - Prioress and Sister Mary Rebecca look through black bar , somewhere down below , whence they would have a good view of Mary Antony on her jasper seat , but no glimpse of the golden stair or of the radiant figure which she watch ascend . 

 so much for the usual visit of the Bishop , when everything be in readiness for his reception . 

 but now , all unexpected , the Bishop wait without the gate , and Mary 
 Antony have to deal with this emergency . 
 cry to the porteress to open wide , she hasten to the step . . . . 
 it be impossible to summon the Reverend Mother in time . . . . the 
 Lord Bishop must not be keep wait ! . . . even now the great door 
 be roll back . 
 Mary Antony mount the six step ; then turn in the doorway . 

 the Lord Bishop must be receive . there be nobody else to do it . she would receive the Lord Bishop ! 

 as she see he rid in upon icon , bless the porteress as he pass , she remember how she have ride round the river meadow as the Bishop . now she must play her part as the prioress . 

 so it come to pass that , as he ride up to the door and dismount , fling his rein to Brother Philip , the Bishop find himself confront by the queer little figure of the aged lay - sister , draw up to its full height and obviously uphold by a sense of importance and dignity . 

 as the Bishop reach the entrance , she kneel and kiss his ring ; then try to rise quickly , fail , and clutch at his hand , exclaim : " Devil take my old knee - joint ! " 

 never before have the Bishop be receive with such a formula ! never have his ring be kiss by a lay - sister ! but remember the scene when old Antony ride round the field upon Icon , he understand that she now be play the part of prioress . 

 " good - day , worthy Mother , " he say , as he raise she . " the spirit be willing I know , but , in your case , the knee - joint be weak . but no wonder , for they have do you long service . why , I get up slowly from kneeling , yet my knee be thirty year young than your . . . . nay I will not mount to the Reverend Mother 's chamber until you acquaint she of my arrival . take I round to the garden , and there let I wait in the shade , while you seek she . " 

 greatly elated at the success of her effort , and embolden by his charming condescension , Mary Antony lead the Bishop through the rose - arch ; and , cast a furtive glance at his face from behind the curtain of her veil , venture to hope there be naught afoot which could bring trouble or care to the Reverend Mother . 

 Mary Antony be trot beside the Bishop , down the long walk between the yew hedge , when she give vent to this anxious question . 

 at once the Bishop slacken speed . 

 " not so fast , Sister Antony , " he say . " I pray you to remember mine age , and to moderate your pace . why should you expect trouble or anxiety for the Reverend Mother ? " 

 " Nay , " say Mary Antony , " I expect naught ; I see naught ; I hear naught ! ' twa all mine own mistake , count with my pea . I tell the Reverend Mother so , and set her mind at rest by carry up six pea , say that I have find six and not five in my wallet . " 

 " let we pause , " say the Bishop , " and look at this lily . how lovely be its petal . how tall and white it shews against the hedge . why do you need to set the Reverend Mother 's mind at rest , Sister Antony , by carry up six pea ? " 

 " because , " say the old lay - sister , " when I have count as they return , the twenty holy lady who have go to vesper , yet another pass make twenty - one . upon which I run and report to the Reverend Mother , say in my folly , that I fear the twenty - first be Sister Agatha , return to walk amongst the living , she be over fifty year number with the Dead . yet many a time , just before dawn , have I hear she rap on the cloister door ; aye , many a time tap ! tap ! tap ! but what good would there be in opening to a poor lady you help thrust into her shroud , nigh upon sixty year before ? so ' tap away ! ' say I ; ' tap away , Sister Agatha ! try Saint Peter at the gate of Paradise . Old Antony know well than to let you in . ' " 

 " what say the Reverend Mother when you report on a twenty - first 
 White Lady ? " ask the Bishop . 
 " Reverend Mother bid I begone , while she herself deal with the wraith of Sister Agatha . " 

 " and why do you not go ? " ask the Bishop , quietly . 

 completely take aback , Mary Antony 's ready tongue fail she . she stand stock still and star at the Bishop . her gum begin to rattle and she clap her knuckle against they , horror and dismay in her eye . 

 the Bishop look searchingly into the frightened old face , and there read all he want to know . then he smile ; and , take she gently by the arm , pace on between the yew hedge . 

 " Sister Antony , " he say , and the low tone of his voice fall like quiet music upon old Antony 's perturb spirit ; " you and I , dear Sister Antony , love the Reverend Mother so truly and so faithfully , that there be nothing we would not do , to save she a moment 's pain . we know how noble and how good she be ; and that she will always decide aright , and follow in the footstep of our blessed Lady and all the holy saint . but other there be , who do not love she as we love she , or know she as we know she ; and they might judge she wrongly . therefore we must tell to none , that which we know how the Reverend Mother , alone , deal with that visitor , who be not the wraith of Sister Agatha . " 

 Mary Antony peep up at the Bishop . a light of great joy be on her face . her eye have lose their look of terror , and begin to twinkle cunningly . 

 " I know naught , " she say . " I see naught ; I hear naught . " 

 the Bishop smile . 

 " how many pea be leave in your wallet , Sister Antony ? " 

 " five , " chuckle Mary Antony . 

 " why do you shew six to the Reverend Mother ? " 

 " to set her mind at rest , " whisper the old lay - sister . 

 " to cause she to think that you have hear naught , see naught , and know naught ? " 

 Mary Antony nod , chuckle again . 

 " faithful old heart ! " say the Bishop . " what give thee this thought ? " 

 " our blessed Lady , in answer to her petition , sharpen the wit of old 
 Antony . " 
 the Bishop sigh . " may our blessed Lady keep they sharp , " he murmur , half aloud . 

 " amen , " say Mary Antony with fervour . 

 CHAPTER XXVI 

 love never FAILETH 

 the Bishop await the Prioress on that stone seat under the beech , from which the robin have carry off the pea . 

 he see she come through the sunlit cloister . 

 as she move down the step , and come swiftly toward he , he be conscious at once of an indefinable change in she . 

 have that ride upon Icon set she free from trammel in which she have be hitherto immeshe ? 

 as she reach he , he take both her hand , so that she should not kneel . 

 " already I have be receive with obeisance , my daughter , " he say ; and tell she of old Mary Antony 's quaint little figure , stand to do the honour in the doorway . 

 the prioress , at this , laugh gaily , and in her turn tell the Bishop of the scene , on this very spot , when old Antony display her pea to the robin . 

 " what pea ? " ask the Bishop ; and so hear the whole story of the twenty - five pea and the daily counting , and of the identifying of certain of the pea with various member of the Community . " and a large , white pea , choose for its fine aspect , be myself , " say the prioress ; " and , leave the Sub - Prioress and Sister Mary Rebecca , Master Robin swoop down and fly off with I ! hear cry of distress , I hasten hither , to find Mary Antony denounce the robin as ' Knight of the Bloody Vest , ' and make loud lamentation over my abduction . her imagining become more real to she than reality . " 

 " she hath a faithful heart , " say the Bishop , " and a shrewd wit . " 

 " faithful ? aye , " say the prioress , " faithful and loving . yet it be but lately I have realise , the love , beneath her carefulness and devotion . " the Prioress bend her level brow , look away to the overhang branch of the Pieman 's tree . " how quickly , in these place , we lose the very remembrance of the meaning of personal , human love . we grow so soon accustomed to allow ourselves to dwell only upon the abstract or the divine . " 

 " that be a loss , " say the Bishop . he turn and begin to pace slowly toward the cloister ; " a grievous loss , my daughter . soon than that you should suffer that loss , beyond repair , I would let the daring Knight of the Bloody Vest carry you off on swift wing . well a robin 's nest , if , love be there , than a nunnery full of dead heart . " 

 he hear the quick catch of her breath , but give she no chance to speak . 

 " ' and now abideth faith , hope , love , these three , ' " quote the Bishop ; " ' but the great of these be love . ' " 

 they be move through the cloister . the Prioress turn in the doorway , pause that the Bishop might pass in before she . 

 " this , my lord , " she say , with a fine sweep of her arm , " be the abode of Faith and Hope , and also of that divine Love , which excelleth both Hope and Faith . " 

 " Nay , " say the Bishop , " I pray you , listen . ' love suffereth long , and be kind ; love envieth not ; love vaunteth not itself , be not puff up ; doth not behave itself unseemly ; seeketh not her own ; be not easily provoke , think no evil ; rejoiceth not in iniquity , but rejoiceth in the truth ; beareth all thing , believeth all thing , hopeth all thing , endureth all thing . love never faileth . ' methink , " say the Bishop , in a tone of gentle meditation , as he enter the prioress 's cell , " the apostle be speak of a most human love ; yet he rat it high than faith and hope . " 

 " be you still dwell upon Sister Mary Seraphine , my lord ? " inquire the prioress , and in her voice he hear the sound of a gathering storm . 

 " Nay , my dear prioress , " say the Bishop , seat himself in the spanish chair , and lay his biretta upon the table near by ; " I speak not of self - love , nor do the apostle whose word I quote . I take it , he write of human love , sanctify ; upborne by faith and hope , yet great than either ; just as a bird be great than its wing , yet can not mount without they . we must have faith , we must have hope ; then our poor earthly love can rise from the low level of self - seeking and self - pleasing and take their place among those thing that be eternal . " 

 the Prioress have place her chair opposite the Bishop . she be very pale , and her lip tremble . she make so great an effort to speak with calmness , that her voice sound stern and hard . 

 " why this talk of earthly love , my Lord Bishop , in a place where all earthly love have be renounce and forget ? " 

 the Bishop , see those trembling lip , ignore the hard tone , and answer , very tenderly , with a simple directness which scorn all evasion : 

 " because , my daughter , I be here to plead for Hugh . " 

 CHAPTER XXVII 

 the woman and her CONSCIENCE 

 " for Hugh ? " say the Prioress . and then again , in low tone of incredulous amazement , " for Hugh ! what know you of Hugh , my lord ? " 

 the Bishop look steadfastly at the prioress , and reply with exceed gravity and earnestness : 

 " I know that in break your solemn troth to he , you be break a very noble heart ; and that in leave his home desolate , you be rob he not only of his happiness but also of his faith . man be apt to rate our holy religion , not by its theory , but by the way in which it causeth we to act in our dealing with they . if you condemn Hugh to sit beside his hearth , through the long year , a lonely , childless man , you take the Madonna from his home ; if you take your love from he , I greatly fear lest you should also rob he of his belief in the love of God . I do not say that these thing should be so ; I say that we must face the fact that thus they be . and remember between a man and woman of noble birth , each with a stainless escutcheon , each believe the other to be the soul of honour , a broken troth be no light matter . " 

 " I do not break my troth , " say the prioress , " until I believe that 
 Hugh have break his . I have suffer sore anguish of heart and 
 humiliation of spirit , over the news of his marriage with his cousin 
 Alfrida , ere I resolve to renounce the world and enter the cloister . " 
 " but Hugh do not we d his cousin , nor any other woman , " say the Bishop . " he be true to you in every thought and act , even after he also have pass through sore anguish of heart by reason of your suppose marriage with another suitor . " 

 " I learn the truth but a few day since , " say the prioress . " for seven long year I think Hugh false to I . for seven long year I believe he the husband of another woman , and school myself to forget every memory of past tenderness . " 

 " you be both deceive , " say the Bishop . " you have both pass through deep water . you each owe it to the other to make all possible reparation . " 

 " for seven holy year , " say the prioress , firmly , " I have be the bride of Christ . " 

 " do you love Hugh ? " ask the Bishop . 

 there be silence in the chamber . 

 the Prioress desire , most fervently , to take her stand as one dead to all earthly love and desire . yet each time she open her lip to reply , a fresh picture appear in the mirror of her mental vision , and close they . 

 she see herself , with hand outstretche , clasp Hugh 's as they kneel together before the shrine of the Madonna . she could feel the rush of pulse life flow from his hand to the palm of her , and so upward to her poor numbed heart , make it beat its wing like a cage bird . 

 she feel again the strength and comfort of the strong arm on which she lean , as slowly through the darkness she and Hugh pace in silence , side by side . 

 she remember each time when obedience have seem strangely sweet , and she have love the manly abruptness of his command . 

 she see Hugh , in the ring of yellow light cast by the lantern , kneel at her foot . she feel his hair , thick and soft , between her finger . 

 and then she remember that shudder sob , and the instant breaking down of every barrier . he be her , to comfort ; she be his , to soothe his pain . then the exquisite moment of yield ; the relief of the clasp of his strong arm ; the pass away of the suffering of long year , as she feel his lip on her , and surrender to the hunger of his kiss . 

 then one last picture when loyal to her wish , feel rather than express , he have free she , and pass , without further word or touch , up into that dim grey light like a pearly dawn at sea pass , and be lose to view ; she see herself leave in utter loneliness , the heavy door lock by her own turning of the key , he on one side , she on the other , for ever ; she see herself lie beneath the ground , in darkness and desolation , her face in the damp dust where his foot have stand . 

 " do you love Hugh ? " again demand the Bishop . 

 and the prioress lift eye full of suffering , reproach , and pain , but also full of courage and truth , to his face , and answer simply : " alas , my lord , I do . " 

 the silence thereafter follow be tense with conflict . the Bishop turn his eye to the figure of the Redeemer upon the cross , self - sacrifice personify , while the prioress master her emotion . 

 then : " ' love never faileth , ' " say the Bishop gently . 

 but the prioress have regain command over herself , and the gentle word be to she a challenge . she don , forthwith , the breastplate of holy resolve , and draw her sword . 

 " my Lord Bishop , you have wring from I a confession of my love ; but in so do , you have wring from I a confession of sin . a nun may not yield to such love as Hugh d'Argent still desire to win from I . with long hour of prayer and vigil , have I seek to purge my soul from the stain of a weak yielding even for ' a moment ' to the masterful insistence of this man , who force himself , by the subterfuge of a sacrilegious masquerade , into the sacred precinct of our Nunnery . I know not whom he bribe " continue the prioress , flash an indignant glance of suspicion at the Bishop .

 " but I do know , that somebody in high authority must have connive at his plotting , or he could not have find himself alone in the crypt at the hour of Vespers , in such wise as to assume our dress and , mingle with the return procession , gain entrance to the cloister . and somebody must still be aid and abet his plan , or he could not be , as he himself tell I he would be , daily in the crypt alone , during the hour when we pass to and from the clerestory . it anger I , my lord , to think that one who should , in this , be on my side , taketh part against I . "

 " ' Doth not behave itself unseemly , ' " murmur Symon of Worcester , put on his biretta . 

 the Prioress turn she back upon the Bishop , and walk over to the window . she be so angry that she feel the tear sting beneath her eyelid ; yet at the same time she experience a most incongruous desire to kneel down beside that beautiful and dignified figure , rest her head against the Bishop 's knee , and pour out the cruel tale of conflict , uncertainty and striving , temptation and hard - won victory , which , have lately make up the sum of her night and day . he have be her trust friend and counsellor during all these year . yet now she know he array against she , and she fear he more than she fear Hugh . Hugh wrestle with her feeling ; and , on the plane of the sens , she know she will would triumph . but the Bishop wrestle with her mentality ; and behind his calm gentleness be a strength of intellect which , if she yield at all , would seize and hold she , as steel finger in a velvet glove . 

 she return to her seat , compose but determine . 

 " Reverend Father , " she say , " I pray you to pardon my too swift indignation . to you I look to aid I in this time of difficulty . I grieve for the sorrow and disappointment to a brave and noble knight , a loyal lover , and a most faithful heart . but I can not reward faith with un - faith . if I break my sacred vow in order to give myself to he , I should not bring a blessing to his home . well an empty hearth than a hearth where brood a curse . besides , we never could live down the scandal cause . I should be anathema to all . the Pope himself would doubtless excommunicate we . it would mean endless sorrow for I , and danger for Hugh . on these ground , alone , it can not be . " 

 then the Bishop draw from his sash a fold sheet of vellum . 

 " my daughter , " he say , " when Hugh come to I with his grievous tale of treachery and loss , he refuse to give I the name of the woman he seek , say only that he believe she be to be find among the White Ladies of Worcester . when I ask her name he answer : ' Nay , I guard her name , as I would guard mine honour . if I fail to win she back ; if she withhold herself from I , so that I ride away alone ; then must I ride away leave no shadow of reproach on her fair fame . her name will be for ever in my heart , ' say Hugh , ' but no word of mine shall have leave it , in the mind of any man , link with a broken troth or a forsaken lover . ' I tell you this , my daughter , lest you should misjudge a very loyal knight .

 the Bishop pause . it become suddenly difficult to proceed . the clear eye of the Prioress be upon he . 

 " Whereupon , my lord ? " 

 " Whereupon I realise an early dream of mine seem promise a possible fulfilment . I know Hugh as a lad it be a veritable passion with I that all thing should attain unto their full perfection in short , I send a messenger to Rome , bear a careful account of the whole matter , in a private letter from myself to his Holiness the Pope . last evening , my messenger return , bring a letter from the Holy Father , with this enclose . " 

 the Bishop hold out the fold document .

 she turn upon the Bishop . 

 " my lord , the Church seem to be bring its power to bear on the side of the World , the Flesh , and the Devil , leave a woman and her conscience to stand alone and battle unaided with the grim force array against she . but you shall see that she know how to deal with any weapon of the adversary which happen to fall into her hand .  upon which the prioress rent the mandate from top to bottom , then across and again across ; fling the piece upon the floor , and set her foot upon they .

 so speak the angry prioress , make the quiet chamber to ring with her scorn and indignation .

 the Prioress weep , her head upon her hand , clasped and rest upon the Bishop 's knee . 

 Symon of Worcester lay his hand very gently upon that bow head , and as he do so his eye seek again the figure of the Christ upon the cross . the Prioress would have be startle indeed , have she lift her head and see those eye heretofore shrewd , search , kindly , or twinkle and gay , now full of an unfathomable pain . but , sob with her face hide , the Prioress be conscious only of her own suffering .

 the Bishop draw forth and unfold the letter from Rome , and very slowly , that each syllable might carry weight , he read it aloud .

 the grief , the utter disillusion , the dismayed question in her tone , move the Bishop to compunction . 

 " mine be the phrase , to begin with , my daughter , " he admit . " I use it to the Holy Father , and I confess that , in use it , I do mean to convey that which , as you well know . I have long believe , that wifehood and motherhood , if worthily perform , may rank higher in the Divine regard than vow of celibacy . but , in adopt the expression , the Holy Father , we may rest assure , have no thought of undervalue the monastic life , or the high position within it to which you have attain . I should rather take it that he be merely accept my assurance that the new vocation to which you be call would , in your particular case , be high service . " 

 the prioress , lift her head , look long into the Bishop 's face , without make reply . 

 her eye be drown in tear ; dark shadow lie beneath they . yet the light of a high resolve , unconquerable within she , shine through this veil of sorrow , as when the sun , behind it , break through the mist , victorious , chase by its clear beam the baffle fog . 

 see that look , the Bishop know , of a sudden , that he have fail ; that the Knight have fail ; that the all - powerful pronouncement from the Vatican have fail . 

 the woman and her conscience hold the field . 

 have conquer her own love , have master her own natural yearning for her lover , she would overcome with ease all other assailant . 

 in two day ' time Hugh would ride away alone . unless a miracle happen , Mora would not be with he . 

 the Bishop face defeat as he look into those clear eye , fearles even in their sorrowful humility . 

 " oh , child , " he say , " you love Hugh ! can you let he ride forth alone , accompany only by the grim spectre of unfaith and of despair ? his hope , his faith , his love , all centre in you . another Prioress can be find for this Nunnery . no other bride can be find for Hugh d'Argent . he will have his own betrothed , or none .  still kneel , the Prioress throw back her head , look upward , with clasped hand .

 the Prioress pause , look past the Bishop at the gracious figure of the Madonna . she have remember , of a sudden , how Hugh have kneel there , say : " Blessed Virgin . . . help this woman of mine to understand that if she break she troth to I , hold herself from I , now , when I be come to claim she , she send I out to an empty life , to a hearth beside which no woman will sit , to a home forever desolate . " 

 " but ? " say the Bishop , lean forward . " yes , my daughter ? but ? " 

 " but if our bless Lady herself vouchsafe I a clear sign that my first duty be to Hugh , if she absolve I from my vow , make it evident that God 's will for I be that , leave the Cloister , I should we d Hugh and dwell with he in his home ; then I would strive to bring myself to do this thing . but I can take release from none save from our Lord , to whom those vow be make , or from our Lady , who knoweth the heart of a woman , and whose grace hath be with I all through the striving and conflict of the year that be past . " 

 the Bishop sigh . " alas , " he say ; " alas , poor hugh ! " 

 for that our Lady should vouchsafe a clear sign , would have to be a miracle ; and , though he would not have admit it to the prioress , the Bishop believe , in his secret heart , that the age of miracle be past . 

 one so fix in her determination , so persistent in her assertion , so loud in her asseveration , would scarce be likely to hear the inward whispering of divine suggestion . 

 therefore , should our Lady intervene with clear guidance , that intervention must be miraculous . and the Bishop sighing , say : " alas , poor hugh ! "

 " alas , my lord , " she say , " you be witness of my grievous sin in thus rend the gracious message of his Holiness . will it please you to appoint I a penance , if such an act can indeed be expiate ? " 

 " the sin , my daughter , as I will presently explain , be scarcely so great as you think it . but , such as it be , it arise from a lack of calmness and of that mental equipoise which sail unruffled through a sea of contradiction . the irritability which result in display of sudden temper be so foreign to your nature that it point to your have pass through a time of very special strain , both mental and physical ; probably overlong vigil and fasting , while you wrestle with this anxious problem upon which so much , in the future , depend .

" say the Bishop , " that be ever the divine method . punishment should be remedial , as well as deterrent . there be much stiffness of mind of which we must be rid before we can stoop to the portal of God 's ' whosoever ' and , pass through the narrow gate , enter the Kingdom of Heaven as little child . " 

 the Bishop rise , and give his hand to the Prioress raise she to her foot .

" the mandate of his Holiness , inscribe upon parchment , from which hang the great seal of the Vatican , be safely place among my most precious document . you have but destroy the result of an hour 's careful work . I rise betime this morning to make this copy . I should not have allow you to tear it , have not the writing be my own . but I take pain to reproduce exactly the peculiar style of lettering they use in Rome , and you will do the same in your copy . " 

 turn , the Bishop kneel for a few moment in prayer before the Madonna . he could not have explain why , but somehow the only hope for Hugh seem to be connect with this spot .

 rise , the Bishop turn , with unwonted sternness , to the prioress . 

 " remember , " he say , " Hugh rid away to - morrow night ; rid away , never to return . "

 " yes , " say the Bishop slowly , " he have well have ride away ; or , well still , have never come upon this fruitless quest . " 

 he move toward the door . 

 the Prioress reach it before he . 

 with her hand upon the latch : " your blessing , Reverend Father , " entreat the prioress , rather breathlessly . 

 " Benedicite , " say the Bishop , with uplifted finger , but with eye avert ; and pass out . 

 CHAPTER XXVIII 

 the white STONE 

 Old Mary Antony be at the gate , when the Bishop ride out from the courtyard . 

 thrust the porteress aside , she press forward , stand with anxious face uplifted , as the Bishop approach . 

 he rein in Icon , and , bend from the saddle , murmur : " take care of she , Sister Antony . I have leave she in some distress . " 

 " Hath she decide aright ? " whisper the old lay - sister . 

 " she always decide aright , " say the Bishop . " but she be so make that she will thrust happiness from she with both hand unless our Lady should herself offer it , by vision or revelation . I could wish thy gay little Knight of the Bloody Vest might indeed fly with she to his nest and teach she a few sweet lesson , in the green privacy of some leafy paradise . but I tell thee too much , worthy Mother . keep a silent tongue in that shrewd old head of thine . Minister to she ; and send word to I if I be need . Benedicite . " 

 an hour later , mount upon his black mare , Shulamite , the Bishop ride to the high ground , on the north - east , above the city , from whence he could look down upon the river meadow . 

 as he have do on the previous day , he watch the prioress rid upon 
 Icon . 
 once she put the horse to so sudden and swift a gallop that the Bishop , watch from afar , rein back Shulamite almost on to her haunch , in a sudden fear that Icon be about to leap into the stream . 

 for an hour the Prioress ride , with fly veil , white on the white steed ; a fair marble group , quicken into motion . 

 then , that penance be duly perform , she vanish through the archway . 

 Turning Shulamite , Symon of Worcester ride slowly down the hill , pass southward , and enter the city by Friar 's Gate ; and so to the Palace , where Hugh d'Argent wait . 

 the Bishop lead he , through a postern , into the garden ; and there on a wide lawn , out of earshot of any possible listener , the Bishop and the Knight walk up and down in earnest conversation . 

 at length : " to - morrow , in the early morn , " say the Knight , " I send her tire - woman on to Warwick , with all her effect , keep back only the riding suit . should she elect to come , we must be free to ride without draw rein . even so we shall reach Warwick only something before midnight . " 

 " she tear it up and plant her foot upon it , " remark the Bishop . 

 " I will not give up hope , " say the Knight . 

 " nothing short of a miracle , my son , will change her mind , or move she from her fix resolve . " 

 " then our Lady will work a miracle , " declare the Knight bravely . " I pray ' send she to I ! ' and our blessed Lady smile . " 

 " a sculptured smile , dear lad , be ever there . have you pray ' hold she from I ! ' our Lady would equally have smile . " 

 " Nay , " say the Knight ; " I keep my trust in prayer . " 

 they pause at the parapet overhang the river . 

 " I be successful , " say the Knight , " in deal with Eustace , her nephew . there will be no need to apply to the king . the ambition be his mother 's . now Eleanor be dead , he care not for the Castle . next month he wed an heiress , with large estate , and have no wish to lay claim to Mora 's home . all be now once more as it be when she leave it . her own people be in charge . I plan to take she there when we leave Warwick , rid northward by easy stage . " 

 the Bishop , stoop , pick up a smooth , white stone , and fling it into the river . it fall with a splash , and sink . the water close upon it . it have vanish instantly from view . 

 then the Bishop speak . " Hugh , my dear lad , she think it be the Pope 's own deed and signature , yet she tear it across , and then again across ; fling it upon the ground , and set her foot upon it . I deem it now as impossible that the prioress should change her mind upon this matter , as that we should ever see again that stone which now lie deep on the river - bed . " 

 it be a high dive from the parapet ; and , to the Bishop , watch the spot where the Knight cleave the water , the moment seem hour . 

 but when the Knight reappear , the white stone be in his hand . 

 the Bishop go down to the water - gate . 

 " bravely do , my son ! " he call , as the Knight swam to the step . 
 " you deserve to win . " 
 but to himself he say : " fight man and quick - witted woman will be ever with we , gain their end by strenuous endeavour . but the age of miracle be past . " 

 Hugh d'Argent mount the step . 

 " I shall win , " he say , and shake himself like a great shaggy dog . 

 the Bishop , over whom fall a shower , carefully wipe the glistening drop from his garment with a fine italian handkerchief . 

 " go in , boy , " he say , " and get dry . send thy man for another suit , unless it would please thee well that Father Benedict should lend thee a cassock ! give I the stone . it may well serve as a reminder of that famous sacred stone from which the Convent take its name . methink we have , between we , contrive something of an omen , conclude in thy favour . " 

 presently the Bishop , alone in his library , stand the white stone upon the iron - bind chest within which he have place the Pope 's mandate . 

 " the age of miracle be past , " he say again . " iron no long swim , neither do stone rise from the depth of a river , unless the divine command be supplement by the grip of strong human finger . 

 " stand there , thou little tombstone of our hope . mark the place where lie the Holy Father 's mandate , ecclesiastically all - powerful , yet render null and void by the faithful conscience and the firm will of a woman . God send we more such woman ! " 

 the Bishop sound a silver gong , and when his body - servant appear , point to the handkerchief , damp and crumple , upon the table . 

 " Dry this , Jasper , " he say , " and bring I another somewhat large . 
 these dainty trifle can not serve , when ' tear run down like a river . ' 
 Nay , look not distressed , my good fellow . I do but jest . Yonder wet 
 Knight hath give I a shower - bath . " 
 CHAPTER XXIX 

 the vision of MARY ANTONY 

 on the afternoon follow the Bishop 's unexpected visit to the Nunnery , the Prioress elect to walk last in the procession to and from the Cathedral , place Mother Sub - Prioress first . it be her custom occasionally to vary the order of procession . sometimes she walk thirteenth , with twelve before , and twelve behind she . 

 she have at first incline on this day , after her strenuous time with the 
 Bishop , follow by the hour 's ride upon Icon , not to go to vesper . 
 then her heart fail she , and she go . on these two afternoon this and the morrow Hugh would still be in the crypt . she should not so much as glance toward the pillar at the foot of the wind stairway lead to the clerestory ; yet it would be sweet to feel he to be stand there as she pass ; sweet to know that he hear the same sound as fall upon her ear . 

 to - day , and again on the morrow , she might yield to this yearning for the comfort of his nearness ; but never again , for Hugh would not return . 

 she have wonder whether she dare ask he , by the Bishop , on a give date once a year to attend High Mass in the Cathedral , so that she might know he to be under the same roof , worship , at the same moment , the same blessed manifestation of the Divine Presence . 

 but almost at once she have dismiss the desire , realise that comfort such as this , could be comfort but to the heart of a woman , more likely torment to a man . also that should his fancy incline he to seek companionship and consolation in the love of another , a yearly pilgrimage to Worcester for her sake , would stand in the way of his future happiness . 

 walk last in that silent procession back to the Nunnery , the prioress walk alone with her sadness . her heart be heavy indeed . 

 she have anger her old friend , Symon of Worcester . after be infinitely patient , when he might well have have cause for wrath , he have suddenly take a sterner tone , and depart in a certain aloofness , leave she with the fear that she have lose he , also , beyond recall . 

 thus she walk in loneliness and sorrow . 

 as she pass up the step into the cloister , she note that Mary Antony be not in her accustomed place . 

 slightly wonder , and half unconsciously explain to herself that the old lay - sister have probably for some reason go forward with the Sub - Prioress , the prioress move down the now empty passage and enter her own cell . 

 on the threshold she pause , astonish . 

 in front of the shrine of the Madonna , kneel Mary Antony in a kind of trance , hand clasp , eye fix , lip part , the colour go from her cheek , yet a radiance upon her face , like the after - glow of a vision of exceed glory . 

 she appear to be wholly unconscious of the presence of the Prioress , who recover from her first astonishment , close the door , and come forward lay her hand gently upon the old woman 's shoulder . 

 Mary Antony 's eye remain fix , but her lip move incessantly . 
 bend over she , the prioress could make out disjoint sentence . 
 " Gone ! . . . but it be at our Lady 's bidding . . . . Flown ? ah , gay little Knight of the Bloody Vest ! Nay , it must have be the archangel Gabriel , or maybe Saint George , in shin armour . . . . how shall we live without the Reverend Mother ? but the will of our blessed Lady must be do . " 

 " Antony ! " say the Prioress . " wake up , dear Antony ! you be dream again . you be think of the robin and the pea . I have not go from you ; nor be I go . see ! I be here . "

 the old woman 's manner change . she fix her eye upon the prioress , and speak with an air of detachment and of mystery . the very simplicity of her language seem at once to lift the strange tale she tell , into sublimity . 

 " Aye , he come . but not for crumb ; not for cheese ; not to gossip with old Antony .

 CHAPTER XXX 

 the harder PART 

 Dawn break a silver rift in the purple sky and presently steal , in pearly light , through the oriel window . upon the prioress 's table , lie a beautifully execute copy of the Pope 's mandate . beside it , carefully piece together , the tear fragment of the Bishop 's copy . 

 also , open upon the table , lie the Gregorian Sacramentary , and near to it strip of parchment upon which the Prioress have copy two of those ancient prayer , append to each a careful translation . 

 these be the sixth century prayer which the Prioress have find comfort in copying and translating , during the long hour of her vigil . 

 o God , the Protector of all that trust in Thee , without whom nothing be strong , nothing be holy ; Increase and multiply upon we Thy mercy , that Thou be our ruler and guide , we may so pass through thing temporal , that we finally lose not the thing eternal ; Grant this , o heavenly Father , for Jesus Christ 's sake our Lord . amen . 

 and on another strip of parchment : 

 o Lord , we beseech Thee mercifully to receive the prayer of Thy people who call upon Thee ; and grant that they may both perceive and know what thing they ought to do , and also may have grace and power faithfully to fulfil the same : through Jesus Christ our Lord . amen . 

 then , in that darkest hour before the dawn , she have open the heavy clasp of an even old volume , and copy a short prayer from the Gelasian Sacramentary , under date A.D. 492 . 

 lighten our darkness , we beseech Thee O Lord , and my Thy great mercy defend we from all peril and danger of this night ; for the love of Thy only Son , our Saviour , Jesus Christ . amen . 

 this appear to have be copy last of all . the ink be still wet upon the parchment . 

 the candle have burn down to the socket , and go out . the 
 Prioress 's chair , push back from the table , be empty . 
 as the dawn creep in , it discover she kneeling before the shrine of the Madonna , absorb in prayer and meditation . 

 she have not yet take her final decision as to the future ; but her hesitation be now rather the slow , wondering , opening of the mind to accept an astounding fact , than any attempt to fight against it . 

 not for one moment could she doubt that our Lady , in answer to Hugh 's impassioned prayer , have choose to make plain the Divine will , by mean of this wonderful and most explicit vision to the aged lay - sister , Mary Antony . 

 when , have leave Mary Antony , as she suppose , asleep , the Prioress have reach her own cell , her first adore cry , as she prostrate herself before the shrine , have take the form of the thanksgiving once offer by the Saviour : " I thank Thee , o Father , Lord of Heaven and earth , that Thou hast hide these thing from the wise and prudent , and hast reveal they unto babe . " 

 she and the Bishop have indeed be wise and prudent in their own estimation , as they discuss this difficult problem . yet to they no clear light , no divine vision , have be vouchsafe . 

 it be to this age nun , the most simple so think the prioress the most humble , the most childlike in the community , that the revelation have be give . 

 the Prioress remember the nosegay of weed offer to our Lady ; the game with pea ; the childish pleasure in the society of the robin ; all the many indication that second - childhood have gently come at the close of the long life of Mary Antony ; just as the moon begin as a sickle turn one way and , after come to the full , wane at length to a sickle turn the other way ; so , after ninety year of life 's pilgrimage , Mary Antony be a little child again and of such be the Kingdom of Heaven ; and to such the Divine will be most easily reveal . 

 the Prioress be conscious that she and the Bishop the wise and prudent have so completely arrive at decision , along the line of their own point of view , that their mind be not ready to receive a divine unveiling . but the simple , childlike mind of the old lay - sister , full only of humble faith and love devotion , be ready ; and to she the manifestation come . 

 no shade of doubt as to the genuineness of the vision enter the mind of the prioress . she and the Bishop alone know of the Knight 's intrusion into the Nunnery , and of her interview with he in her cell . 

 before go in search of the intruder , she have order Mary Antony to the kitchen ; and disobedience to a command of the Reverend Mother , be a thing undreame of in the Convent . 

 afterwards , her anxiety lest any question should come up concern the return of a twenty - first White Lady when but twenty have go , be completely set at rest by that which have seem to her old Antony 's fortunate mistake in believe herself to have be mistake . 

 in recount the fictitious vision , with an almost uncanny cleverness , Mary Antony have describe the Knight , not as he have appear in the prioress 's cell , in tunic and hose , a simple dress of velvet and cloth , but in full panoply as a Knight - Crusader . the shin armour and the blood - red cross , fully in keep with the vision , would have preclude the idea of an eye - witness of the actual scene , have such a thought unconsciously suggest itself to the prioress . 

 as it be , it seem beyond question that all the knowledge of Hugh shewn by the old lay - sister , of his person his attitude , his very word , could have come to she by divine revelation alone . that be so , how could the prioress presume to doubt the climax of the vision , when our bless Lady place her hand in Hugh 's , utter the wondrous word : " take she . she hath be ever thine . I have but keep she for thee . " 

 over and over the prioress repeat these word ; over and over she thank our Lady for have vouchsafe so explicit a revelation . yet be she distressed that her inmost spirit fail to respond , acclaim the word as divine . she know they must be divine , yet could not feel that they be so . 

 as dawn creep into the cell , she find herself repeat again and again " a sign , a sign ! Thy will be hide from I ; yet I accept its revelation through this babe . but I ask a sign which shall speak to mine own heart , also ! a sign , a sign ! " 

 she rise and open wide the casement , not of the oriel window , but of one to the right of the group of the Virgin and child , and near by it . 

 she be wear out both in mind and body , yet could not bring herself to leave the shrine or to seek her couch . 

 she remember the example of that reverend and holy man , Bishop Wulstan . she have lately be read , in the Chronicles of Florence , the monk of Worcester , how " in his early life , when appoint to be chanter and treasurer of the Church , Wulstan embrace the opportunity of serve God with less restraint , give himself up to a contemplative life , go into the church day and night to pray and read the Bible . so devoted be he to sacred vigil that not only would he keep himself awake during the night , but day and night also ; and when the urgency of nature at last compel he to sleep , he do not pamper his limb by rest on a bed or covering , but would lie down for a short time on one of the bench of the Church , rest his head on the book which he have use for pray or reading . " 

 the Prioress chance to have read this passage aloud , in the Refectory , two day before . 

 as she stand in the dawn light , overcome with sleep , yet unwilling to leave her vigil at the shrine , she remember the example of this greatly revere Bishop of Worcester , " a man of great piety and dovelike simplicity , one belove of God , and of the people whom he rule in all thing , " dead just over a hundred year , yet ever live in the memory of all . 

 so , remember his example , the Prioress go to her table , and shut the clasp of her treasured gregorian Sacramentary , place it on the floor before the shrine of the Virgin . 

 then , fling her cloak upon the ground , and a silk covering over the book , she sink down , stretch she weary limb upon the cloak and lay her head on the Sacramentary , trust that some of the many sacred prayer therein contain would pass into her mind while she sleep . 

 yet still her spirit cry : " a sign , a sign ! however slight , however small ; a sign mine own heart can understand . " 

 whether she sleep a few moment only or an hour , she could not tell . yet she feel strangely rest , when she be awaken by the sound of a most heavenly song outpoure . it flood her cell with liquid trill , as of little silver bell . 

 the Prioress open her eye , without stir . 

 Sunlight stream in through the open window ; and lo , upon the marble hand of the Madonna , that very hand which , in the vision , have take hers and place it within Hugh 's , stand Mary Antony 's robin , that gay little Knight of the Bloody Vest , pour forth so wonderful a song of praise , and love , and fulness of joy , that it seem as if his little ruffle throat must burst with the rush of joyous melody . 

 the robin sing . our Lady smile . the Babe on her knee look merry . 

 the Prioress lie watch , not dare to move ; her head rest on the 
 Sacramentary . 
 then into her mind there come the suggestion of a test a sign . 

 " if he fly around the chamber , " she whisper , " my place be here . but if he fly straight out into the open , then doth our blessed Lady bid I also to arise and go . " 

 and , scarce have she so think , when , with a last triumphant trill of joy , straight from our Lady 's hand , like an arrow from the bow , the robin shoot through the open casement , and out into the sunny , newly - awaken world beyond . 

 the Prioress rise , fold her cloak , place the book back upon the table ; then kneel before the shrine , take off her cross of office , and lay it upon our Lady 's hand , from whence the little bird have fly . 

 then with bow head , pale face , hand meekly cross upon her breast , the Prioress kneel long in prayer . 

 the breeze of an early summer morn , blow in at the open window , and fan her cheek . 

 in the garden without , the robin sing to his mate .

 the Bishop 's prayer have be answer . 

 the Prioress have be give grace and strength to choose the hard part , believe the hard part to be , in very deed , God 's will for she .

 Almighty and everlaste God , who dost govern all thing in heaven and earth ; mercifully bear the supplication of Thy people , and grant we Thy peace , all the day of our life ; through Jesus Christ our Lord . amen .

 but this ungoverned impulse last but for the moment in which his passionate joy , recoil upon himself , strike he a blinding , a bewildering blow . 

 in ten second he have recover . his arm tighten more securely around she . 

 she have come to he . whatever complex emotion might now be stir within she , this fact be beyond question . also , she have come of her own free will . the foot which have dare to stamp upon the torn fragment of the Pope 's mandate , have , with an equal courage , step aside from the way of convention and have bring she within the compass of his arm . 

 he could not put she from he . she be his to hold and keep . but she be his also to shield and guard ; aye , to shield not from outward danger only , but from anything in himself which might cause her pain or perplexity , thus make more difficult her noble act of self - surrender . 

 word speak by the Bishop , in the banqueting hall , come back to he with fuller significance . 

 a joy arise within he , deeply far than the rapture of passion ; the joy of a faithful patience , of a strong man 's mastery over the strong thing in himself , of a lover 's comprehension , by sure instinct , of that which no word , however clear and forcible , could have succeed in make plain . 

 his love arise , a kingly thing , crown by her trust in he . 

 as he fold back the cloak , he stand with eye uplifted to the arched roof above his head . and the vision he see , in the dim pearly light , be a vision of the Madonna in his home . 

 the shelter of the cloak remove , the Prioress look around with startled eye , full of an unspeakable shrinking ; then upward to the face of her lover , and see it transfigure by the light of holy purpose and of a great resolve . 

 but , even as she look , he take his arm from about she , step a pace forward , leave she in the shadow , and whistle thrice the do - it - now call of the thrush . 

 instantly the man - at - arm leapt to their foot , and make quickly for the entrance to the Cathedral from the crypt , stand to hold it from without , against all comer . 

 as their run foot rang on the step , softly there sound through the crypt the plaintive call of the curlew . 

 the man lie upon the stretcher rise , leave his bandage behind ; and , without glance to right or left , pass quickly in and out amongst the forest of column , and be lose to view . the entrance he have to guard from within , be out of sight of the altar . to all intent and purpose , the two who still stand motionless in the shadow , be now alone . 

 then the Knight turn to the prioress , take she right hand with his left , and lead she forward to the altar . 

 there he loose her hand as they kneel side by side ; he clasp his upon the cross hilt of his sword ; she cross her upon her breast . 

 presently the Prioress draw the marriage ring from the third finger of her left hand , and give it to the Knight . 

 divine her desire , he rise , lay the ring upon the altar , then knelt again .

 the sad eye of the prioress , watch he , say to this neither " yea " nor " nay . "

 " Lay thyself down thereon , " he say . " I grieve to ask it of thee , 
 Mora ; but there be no other way of take thee hence , unobserved . " 
 the Prioress take two step forward , and stand beside the stretcher . 

 it be many year since she have lie in any human presence . stand , walking , sitting , kneeling , she have be see by the nun ; but lie never . 

 though her cross of office and sacred ring be go , her dignity and authority seem still to belong to she while she stand , stately and tall , upon her foot .

 " lie down , " say the Knight , sternly .

 " our Lady be with thee . it will not be for long . " 

 then , shrill through the silent crypt , ring the dear call of the blackbird . 

 CHAPTER XXXII 

 a great RECOVERY and RESTORATION 

 Symon , Bishop of Worcester , attend by his Chaplain , chance to be walk through the precinct on his way from the Priory to the Palace , just as the man - at - arm bear the stretcher come through the great door of the Cathedral . 

 Father Benedict , cowl , and rob completely in black , a head and shoulder tall than the Bishop , walk behind he , a somewhat sinister figure . 

 the Bishop stop . " precede I to the Palace , Father Benedict , " he say . " I wish to have speech with yonder Knight who , I think , come this way . " 

 the Chaplain stand still , make deep obeisance , jerk his cowl more closely over his face , and stride away . 

 the Bishop wait , a radiant figure , in the afternoon sunshine . his silken cassock , his silvery hair , his blue eye , so vivid and search , not only make a spot on which light concentrate , but almost seem themselves to give forth light . 

 the steady tramp of the man - at - arm draw nearer . 

 Hugh d'Argent walk beside the stretcher , head erect , eye shin , his hand upon the hilt of his sword .

 " Aye , my lord , " reply the Knight , " a great recovery and restoration . 
 we start for Warwick in an hour 's time . " 
 " wonderful ! " say the Bishop . " our Lady and the holy Saint be praise ! but you be wise to keep the patient well cover . however complete the restoration , great care be require at first , and over - exertion must be avoid . " 

 " your blessing for the patient , Reverend Father , " say the Knight , uncovering . 

 the Bishop move nearer . he lay his hand upon the form beneath the blue and silver cloak . 

 " Benedictio Domini sit vobiscum , " he say . then add , in a low tone : " be not afraid , neither be thou dismayed . . . . go in peace . " 

 the two man who love the prioress , look steadily at one another . 

 the man - at - arm move forward with their burden .

 the Bishop hasten to the Palace .

 the Bishop be white to the lip . his hand tremble as he walk .

 it be one thing to theorize , to speculate , to advise , when the prioress be safe in her Nunnery . it be quite another , to know that she be be carry through the street of Worcester , helpless , upon a stretcher ; that when that blue pall be lift , she would find herself in a hostel , alone with her lover , surround by man , not a woman within call . 

 the heart of a nun be a thing well know to the Bishop , and he tremble at thought of this , which he have help to bring about .

 arrive in the courtyard of the Palace , he call for Brother Philip . 

 " saddle I Shulamite , " he say . " also mount Jasper on our fast nag , with saddle - bag . we ride to Warwick ; and must start within a quarter of an hour . " 

 a portion of that time the Bishop spend write in the library . 

 when he be mount , he stoop from the saddle and speak to Brother 
 Philip . 
 " Philip , " he say , " a very noble lady , betroth to Sir Hugh d'Argent , have just arrive at the Star hostel , where for some day he have await she . she rid with the Knight forthwith to Warwick , where they will join I at the Castle . it be my wish to lend Iconoklastes to the lady . therefore I desire thee to saddle the palfrey precisely as he be saddle when he go to the Convent of the White Ladies for their pleasuring and play . lead he , without delay , to the hostel ; deliver he over to the man - at - arm of Sir Hugh d'Argent , and see that they hand this letter at once to the Knight , that he may give it to his lady . lose not a moment , my good Philip . look to see I return to - morrow . " 

 the Bishop gather up the rein , and start out , at a brisk pace , for the Warwick road . 

 the letter he have intrust to Brother Philip , seal with his own signet , be address to Sir Hugh d'Argent . but within be write : 

 will the Countess of Norelle be pleased to accept of the palfrey Iconoklastes as a marriage gift from her old friend Symon Wygorn . 

 CHAPTER XXXIII 

 MARY ANTONY hold the FORT 

 Mary Antony await in the cloister the return of the White Ladies from Vespers .

 leave alone , Mary Antony slowly open she right hand , and peer into the palm . 

 one pea lie within it .

 twenty - four ! one holy Lady have therefore not return . this must be report at once to the Reverend Mother . in her excitement , Mary Antony forget the emotion which have so recently possess she .

 the Reverend Mother 's cell be empty .

I be otherwise employ . and remember . Reverend Mother be on no account to be disturb . " 

 the porteress , at the gate , jump well - nigh out of her skin when , turning , she find Mary Antony at her elbow .
