 CHAPTER XXXIV 

 mora DE NORELLE 

 Symon , Bishop of Worcester , chid himself for restlessness . surely for once his mind have lose control of his limb . 

 no soon do he decide to walk the smooth lawn around the Castle , than he find himself mount to the battlement ; and now , though he have instal himself for greatly need repose in a deep seat in the hall chamber , yet here he be , pace the floor , or move from one window to another . 

 by dint of hard riding he have reach Warwick while the sun , though already dip beneath the horizon , still fleck the sky with rosy cloud , and spread a golden mantle over the west . 

 the lord of the Castle be away , in attendance on the king ; but all be in readiness for the arrival of the Bishop , and great preparation have be make for the reception of Sir Hugh d'Argent . his people , have leave Worcester early that morning , be about in the courtyard , as the Bishop ride in . 

 as he pass through the doorway , an elderly woman , buxom , comely , and of motherly aspect , whom he easily divine to be the tire - woman of whom the Knight have speak , come forward to meet he . 

 " Good my lord , " she say , her eagerness allow of scant ceremony , " come Sir Hugh d'Argent hither this night ? " 

 " aye , " reply the Bishop , look with kindly eye upon Mora 's old nurse . " within two hour , he should be here . " 

 " come he alone , my lord ? " ask Mistress Deborah . 

 " Nay , " reply the Bishop , " the Countess of Norelle , a very noble lady to whom the Knight be betroth , rid hither with he . "

 " a corpse for a bride ! a corpse for a bride ! " the hoof of the black mare Shulamite have seem to beat out upon the road . " alas , poor Knight ! a corpse for a bride ! " 

 the Bishop come down from the battlement .

 a night - hawk , fly high overhead and look downward as it fly , might have suppose that a great scarlet poppy have leave its clump in the flower - bed , and be promenade on the turf .

 but suppose the prioress have falter at the last , and have beseech to be return to the Nunnery ? would the chivalry of the Knight have stand such a test ? and , have leave in secret , how could she return openly ? would the way through the crypt be possible ? 

 the Bishop begin to wish that he have ride to the Star hostel and await development there , instead of hasten on before . 

 the hall chamber be in the centre of the Castle . its casement look out upon the garden . thus it come about that he do not hear a cavalcade ride into the courtyard . he do not hear the shouting of the man , the ring of hoof on the pave stone , the champing of horse .

 suddenly , without any warning , the door , lead from the ante - chamber at the further end of the hall , open . 

 frame in the doorway appear a vision , which for a moment lead Symon of Worcester to question whether he dream , so beautiful beyond belief be the woman in a green riding - dress , look at he with starry eye , her cheek aglow , a veil of golden hair fall about her shoulder . 

 oh , Mora , child of delight ! have the exquisite promise of thy girlhood indeed fulfil itself thus ? have the year change thee so little -and yet so greatly ? 

 " the captive exile hasteneth " ; exile , long ago , for thy sake ; seek to be free , yet captive still , catch once and forever in the mesh of that golden hair . 

 oh , Mora , child of delight ! must all this planning for thy full development and perfecting of joy , involve the poignant anguish of thus see thee again ? 

 Symon of Worcester rise and stand , a noble figure in crimson and gold , at the top of the hall . but for the silver moonlight of his hair , he might have be a man in his prime so erect be his carriage , so keen and bright be his eye .

 CHAPTER XXXIX 

 the " SPLENDID knight " 

 on the step of Warwick Castle stand the Knight and his bride . 

 their eye still linger on the archway through which the noble figure of Symon , Bishop of Worcester , mount upon his black mare , Shulamite , have just disappear from view . 

 the marriage have take place in the Castle chapel , half an hour before , with an astonishing amount of pomp and ceremony . priest and acolyte have appear from unexpected place . Madonna lily , on graceful stem , gleam white in the shadow of the sacred place . solemn music rise and fall ; the deep roll of the gregorian chant , begin with a low hum as of giant bee in a vast field of clover ; swell , in full - throate unison , a majestic volume of sound which ring against the rafter , wake echo in the clerestory ; then rumble back into silence . 

 stand beneath the sacred canopy , the bridal pair lift their eye to the high altar and see , amid a cloud of incense , the Bishop , in gorgeous vestment , descend the step and come toward they . 

 to Mora , at the time , and afterwards in most thankful remembrance , the wonder of that which follow lie in the fact that where she have dread an inevitable sense of sacrilege in give to another that which have be already consecrate to God , the Bishop so word the service as to make she feel that she could still be spiritually the bride of Christ , even while fulfil her troth to Hugh ; also that , in accept the call to this new Vocation , she be not fall from her old estate , but rather rise above it . 

 as the word be speak which make she a wife , it seem as if the Bishop gently wrap she about with a fresh mantle of dignity that dignity which have fall from she in those moment of humiliation when , at Hugh 's bidding she lay herself down upon the stretcher . 

 the Bishop voice the Church with a pomp and power which could not be withstand ; and when , in obedience to his command Hugh grasp she right hand with his right hand , and the Bishop lay his own on either side of their clasp hand , and pronounce they man and wife , it seem indeed as if a divine touch unite they , as if a divine voice ratify their vow and sanctify their union . 

 Mora have never before see the man so completely merge in his high office . 

 and , when all be over , even as he mount Shulamite and ride away , he ride out of the courtyard with the air of a Knight Templar rid forth - to do battle in a Holy War . 

 it seem to Mora that she have bid farewell to her old friend of the kindly smile , the merry eye , and the ready jest , in the early hour of that morning , as together they leave the arbour of the golden rose . 

 there remain therefore but one man to be consider : the ' splendid Knight " of old Antony 's vision ; the lover who have pursue she into her Nunnery ; woo she in her own cell , unabashe by the dignity of her office ; master her will ; force her numbed heart to awaken , disturb by the thrill of an unwilling tenderness ; move she to passion by the poignant anguish of a parting , which she regard as inevitably final ; win the Bishop over , to his side , and , through he , the Pope ; and finally , by the persistence of his pleading , move our blessed Lady to vouchsafe a vision on his behalf . 

 this be the ' splendid Knight " against whom the star in their course have most certainly not fight . principality and power have all be for he ; against he , just a woman and her conscience , and he have win . 

 when , at their first interview in her cell , in reply to her demand : " why be you not with your wife ? " he have answer : " I be with my wife ; the only wife I have ever want , the only woman I shall ever we d , be here " she stand ready to strike with ivory and steel , at the first attempt upon her inviolable chastity , and could afford to smile , in pity derision , at so empty a boast . 

 but now ? if he say : " my wife be here , " and choose to seize she with possessive grasp , she must meekly fold her hand upon her breast , and say : " even so , my lord . I be yours . deal with I as you will . " 

 as the Bishop 's purple cloak and the hind quarter of his noble black mare , disappear from view , the crowd which hitherto have surround the bridal pair , also vanish , as if at the wave of a magic wand . thus for the first time , since those tense moment in the Cathedral crypt , Mora find herself alone with Hugh . 

 she be not young enough to be embarrassed ; but she be old enough to be afraid ; afraid of he , and afraid of herself ; afraid of his masterful nature and imperious will , which have always incline to break rather than bend anything which stand in his way ; and afraid of something in herself which leapt up in response to this fierce strength in he , yearn to be master , hungry to yield , wishful to obey ; yet which , if yield to , would lay her spirit in the dust , and turn the awakened tenderness in her heart to scorn of herself , and anger against he . 

 so she fear as she stand in the sunshine , watch the now empty archway through which her sole remain link with Convent life have vanish ; conscious , without look round , that Debbie , who have be curtsey behind she , be there no long ; that Martin Goodfellow , who have hold Shulamite 's bridle while the Bishop mount , have disappear in one direction , the rest of the man in another ; intensely conscious that she and Hugh be now alone ; and fear , she shiver again , as she have shiver in the crypt ; then , of a sudden , know that she have do so , and , with a swift impulse of shame and contrition , turn and look at Hugh . 

 he be indeed the ' splendid Knight " of Mary Antony 's vision ! he have don for his bridal the dress of white and silver , which he have last put on when he sup at the Palace with the Bishop . this set off , with strike effect , his dark head and the noble beauty of his countenance ; and Mora , who chiefly remember he as a handsome youth , graceful and gay , realise for the first time his splendour as a man , and the change work in he by all he have face , endure , and overcome . 

 in the crypt , the day before , and during the hour which follow , she have scarce let herself look at he ; and he , though always close beside she , have keep out of her immediate range of vision . 

 since that infolding clasp in the crypt when he have fling the cloak about she , not once have he touch she , until the Church just now bid he , with authority , to take she right hand , with his . 

 her mind fly back to the happening of the previous day . with the lightning rapidity of retrospective thought , she pass again through each experience from the moment when the call of the blackbird sound in the crypt . the helpless horror of be lift by unseen hand ; the slow , swing progress , to the accompaniment of the measured tread of the man - at - arm ; the stifle darkness , air and light shut out by the heavy cloak , and yet the clear consciousness of the moment when the stretcher pass from the Cathedral into the sunshine without ; the sudden pause , as the Bishop meet the stretcher , and then as she lie helpless between they Symon 's question and Hugh 's reply , with their subtlety of hidden meaning , which fill she with impotent anger , shew as it do the completeness of the Bishop 's connivance at Hugh 's conspiracy . then Hugh 's request , and the Bishop 's hand lay upon she , the Bishop 's voice uplifted in blessing . then once again the measured tramp , tramp , and the steady swing of the stretcher ; but now the man 's heel ring on cobble , and voice seem everywhere ; cheery greeting , snatch of song , chance word concern a bargain or a meeting , a light jest , a coarse oath ; and , all the while , the steady , tramp , tramp , and the ring of Hugh 's spur . 

 she grow faint and it seem to she she be about to die beneath the cloak , and that when at length Hugh remove it , it would prove a pall beneath which he would find a dead bride . 

 " dead bride ! dead bride ! " sound the tramping footstep . and all the way she be haunt by the belief , assail her confused sens in the darkness , that the spirit of Father Gervaise have meet the stretcher ; that his be the voice which murmur low and tenderly ; " be not afraid , neither be thou dismayed . go in peace . "

 CHAPTER XLI 

 what the BISHOP REMEMBERED 

 Symon , Bishop of Worcester , sit in his library , in the cool of the day . 

 he be weary , with a weariness which surpass all his previous experience of weariness , all his imagining as to how weary , in body and spirit , a man could be , yet continue to breathe and think . 

 with some , extreme fatigue lead to restlessness of body . not so with the Bishop . the more tired he be , the more perfectly still he sit ; his knee cross , his elbow on the arm of his chair , the finger of both hand press lightly together , his head rest against the high back of the chair , his gaze fix upon the view across the river . 

 as he look with unseee eye upon the wide stretch of meadow , the distant wood and the soft outline of the Malvern hill , he be think how good it would be never again to leave this quiet room ; never to move from this chair ; never again to see a human being ; never to have to smile when he be heart - sick , or to bow when he feel ungracious ! 

 those who know the Bishop well , often speak together of his wondrous vitality and energy , their favourite remark be : that he be never tired . they might with more truth have say that they have never know he to appear tired . 

 it have long be a rule in the Bishop 's private code , that weariness , either of body or spirit , must not be shewn to other . the more tired he be , the more ready grow his smile , the more alert his movement , the more gracious his response to any call upon his sympathy or interest . 

 he never sigh in company , as do Father Peter when , have sup too well off jolly of salmon , roast venison , and raisin pie , he be fain to let indigestion pass muster for melancholy . 

 he never yawn in Council , either gracefully behind his hand , as do the lean Spanish Cardinal ; or openly and unashamed , as do the round and rosy Abbot of Evesham , display to the fascinated gaze of the brother in stall opposite , a cavernous throat , a red and healthy tongue , and a particularly fine set of tooth . 

 moreover the Bishop would as soon have think of carry a garment from the body of a plague - stricken patient into the midst of a family of healthy child , as of enter an assemblage with a jade countenance or a languorous manner . 

 therefore : " he be never weary , " say his friend . 

 " he knoweth not the meaning of fatigue , " agree his acquaintance . 

 " there be no merit in labour which be not in anywise a burden , but , rather , a delight , " pronounce those who envy his power . 

 " he be possess , " sneer his enemy , " by a most energetic demon ! 
 be that demon exorcise , the Bishop would collapse , exhausted . " 
 " he be fill , " say his admirer , " by the Spirit of God , and be thus so energized that he can work incessantly , without experience ordinary human weakness . " 

 and none know that it be a part of his religion to Symon of Worcester , to hide his weariness from other . 

 yet once when , in her chamber , he sit talk with the prioress , she have rise , of a sudden , say : " you be tired , Father . rest there in silence , while I work at my missal . " 

 she have pass to the table ; and the Bishop have sit resting , just as he be sit now , save that his eye could then dwell on her face , as she bend , absorb , over the illumination . 

 after a while he have ask : " how know you that I be tired , my dear 
 prioress ? " 
 without lift her eye , she have make answer : " because , my Lord 
 Bishop , you twice smile when there be no occasion for smile . "

 and she have answer : " they would speak more truly if they say that you be ever brave . " 

 it have amaze the Bishop to find himself thus understand . moreover he could scarce put on his biretta , so crowned be his head by the laurel of her praise . also this have be the only time when he have wonder whether the Prioress really believe Father Gervaise to be at the bottom of the ocean . it be ever an astonishment to a man when the unerring intuition of a woman be bring to bear upon himself . 

 now , in this hour of his overwhelming fatigue , he recall that scene . close his eye on the distant view , and open they upon the enchant vista of memory , he speedily see that calm face , with its chastened expression of fine self - control , bend above the page she be illuminate . he see the severe line of the wimple , the fold of the flow veil , the delicate movement of the long finger , and yes ! rest upon her bosom the jewelled cross , sign of her high office .

 CHAPTER XLII 

 the WARNING

 MORA mount to the battlement

 the song of the THRUSH

 CHAPTER XLVII 

 the BISHOP be TAKEN UNAWARES

 a strange chance

 twice deceive

 the SILVER SHIELD

 if the Bishop make the way easy , she might return to the Nunnery . 

 but all the true life of she would be leave behind with her lover . 

 she would bring to the Cloister a lacerated conscience , and a broken heart . 

 surely the two man who love she , if they thrust away all thought of self , and think only of she , could save she this anguish .

 " my dear hugh , " he say , " you do well to come to I in order to consult over these plan before take the irrevocable step which should set they in motion . I be shortly leave Worcester , leave this land and return to my beauteous Italy . the Holy Father have be pleased to tell I privately of high preferment shortly to be offer I . I have to - day decide to accept it . I return to Italy a Cardinal of Holy Church . "

" say Symon of Worcester ; " bent upon thine own way , and easy to deceive . when I speak of go , I say it for her sake , hop the prospect of my absence might hold you from your purpose . but now truly be I convince that you be bent upon risk your own happiness , and imperille her . therefore will I devise some mean of detain the Holy Father 's messenger , so that my answer need not be give until two week be past . you will reach Mora , at long , five day from this . as soon as she decide what she will do , send word to I by a fast messenger . should she elect to return to the Nunnery , state when and where , upon the road , I be to meet she . her habit as prioress , and her cross of office , I have here . the former you return to I , from the hostel ; the latter I find in her cell . you must take they with you . if she return , she must return fully rob . if , on the other hand , she should decide to remain with you ; if as may God grant she be content , and require no help from I , send I this news by messenger . "

 alas , I would indeed that I might rightly be turn therefrom . "

" 

 " to withhold a truth be not to lie , " assert the Bishop .

' our name be Argent , and we ever have the right to carry a pure silver shield . but I win the name because my shield be always bright ; because not once in battle do it fall in the dust ; because it never be allow to tarnish . so bright it be , that as I ride , bear it before I , reflect the ray of the sun , it dazzle and blind the enemy . my lord , I can not tarnish my silver shield by connive at falsehood , or keep silence when mine Honour bid I speak . " 

 look at the gallant figure before he , the Bishop 's soul respond to the noble word , and he long to praise they and applaud . but he think of Mora 's peace of mind , Mora 's awakened heart and dawn happiness . for her sake he must make a final stand . 

 " my dear hugh , " he say , " all this talk , of a silver shield and of the challenge of honour , be well enough for the warrior on the battle - field . but the lover have to learn the hard lesson ; he have to give up Self , even the self which hold honour dear . when you polish your silver shield , keep it so bright , what see you reflect therein ? why , your own proud face . even so , now , you fear the faint tarnish on your sense of honour , but you will keep that silver shield bright at Mora 's expense , rid on proudly alone in your glory , reflect the sun , dazzle all beholder , while your wife who love and trust you , Mora , who tell you the sweet wonder of her love in word of deep tenderness , lie desolate in the dark , with a shattered life , and a broken heart . hugh , I would have you think of the treasure of her golden heart , rather than of the brightness of your own selfish , silver shield . " 

 " selfish ! " cry the Knight . " selfish ! be it selfish to hold honour dear ? be it selfish to be ashamed to deceive the woman one love ? have I , who have so striven in all thing to put her welfare first , be selfish towards my wife in this hour of crisis ? " 

 he sit down , heavily ; lean his elbow on his knee , and drop his head into his hand .

" but , thank Heaven , no harm have yet be do . listen to I and I will shew you how you may keep your honour safely untarnishe , yet withhold from Mora all knowledge which might cause her disquietude of mind , thus secure her happiness and your own .  CHAPTER LI 

 two NOBLE HEARTS GO different way

 CHAPTER LII 

 the ANGEL - child

 yet should that sudden leap be describe as " impulsive " ? the Bishop , ever a stickler for accuracy in descriptive word , consider this .

 CHAPTER LIII 

 on the HOLY MOUNT 

 on the ninth day since Hugh 's departure , the day when fast riding might make his return possible before nightfall , Mora rise early . 

 at the hour when she have be will not to ring the Convent bell , she be walk swiftly over the moor and climb the heather - clothe hill . 

 she have remember a little chapel , high up in the mountain , where dwelt a holy Hermit , hold in high repute for his saintliness of life , his wisdom in the giving of spiritual counsel , and his skill in minister to the sick . 

 it have come to Mora , as she pray and ponder during the night , that if she could make full confession to this holy man , he might be able to throw some clear beam of light upon the dark tangle of her perplexity . 

 this hope be strongly with she as she walk . 

 " lighten my darkness ! lead I in a plain path ! " be the cry of her bewildered soul . 

 it seem to she that she have two issue to consider . first : the question as to whether Hugh , guide by the Bishop , would keep silence ; thus make himself a party to her deception . secondly : the position in which she be place by the fact that she have leave the Convent , owe to that deception . but , for the moment the first issue be so infinitely the great , that she find herself thrust the second into the background , allow herself to be conscious of it merely as a question to be face later on , when the all - important point of Hugh 's attitude in the matter should be settle . 

 she walk forward swiftly , one idea alone possess she : that she hasten toward possible help . 

 she do not slacken speed until the chapel come into view , its grey wall glisten in the morning light , a clump of feathery rowan tree beside it ; at its back a mighty rock , fling down in bygone century from the mountain which tower behind it . from a deep cleft in this rock spring a young oak , dip its fresh green to the roof of the chapel ; all around it , in every crack and cranny , parsley fern , hare - bell on delicate , sway stalk , foxglove tall and straight , and glorious bunch of purple heather . 

 nearby be the humble dwelling of the Hermit . the door stand ajar . 

 softly approach , Mora lift her hand , and knock . 

 no voice reply . 

 the sound of her knock do but make evident the presence of a vast solitude . 

 push open the door , she venture to look within . 

 the Hermit 's cell be empty . the remain of a frugal meal lie upon the rough wooden table . also an open breviary , much thumbed and worn . at the further end of the table , a little pile of medicinal herb heap as if shake hastily from the wallet which lie beside they . probably the holy man , even while at an early hour he break his fast , have be call to some sick bedside . 

 Mora turn from the doorway and , shade her eye , scan the landscape . 

 at first she could see only sheep , slowly move from tuft to tuft as they nibble the short grass ; or goat , jump from rock to rock , and suddenly disappear in the high bracken . 

 but soon , on a distant ridge , she perceive two figure and presently make out the brown robe and hood of the Hermit , and a little , barefoot peasant boy , run to keep up with his rapid stride . they vanish over the crest of the hill , and Mora alone in this wild solitude realise that many hour might elapse ere the Hermit return . 

 this check to the fulfilment of her purpose , instead of disappoint she , flood her heart with a sudden sense of relief . 

 the interior of the Hermit 's cell have recall , so vividly , the austerity of the cloistered life . 

 the Hermit 's point of view would probably have be so completely from within . 

 it would have be impossible that he should comprehend the wonder the grow wonder of these day , since she and Hugh ride away from Warwick , culminate in that exquisite hour on the battlement when she have tell he of the vision , whisper her full surrender , and yet he faithful and patient even then have touch she only with his glow eye . 

 how could a holy Hermit , dwell alone among great silent hill , realise the tremendous force of a strong mutual love , the glow , the gladness , the deep , sweet unrest , the call of soul to soul , the throb of heart , fill the purple night with the soft beat of angel ' wing ? 

 how could a holy Hermit understand the shock to Hugh , how fathom the madden torment of suspense , the abyss of hope defer , into which the Bishop 's letter must have plunge he , come so soon after he have say : " I ask no high joy , than to watch the breaking of the day which give thee to my home " ? but the breaking of the day have bring the stern necessity which take he from she . 

 yet why ? how much be in that second letter ? be it less detailed than the first ? have Hugh ride south to learn the entire truth ? or have he ride south to arrange with the Bishop for her complete and permanent deception ? 

 stand on this mountain plateau the morning breeze blow about she , the sun mount triumphant in the heaven " as a bridegroom come out of his chamber , " and all around the scent of heather , the hum of bee , the joyful trill of the soar lark ; her own body bound with life after the swift climb it seem to Mora impossible that Hugh should withstand the temptation to hold to his happiness , at all cost . and how could a saintly Hermit judge he as mercifully as she the woman who love he know that he should be judge ? 

 she feel thankful for the good man 's absence , yet baffle in her need for help .

 " with HIM , in the HOLY MOUNT , " be inscribe across the doorway of the 
 Hermit 's dwelling .

 " with he , in the Holy Mount . "

 move close , she look up and read they . 
 " and when they had lift up their eyes , they see no MAN , SAVE JESUS only . "

 it live ! the face wear a look of search tenderness ; on the lip , a smile of love comprehension ; in the out - stretch hand , an attitude of infinite compassion .

" and , strangely enough , there come back with this the remembrance of the wild voice of Mary Seraphine , shrieking , when tell to contemplate the die Redeemer : " I want life not death ! " 

 here be life indeed ! here be the Saviour of the world , in mortal guise , the Word make manifest . 

 Mora lift her eye and read the word , illumine in letter of gold around the arch of the niche , gleam in the sunlight above the patient head of the Man Divine . 

 " in all point tempt like as we be , yet without SIN . " 

 and higher still , above the arch :

 the Unseen Presence draw nearer . 

 she close her eye to the sculptured form .

 " tempt in all point . " . . . then here be one who could understand Hugh 's hard temptation ; who could pity , if Hugh fall . here be one who would comprehend the breaking of her poor human heart if , love Hugh as she now love , she yet must leave he . 

 " a great High Priest . " . . . what need of any other priest , while " with he in the Holy Mount " ? pass into the heaven , yet ever live to make intercession for we . 

 deep peace steal into her heart , as she kneel in absorb communion in this sacred place , where , for the first time , in her religious life , she have find herself with " Jesus only . "

 CHAPTER LIV 

 the unseen presence

 " which Voice we hear , " write Saint Peter , " when we be with he in the Holy Mount . " she , too , have first hear it there ; but , as she descend , it be with she still . the song of the bird , the rush of the stream , the breeze in the pine , the bee on the wing , all Nature seem to say : " it be the Lord !  Sorrow , suffering , disillusion might await she on the plain ; but , with the Presence beside she , and the Voice within , she feel strong to face they , and to overcome .

 CHAPTER LV 

 the heart of a woman

 CHAPTER LVI 

 the true vision

 it be say in sunny Florence in the year that follow , and , later on , it be remark in Rome , that if the Lord High Cardinal kind of man be try almost beyond bear , if even his calm patience seem in danger of ruffle , or if he be weary , or sad , or dishearten , he have a way of slip his hand into the bosom of his scarlet robe , as if he gently finger something that lie against his heart .

 " I choose TO RIDE alone "

 Deborah .

 CHAPTER LVIII 

 the warrior heart 

 as Mora turn off the highway , and press Icon deep into the glade , she cry over and over aloud , for there be none to hear : " I go to my husband , and I choose to ride alone . " 

 how wondrous it seem , this go to he ; a second giving , a deep surrender , a fuller yielding . 

 when she go to he in the crypt , her body have recoil , her spirit have shrunk , sham , humble , and unwilling . her mind alone , govern by her will , have drive she along the path of her resolve , hold she upon the stretcher , until too late to cry out or to return . 

 now how different ! free as air , alone , uncoerced , even unexpected , she leave her own home , and her own people , to ride , unattended , straight to the arm of the man who have win she . 

 a wild joy seize and shake she . 

 the soft , mysterious glade , beneath vast , leafy dome , seem enchant ground . the hoof of Icon thud softly on the moss . the stillness seem alive with whisper life . rabbit sit still to peep , then whisk and run . great bird rise suddenly , on whir wing . tiny bird , fearless , stay on their twig and sang . 

 there be scurry among fern and rock , tell of bright , watchful eye ; of life , safeguard itself , unseen . yet all these varied sound , Nature disturb in the shady haunt which be her rightful home , do but emphasize the vast stillness , the utter solitude , the complete remoteness from human dwelling - place . 

 shin through part bough and slowly move leaf , the sunlight fall , in golden bar or shift yellow patch , on the glade . 

 the joy which thrill his rider , seem to communicate itself to Icon . he gallop over the moss on the broad ride , and would scarce be restrain when pass between great rock , or turn sharply into an unseen way . 

 Mora ride as in a dream . " I ride to my husband , " she cry to the forest , " and I choose to ride alone ! " and once she sing , in an irrepressible burst of praise : " Jesu dulsis memoria ! " then , when she fall silent : " Dulsis ! dulsis ! " carol unseen chorister in leafy clerestory overhead . and each time Icon hear her voice , he lay back his ear and canter fast . 

 not far from her journey 's end , the way lie through a deep gorge in the very heart of the pine wood . 

 here the sun 's ray could scarce penetrate ; the path become rough and slippery ; a hidden stream ooze up between loose stone . 

 Icon pick his way , with care ; yet even so , he slip , recover , and slip again . 

 with a sudden rush , some wild animal , huge and heavy , go crash through the undergrowth . 

 stealthy footstep seem to keep pace with Icon 's , high up among the tree trunk . 

 yet this valley of the shadow hold no terror for the woman whose heart be now so blissfully at rest . 

 have leave behind forever the dark vale of doubt and indecision , she mount triumphant on the wing of trust and certainty . 

 " I ride to my husband , " she whisper , as if the word be a charm which might bring the sense of his strong arm about she , " and I choose to ride alone . " 

 with a gentle caress on the arch of his snowy neck , and with soft word in the anxiously point ear , she encourage the palfrey to go forward . 

 at length they round a great grey rock jut out into the path , and the upward slope of a mossy glade come into view . 

 with a whinny of pleasure , Icon lay back his ear and break into a swift canter . 

 up the glade they fly ; out into the sunshine ; clear into the open . 

 here be the moor ! here the highroad , at last ! and there in the distance , the grey wall of Hugh 's castle ; the portal of home . 

           

 it be the Knight 's trust foster - brother , Martin Goodfellow , amazed , yet smile a glad welcome , who hold Icon 's bridle as Mora dismount in the courtyard . 

 she fondle the palfrey 's nose , lay her cheek against his neck . for the moment it become imperative that she should hide her happy eye even from this faithful fellow , in whom she have learn to place entire confidence . 

 " Icon , brave and beautiful ! " she whisper . " Thou hast carry I here where I long to be . Thy foot be well - nigh as swift as my desire . " 

 then she turn , speak quickly and low . 

 " Martin , where be my husband ? where shall I find Sir Hugh ? " 

 " my lady , " say Martin , " I see he last in the armoury . " 

 " the armoury ? " she question . 

 " a chamber opening out of the great hall , face toward the west , with step lead down into the garden . " 

 " even as my chamber ? " 

 " the armoury door face the door of your chamber , Countess . the width of the hall lie between . " 

 " can I reach my chamber without enter the hall , or pass the armoury window ? I would rid I of my travel - stain , before I make my presence know to Sir Hugh . " 

 " pass round to the right , and through the buttery ; then you reach the garden and the step up to your chamber from the side beyond the armoury . " 

 " good . tell no one of my presence , Martin . I have here the key of my chamber . have Sir Hugh ask for it ? " 

 " Nay , my lady ; nor guess how often we ride hither . we reach the castle scarce two hour ago . the Knight bath , and change his dusty garment ; then din alone . after which he go into the armoury . " 

 " when do you see he last , Martin ? " 

 " two minute ago , lady . I come this moment from the hall . " 

 " what be he do , Martin ? " 

 Martin Goodfellow hesitate . he know something of love , and as much as an honest man may know , of woman . he shrewdly suspicione what she would expect the Knight to be do . he be sorely tempt to give a fancy picture of Sir Hugh d'Argent , in his lovelorn loneliness . 

 he look into the clear eye bent upon he ; glance at the firm hand , arrest for a moment in its caress of Icon 's neck ; then decide that , though the truth might probably be unexpected , a lie would most certainly be unwise . 

 " truth to tell , " say Martin Goodfellow , " Sir Hugh be test his armour , and sharpen his battle - axe . " 

 as Mora pass into the dim coolness of the buttery , she be conscious of a very definite sense of surprise . she have picture Hugh in his lonely home , nurse his hungry heart , beside his desolate hearth . she have see herself come softly behind he , lay a tender hand upon those bow shoulder ; then , as he lift eye in which dull despair would quickly give place to wonder joy , say : " Hugh , I be come home . " 

 but now , as she pass through the buttery , Mora have to realise that yet again she have fail to understand the man she love .

 all be as she have leave it . 

 fasten the door by which she have enter from the garden , she noiselessly open that which give on to the great hall .

 CHAPTER LIX 

 the MADONNA in the home 

 Hugh d'Argent have polish his armour , put a keen edge on his battle - axe , and rub the rust from his sword . 

 the torment of suspense , the sicken pain of hope defer , could be well bear , while he turn his mind on future battle , and his muscle to vigorous action . 

 of the way in which the cup of perfect bliss have be snatch from his very lip , he could not trust himself to think . 

 his be the instinct of the fighter , to bend his whole mind upon the present , prepare for the future ; not waste energy in useless reconsideration of an accomplished past . 

 he have act as he have feel bind in honour to act . gain or loss to himself have not be the point at issue . even as , in the hot fight with the Saracens , slay or be slay might incidentally result from the action of the moment , but the possession of the Holy Sepulchre be the true object for which each warrior who have take the cross , draw his sword or swing his battle - axe . 

 be honour , hold unsullied , to prove in this case , the tomb of his life 's happiness ? three day of suspense , during which Mora consider , and he and the Bishop wait . on the third day , would Love arise victorious , purify by suffering , clothe in raiment of dazzle whiteness ? would there be Easter in his heart , and deep peace in his home ? or would his beloved wind herself once more in cerement , would the seal of the Vatican be set upon the stone of monastic rule and regulation , make it fast , secure , inviolable ? would he , turn sadly from the Zion of hope fulfil , be walk in dull despair to the Emmaus of an empty home , of a day far spend , hold no promise of a bright dawn ? 

 but , even as his mind dwelt on the symbolism of that sacred scene , the Knight remember that the two who walk in sadness do not long walk alone . one , step silently , come up with they ; know all , yet ask tenderest question ; the Master , whom they mourn , himself draw near and go with they . 

 it seem to Hugh d'Argent that if so real a presence as that , could draw near to he and to Mora at this sad parting of the way , if their religion do but hold a thing so vital , then might they have a true vision of Life , which should make clear the reason for the long year of suffering , and point the way to the glory which should follow . then , be bless , not merely by the Church and the Bishop but by the Christ himself he who at Cana grant the good wine when the earthly vintage fail the wedding feast they might leave behind forever the empty tomb of hope frustrate , and return together , with exceed joy , to the Jerusalem of joy fulfil . 

 Hugh lay down his sword , rise , stretch himself , and stand look full into the golden sunset . 

 he could not account for it , but somehow the darkness have lift . the sense of loneliness be go . an Unseen Presence seem with he . the thought of prayer throb through his helpless spirit , like the uplift beat of strong white wing . 

 " o God , " he say , " thou seemest to I as a stranger , when I meet Thee on mine own life 's way . I know Thee as Babe divine ; I know Thee , crucify ; I know Thee risen , and ascend in such cloud of glory as hide Thee from mine earthbound sight . but , if Thou hast draw near along the rocky footpath of each day 's common happening , then have mine eye indeed be holden , and I know Thee not . " 

 Hugh stand motionless , his eye on the glory of the sunset battlement . and into his mind there come , as clearly as if that moment utter , the word of Father Gervaise : " he ever liveth to make intercession for we . " 

 the Knight raise his right arm . " oh , if Thou livest , " he say , " and living , know ; and know , carest ; grant I a sign of Thy nearness a Vision of Life and of Love , which shall make clear this mist of uncertainty . " 

 turn back to his work , so great a load seem lift from his heart , that he find himself sing as he put a keener edge on his weapon . 

 presently he go over to the corner where stand the silver shield . Hitherto he have keep his eye turn from it . it call up thought which he have strive to beat back . now , he set to work and polish it until its surface shine clear as a mirror . 

 and as he work , he think within himself : " what say the Bishop ? that I see reflect in my silver shield naught save mine own proud face ? but I tell my wife that I see there the face of God , or the near I know to his face ; and , behind he , her face the face of my beloved ; for , have I not put reverence and honour first , my very love for she would have be tarnish . " 

 Hugh stand the silver shield at such an angle as that it reflect the sunset , yet as he kneel upon one knee before it he could not see his own reflection . 

 the sun , round and blood red , almost dip below the horizon , shine out in crimson glory from the deep heart of the silver . 

 Hugh remember two verse of a hebrew poem which the Rabbi use to recite at sunset . " the Lord God be a Sun and Shield : the Lord will give Grace and Glory ; no good thing will he withhold from they that walk uprightly . o Lord of Hosts , bless be the man that trusteth in Thee . " 

 his eye upon the shield , his hand clasp around his knee , Hugh say , softly : " the face of God , my beloved , or the near I know to his face : and behind he , thy face " 

 and then his voice fall of a sudden silent ; his heart beat in his throat , his finger grip his knee ; for something move softly in the shin surface , and there look out at he from his own silver shield , the face of the woman he love . 

 how long he kneel and gaze without stir , Hugh could not tell . at that moment life pause suspend , and he cease to be conscious of time . but , at length , press nearer , his own dark head appear in the shield , and above he , bend toward he , Mora , shimmer in soft white , as on her wedding morn , her hand outstretche , her eye full of a tender yearning , gaze into his . 

 " the Vision for which I pray ! " cry the Knight . " o , my God ! be this the sign of Thy nearness ? be this a promise that my wife will come to I ? " 

 he hide his face in his hand . 

 a gentle touch fall lightly on his hair . 

 " not a promise , Hugh , " come a tender whisper close behind he . " a sign of God 's nearness ; a proof of mine . Hugh , my own dear Knight , lift up your head and look . your wife have come home . " 

 leap to his foot , he turn ; still dazzle , incredulous . 

 no shadowy reflection this . his wife stand before he , fair as on her wedding morning , a jewel circlet clasp the golden glory of her hair . but his eye see only the look in her . 

 yet he keep his distance .

I have see all other fail , but my Knight of the Silver Shield stand faithful . Thy faithfulness sham my poor doubt of thee . the richness of thy giving , beggar my yearning to bestow . yet now at last thy wife can come to thee without a doubt , without a tremor , all hesitancy go , all she be , and all she have , quite simply , thine . oh , Hugh , thine own to do with as thou wilt . all these year keep for thee . take I ah ! . . . oh , Hugh , thy strength ! be this love , or be there some deep , more rapturous word ? oh , dear man of mine , how strong must have be the flood - gate , if this be the pen - up force behind they ! " 

 he carry she to the hearth in the great hall , and place she in the chair in which his mother use to sit .

 presently : " and do thy people come with thee , my sweetheart ? and how could a three hour ' ride be accomplish in this bridal array ? oh , Heaven help I , Mora ! thou art so beautiful ! " 

 " hush , " she say , " thou dear , foolish man ! Heaven hath help thee through bad strait than that ! Nay , I ride alone , and in my riding dress of green . arrive here , I change , in mine own chamber , to these marriage garment . "

 " here here , in thine own chamber , Mora ? " 
 the mother in she thrill with tenderness , as she bend and look into those bewildered eye . for once , she feel old than he , and wiser . the sense of inexperience fall from she . for very joy she laugh as she make answer .

 she lay her lip upon his hair . 

 " I hope it will please thee , my lord , " she say . " come and see . "

 she would soon have go on her own foot ; but her joy this day , be to give he all he wish , and as he wish it .

 then Hugh pass within . 

 CHAPTER LX 

 the convent BELL 

 the slanting ray of the set sun lay , in golden band , upon the flag of the Convent cloister . 

 complete silence reign . 

 the White Ladies have return from vesper . each , in the solitude of her own cell , be spend , in prayer and meditation , the hour until the Refectory bell should ring . 

 the great door into the cloister stand wide . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress appear in the far distance , move down the passage . as she pass between the long line of closed door , she turn her face quickly from side to side , pause occasionally to listen , ear lay against the panelling .

 she do not blink , as old Mary Antony use to blink . her small eye peer from out her veil as sharply in sunshine as in shadow .

 move along the cloister , she seat herself upon the stone slab in the archway overlook the lawn and the pieman 's tree ; then draw forth from beneath her scapulary , the worn leathern wallet which have belong to the old lay - sister , Mary Antony .

 very bright - eye , and tall on his leg , be Mary Antony 's little vain man . with his head on one side , he look inquiringly at Mother Sub - Prioress ; and Mother Sub - Prioress , from out the curtain of her veil , frown back at he .

 this be the daily formula . 

 the " jaunty little layman , " undismaye though the look be austere , and the voice , forbid hop gaily near , peck eagerly . no gap mouth now wait his return . his nestling be grow and fly . at last he could afford to feast himself .

 whereupon something break in the cold heart of Mother Sub - Prioress . tear run slowly down the thin face . she would not stir nor lift her hand to wipe they away , and they fall in heavy drop upon her fold finger .

"

 this evidence of the trust in she of a little live thing , be the one rope to which Mother Sub - Prioress clung in those first moment , during which the black water of remorse and despair pass over her head a rope make of frail enough strand , God know : bright eye alert , small cling foot , a pair of fold wing . yet do the frailest thread of love and trust , make a safe rope to which to cling when shipwreck threaten the heart , than the iron chain of obligation and duty .

 for what , then ? . . . 

 Mother Sub - Prioress whisper the answer ; and as she whisper it , her tear fall afresh ; but now they be tear without bitterness ; a healing fount seem to well up within her soften heart .
